{"query":{"pages":{"11591890":{"pageid":11591890,"ns":0,"title":"2002 (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=March 2013}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = 2002\n| image                 =\n| caption            =\n| image_size            =\n| background          = group_or_band\n| alias               =\n| origin              = Texas, United States\n| instrument          =\n| genre               = [[New-age music|New age]], [[neoclassical new age]]\n| occupation          =\n| years_active        = [[1992 in music|1992]]\u2013present\n| label               = [[Real Music]]<br />[[Gemini Sun Records]]<br />[[Galactic Playground Music]]\n| associated_acts     =\n| website                 = [http://www.2002music.com 2002music.com]\n| current_members     = Randy Copus<br />Pamela Copus\n| past_members        =\n| notable_instruments =\n}}\n'''2002''' is a [[New-age music|new age]] group composed of Randy and Pamela Copus. 2002 has charted nine albums on the ''[[Billboard Magazine|Billboard]]'' New Age Charts.<ref name=\"BIO\">{{cite web | url=http://www.2002music.com/bio/ | title=2002 Biography}}</ref> ''This Moment Now'' won the [[Coalition of Visionary Retailers|COVR]] award for Best New Age Album in 2004.<ref name=\"BIO\"/> 2002 was named amongst the top new age artists in ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard's]]'' 2003 \u201cYear in Review\u201d issue (December 2003), a list that also featured [[Yanni]], [[Manheim Steamroller]], [[Jim Brickman]], [[George Winston]] and [[Enya]].<ref name=\"BIO\"/>\n\nThe themes of several of 2002's albums are deeply rooted in [[mythology]].  ''Wings'' is based on the [[Greece|Greek]] legend of [[Icarus]].  ''Savitri'' and ''The Emerald Way'' are both inspired by the ancient [[Hindu]] story of [[Savitri and Satyavan]] from the [[Mahabharata]].  ''Land of Forever'' is a ballad of the mystic island of [[T\u00edr na n\u00d3g]], an Irish legend.\n\nPamela and Randy record all their music at their state-of-the-art studio. Randy Copus plays piano, [[electric cello]], guitar, bass, and keyboards. Pamela Copus plays [[flute]]s, [[harp]], keyboards, and a wind instrument called a [[WX5]]. Both musicians also provide all of the vocals on their albums, recording their voices many, many times and layering them to create a \"virtual [[choir]]\" with a celestial, angelic quality. The vocals also have many dimensions, as words and chants in Sanskrit, Spanish, Latin and Japanese, representing sacred traditions throughout the world, can be heard on their albums.<ref name=\"BIO\"/>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"8878840":{"pageid":8878840,"ns":0,"title":"3rd Force","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{BLP sources|date=July 2011}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = 3rd Force\n| image           = \n| alt             = \n| caption         = \n| image_size      = \n| landscape       = <!-- yes, if wide image, otherwise leave blank -->\n| background      = group_or_band\n| alias           = \n| origin          = \n| genre           = [[smooth jazz]]\n| years_active    =  {{start date|1994}}\u2013present \n| label           = [[Higher Octave]]\n| associated_acts = \n| website         =  {{URL|http://www.3rdforcemusic.com/}} \n| current_members = William Aura<br>Craig Dobbin<br>Alain Eskinasi\n| past_members    = \n}}\n\n'''3rd Force''' is a [[smooth jazz]] band on the EMI Higher Octave label, consisting of trio William Aura, Craig Dobbin, and Alain Eskinasi.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://jazztimes.com/articles/13215-gentle-force-3rd-force|title=Gentle Force 3rd Force|date=July\u2013August 2002|author=Chris Walker|publisher=[[JazzTimes]]|accessdate=June 27, 2011}}</ref> Founded in 1994 by William Aura after a prolific solo career in [[New Age music]], he, Dobbin, and Eskinasi immediately set out working on their self-titled debut album, ''3rd Force'' which was released that same year. After the album's commercial success, the trio continued the studio project with their next release, ''Force of Nature'' in 1995.  This album garnered an even bigger success than their debut spawning the popular single ''Here Comes the Night'' featuring guest guitarist Peter White.  After a two year break, 3rd Force released their 3rd album ''Vital Force'' in 1997. The album gained 3rd Force's second hit single ''You Gotta Be Real'' once again featuring guest guitarist Peter White.  The 4th album, called ''Force Field'', was released in 1999 resulting in another of the band's singles ''Revelation of the Heart'', with guest saxophonist Paul Taylor.  In 2000 Higher Octave released a best-of compilation of 3rd Force, entitled ''Collective Force'', which featured the band's best hits in both radio and fan favorites,along with two new songs, ''Dance With Me'' and ''Sweet Surrender''.  2002 saw the release of their 5th studio album, ''Gentle Force'', which showcased a mellower jazz sound than the band's usual output. Three years later,3rd Force released their latest album to date, ''Driving Force'' in 2005.  Their latest release showcases a completely opposite style than the previous ''Gentle Force'' album which was almost lounge-style mellow jazz in sound. ''Driving Force'', however, features a funky lively jazz mix never before heard in 3rd Force's music.  The most popular singles from their latest release are ''Believe In Me'', featuring the trumpeter [[Greg Adams (musician)|Greg Adams]], keyboardist [[Jeff Lorber]], and guitarist [[Brian Hughes (musician)|Brian Hughes]], and ''You Got It'', featuring guitarist [[Marc Antoine (musician)|Marc Antoine]]."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2733539":{"pageid":2733539,"ns":0,"title":"Philip Aaberg","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n|name           = Philip Aaberg\n| image         = \n| caption       = \n| image_size    = \n|background     = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n|birth_place    = {{Birth date and age|1949|04|08}}\n|origin         = [[Havre, Montana|Havre]], [[Montana]], [[United States|USA]]\n|instrument     = [[piano]]\n|genre          = [[Jazz]], [[instrumental]]\n|occupation     = [[Composer]], [[musician]]\n|years_active   = 1979\u2013present\n|associated_acts= [[William Ackerman|Will Ackerman]], [[Darol Anger]], [[Michael Hedges]]\n}}\n\n'''Philip Aaberg''' (born April 8, 1949) is an American pianist, keyboardist, and composer.<ref name=aaberg>{{cite news|title=Philip Aaberg Plays for Fine Arts Series Finale|newspaper=Bozeman Daily Chronicle|url=http://www.bozemandailychronicle.com/arts_and_entertainment/sounds/article_afaf9cc0-66d7-11e0-a00c-001cc4c002e0.html|date=April 15, 2011|accessdate=August 6, 2011}}</ref> He gained international recognition through a series of successful piano recordings released on [[Windham Hill Records]]. Although classically trained, Aaberg incorporates classical, jazz, bluegrass, rock, and new music elements into his compositions and musical structures.<ref name=\"Sweetgrass Music\">[http://www.sweetgrassmusic.com Sweetgrass Music].</ref> Although best known for his solo piano work, he is most at home in the [[chamber jazz]] genre. His compositions are noted for their \"rigorous keyboard technique, diverse influences, and colorful compositional style.\"<ref name=aaberg2>{{cite web|url={{Allmusic|class=artist|id=q71083|pure_url=yes}}|title=Biography: Philip Aaberg|last=Kohanov|first=Linda|publisher=Allmusic|accessdate=September 5, 2011}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2865593":{"pageid":2865593,"ns":0,"title":"William Ackerman","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{more footnotes|date=March 2012}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = William \"Will\" Ackerman\n| image               = \n| caption             = \n| image_size          = \n| background          = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_date          = {{birth year and age|1949}}\n| alias               = \n| genre               = [[Fingerstyle guitar|Fingerstyle acoustic]], [[new-age music|new age]], [[chamber jazz]]\n| occupation          = [[Musician]]\n| instrument          = [[Guitar]]\n| years_active        = 1976&ndash;present\n| label               = [[Windham Hill]], Imaginary Road, Lifescapes\n| associated_acts     = \n| website                 = [http://www.williamackerman.com Official Site]\n| notable_instruments = \n|}}\n\n'''William Ackerman''' (born 1949)<ref name=\"allmusic\">Ruhlmann, William. The act's first and only album to date, ''[[Fate of a Dreamer]]'', was recorded in 2001, when van der Veen was just 14 years old. Ambeon's atmospheric sound draws from a wide variety of influences, including [[Celtic music|Celtic]], [[Gothic rock|gothic]] and [[Progressive metal|progressive music]]. The songs on ''Fate of a Dreamer'' are mostly composed of different remixed pieces of songs from [[Ayreon]] albums, whereas the lyrics are original, written by van der Veen."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"10605965":{"pageid":10605965,"ns":0,"title":"Amethystium","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use dmy dates|date=June 2013}}\n{{Unreferenced|date=September 2010}}\n{{Infobox musical artist| <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = Amethystium\n| image                 =\n| caption            =\n| image_size            = 210\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[Trondheim]], [[Norway]]<!--DO NOT CHANGE WITHOUT A TALK PAGE DISCUSSION -->\n| genre               = [[Ambient music|Ambient]], [[electronica]], [[New-age music|new age]], [[Neoclassical dark wave|neoclassical]]<!-- Same as above -->\n| years_active        = 1999\u2013present\n| label               = [[Neurodisc Records]]\n| associated_acts     =\n| website                 = [http://www.amethystium.com Official Website]\n| current_members     = [[\u00d8ystein Ramfjord]]\n| past_members        =\n}}\n\n'''Amethystium''' is an [[Ambient music|Ambient]]/[[Electronica]]/[[Neoclassical (Dark Wave)|Neoclassical]] music project created by  [[Norway|Norwegian]] producer/composer/multi-instrumentalist \u00d8ystein Ramfjord.  Under the Amethystium name, Ramfjord has released five full-length albums, ''Odonata'', ''Aphelion'', ''Evermind'', ''Isabliss'', and \"Transience\" a collection of works, ''Emblem (Selected Pieces)'', all on [[Neurodisc Records]], as well as two EPs."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"92374":{"pageid":92374,"ns":0,"title":"Autechre","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use dmy dates|date=June 2013}}\n{{Use British English|date=June 2013}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = Autechre\n| alias               = Lego Feet\n| image               = Autechre.jpg\n| caption             = Rob Brown and Sean Booth performing live as Autechre in 2007\n| alt                 = Two men performing live electronic music as a group/band in a dark room.\n| landscape           = yes\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[Rochdale]], [[Greater Manchester]], England\n| genre               = [[intelligent dance music|IDM]], [[electronic music|electronic]], [[ambient techno]], [[experimental music|experimental]], [[ambient music|ambient]]\n| years_active        = 1987\u2013present\n| label               = [[Warp Records|Warp]], [[Skam Records|Skam]], [[Wax Trax Records|Wax Trax!]], [[TVT Records|TVT]], [[Nothing Records|Nothing]]\n| associated_acts     = [[Gescom]]\n| website             = {{URL|1=autechre.ws}}\n| current_members     = Sean Anthony Booth<br/>Robert John Brown\n| notable_instruments = [[Elektron (company)|Elektron]] [[Machinedrum]]<br />[[Elektron Monomachine|Monomachine]]\n}}\n\n'''Autechre''' are an English [[electronic music]] duo consisting of Rob Brown and Sean Booth, both from [[Rochdale]], [[Greater Manchester]]. Formed in 1987, they are one of the most prominent acts signed to [[Warp Records]], a label known for its pioneering electronic music and through which all Autechre albums have been released.\n\nWhile heavily associated with [[Intelligent dance music|IDM]] (intelligent dance music), Booth and Brown are ambivalent about relating their sound to established genres.<ref name=\"pitchfork\">[http://www.pitchforkmedia.com/article/feature/14673/Interview_Interview_Autechre Drew Daniel interview, November 2005]\u2014''[[Pitchfork Media]]''</ref> Their music has exhibited a gradual shift in aesthetic throughout their career, from their earlier work with clear roots in [[techno]], [[house music|house]], [[electro music|electro]] and [[hip hop]], to later albums that are often considered experimental in nature, featuring complex patterns of rhythm and subdued melodies.\n\nAutechre have also recorded under various pseudonyms. One of the duo's earliest recordings was a [[12-inch single|12\"]] under the alias Lego Feet, released in 1991 on [[Skam Records]]. The majority of releases by the mysterious \"umbrella project\" [[Gescom]], most of them on Skam, have been attributed to Booth and Brown, among other artists."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"25859362":{"pageid":25859362,"ns":0,"title":"The American Dollar (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{refimprove|date=February 2010}}\n\n{{Infobox musical artist\n|name = The American Dollar\n|image =\n|caption =  \n|background = group_or_band\n|origin = [[Queens]], [[New York]], United States\n|Instruments = \n|genre = [[Post-rock]], [[Ambient music|Ambient]], [[Electronic music|Electronic]]\n|Formed = 2005\n|years_active = 2005 \u2013 present\n|label = [[Yesh Music]]\n|website = [http://www.theamericandollar.info www.theamericandollar.info]\n|current_members = [[John Emanuele]] <small>- Drums/Keys </small><br>[[Richard Cupolo]] <small>- Guitar/Keys</small>}}\n\n'''The American Dollar''' is an American music project, formed in 2005 in [[Queens]], [[New York]].<ref>{{Cite web |url=http://www.sputnikmusic.com/bands/The-American-Dollar/11266/ |title=The American Dollar |work=[[Sputnikmusic]] |accessdate=February 27, 2011}}</ref> The band consists of drummer/keyboardist John Emanuele and guitarist/keyboardist/producer Richard Cupolo.  They have released five [[studio album]]s, three deductive ambient remix albums and two EP\u2019s, one a split with Arms and Sleepers and the other a live album. Their debut self-titled effort was released in 2006.<ref>[http://www.trouserpress.com/entry.php?a=american_dollar Album review], [[Trouser Press]], 2006.</ref> ''A Memory Stream'', the band's third full-length, was issued in 2008.<ref>[http://www.popmatters.com/pm/review/the-american-dollar-a-memory-stream A Memory Stream review]. [[Pop Matters]], October 20, 2008.</ref><ref>[http://www.absolutepunk.net/showthread.php?t=496181 A Memory Stream Review], [[Absolute Punk]]</ref> Their fourth album, entitled ''Atlas'', was released by Yesh Music on January 1, 2010.<ref>{{Cite web |url=http://www.thesilentballet.com/dnn/Reviews/2010/MostViewed/tabid/161/ctl/Details/mid/637/ItemID/3093/Default.aspx |title=The American Dollar - Atlas |author=Tom Butcher |work=thesilentballet.com |date=February 6, 2010 |accessdate=February 27, 2011}}</ref><ref>[http://www.redefinemag.com/music/reviews_album_2.php?artist=The-American-Dollar&id=1403 Album Review], Redefine Magazine, January, 2010.</ref><ref>[http://strangeglue.com/reviews/the-american-dollar-atlas Album Review] Strange Glue, January 5, 2010.</ref><ref>[http://www.absolutepunk.net/showthread.php?t=2064332 Atlas Review], [[Absolute Punk]].</ref> The band has toured America and Canada, and played shows in Russia, with plans to tour a wider swath of the world in 2012. The American Dollar's fifth full length album, Awake In The City, was released on March 24, 2012. On December 6th, 2014, the duo announced plans to begin recording a new album that will be released in 2015.<ref>[https://www.facebook.com/theamericandollar] The American Dollar Facebook Page</ref>\n\nThe band has achieved considerable success in mainstream culture both within the United States and internationally while working in traditionally eclectic genres. Their music has been a pivotal addition to television shows that run the gamut from CSI: Miami to MLB Network specials, and also film trailers such as Extremely Loud & Incredibly Close and Up In The Air. <ref>[http://www.imdb.com/name/nm2923503/resume?ref_=nm_ov_res] The American Dollar on IMDb</ref> Partially due to their rising popularity, the band has been recognized by prominent music industry figures such as The Recording Academy and Tom Windish, describing what they do as \u201cbrilliant\u201d and \u201c\u2026almost mathematical, or classical-based. It\u2019s not just simple chord progressions on a guitar.\u201d<ref>[http://www.grammy.com/news/explosions-in-the-sky-mogwai-and-sigur-r-s-have-post-rock-euphoria] Grammy.com Feature</ref>\n\nIn August of 2011 the band brought a copyright infringement lawsuit against Joel and Victoria Osteen and the Lakewood Church for using their music on DVD\u2019s and television broadcasts without permission. U.S. Federal District Judge Keith Ellison concluded the Plaintiffs properly stated claims for infringement but dismissed the claims against the Osteens themselves with leave to amend certain pleading technicalities. After several failed appeal attempts by the Osteens and Lakewood Church to the 5th Circuit courts, the case was later settled on undisclosed terms.<ref>[http://religionclause.blogspot.com/2012/02/copyright-infringement-claims-against.html] Religion Clause</ref><ref>[http://www.law360.com/articles/465286/5th-circ-won-t-toss-copyright-suit-against-televangelist] Law 360</ref><ref>[http://blog.chron.com/believeitornot/2011/08/secular-band-the-american-dollar-wants-big-bucks-from-lakewood-church] Houston Chronicle</ref><ref>[http://www.legalzoom.com/news/entertainment/recordings/new-york-band-sues-texas-800587194] Legalzoom</ref><ref>[http://www.christianpost.com/news/joel-osteen-church-sued-by-band-for-3m-54585] The Christian Post</ref><ref>[http://blog.chron.com/believeitornot/2012/02/judge-favors-lakewood-in-music-copyright-suit] Houston Chronicle</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"18949200":{"pageid":18949200,"ns":0,"title":"Aphex Twin","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use British [http://syro2eznzea2xbpi.com/ Syro]\n}}\n'''Richard David James''' (born 18 August 1971), best known by his alias '''Aphex Twin''', is a British electronic musician and composer. He has been described by ''[[The Guardian (newspaper)|The Guardian]]'' as \"the most inventive and influential figure in contemporary electronic music\", and is the co-founder of [[Rephlex Records]] with [[Grant Wilson-Claridge]].<ref name=\"lester\">{{cite news |first=Paul |last=Lester |title=Tank boy |url=http://arts.guardian.co.uk/fridayreview/story/0,,734809,00.html |work=[[The Guardian]] |publisher=[[Guardian Media Group]] |date=5 October 2001 |accessdate=2008-06-14 | location=London| archiveurl= http://web.archive.org/web/20080610133038/http://arts.guardian.co.uk/fridayreview/story/0,,734809,00.html| archivedate= 10 June 2008 <!--DASHBot-->| deadurl= no}}</ref> Aphex Twin's album ''[[Selected Ambient Works 85-92]]'' was called the best album of the 1990s by [[Fact Magazine (United Kingdom)|FACT Magazine]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.factmag.com/2012/09/03/the-100-best-albums-of-the-1990s-100-81/101/ |title=The 100 Best Albums of the 1990s \u2013 FACT Magazine: Music News, New Music |publisher=Factmag.com |date=2012-09-03 |accessdate=2014-02-20}}</ref>\n\nJames has also released a number of EPs as '''AFX''' since 1991 including the ''Analogue Bubblebath'' and ''Analord'' series of EPs. James has also used and continues to use several other aliases, such as Polygon Window, Caustic Window, and the Tuss.\n\nIn addition to Rephlex, James has released Aphex Twin records on [[Warp Records|Warp]], [[R&S Records|R&S]], [[Sire Records|Sire]], [[Mighty Force]], Rabbit City and Men Records. Following public sightings of the Aphex Twin logo in London, United Kingdom, and New York City, United States, in August 2014, the Aphex Twin [[Twitter]] account confirmed the release of ''[[Syro]]'', his sixth studio album. Following a subsequent press release, ''Syro'' was officially released on 23 September 2014 through the Warp music label. In February 2015, ''Syro'' won James the [[Grammy Award for Best Dance/Electronic Album]]. Records|EMI]]\n* ISO\n* [[Columbia Records|Columbia]]\n* [[Bertelsmann Music Group|BMG]]\n* [[Pye Records|Pye]]\n* [[Vocalion Records|Vocalion]]\n* [[Parlophone Records|Parlophone]]\n}}\n    | website        = {{URL| davidbowie.com}}\n    }}\n}}\n\n'''David Bowie''' ({{IPAc-en|\u02c8|b|o\u028a|.|i}};<ref name=\"bbc_say_bowie\">{{cite web |url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/blogs/magazinemonitor/2007/01/how_to_say_bowie.shtml |title=How to say: Bowie |accessdate=16 September 2010 |publisher=BBC  |date=8 January 2008 }}</ref> born '''David Robert Jones''', 8 January 1947) is an English singer, songwriter, [[multi-instrumentalist]], record producer, arranger, and actor. He is also a painter and collector of [[fine art]].<ref name=NYT_Art>{{cite news|title=TALKING ART WITH/David Bowie; A Musician's Parallel Passion|url=http://www.nytimes.com/1998/06/14/arts/talking-art-with-david-bowie-a-musician-s-parallel-passion.html|accessdate=October 13, 2014|work=[[New York Times]]|date=June 14, 1998}}</ref> Bowie  has been a major figure in the world of popular music for over four decades, and is renowned as an innovator, particularly for his work in the 1970s. He is known for his distinctive baritone voice as well as the intellectual depth and eclecticism of his work. Aside from his musical abilities, he is recognised for his [[androgynous]] beauty, which was an iconic element to his image, particularly in the 1970s and 1980s.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.oystermag.com/street-style-before-street-style-david-bowie|title=Street Style Before Street Style: David Bowie|work=Oyster Magazine|date=September 15, 2012|accessdate=September 16, 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite book|first1=Leland|first2=Kathy A.|last1=Poague|last2=Parsons|title=Susan Sontag: An Annotated Bibliography 1948-1992|pages=133|isbn=9-781-135575359|publisher=Routledge|year=2003}}</ref>\n\nBowie first caught the eye and ear of the public in July 1969 when his song \"[[Space Oddity (song)|Space Oddity]]\" reached the top five of the [[UK Singles Chart]]. After a three-year period of experimentation he re-emerged in 1972 during the [[glam rock]] era with the flamboyant, [[androgynous]] [[alter ego]] Ziggy Stardust, spearheaded by the hit single \"[[Starman (song)|Starman]]\" and the album ''[[The Rise and Fall of Ziggy Stardust and the Spiders from Mars]]''. Bowie's impact at that time, as described by biographer David Buckley, \"challenged the core belief of the rock music of its day\" and \"created perhaps the biggest cult in popular culture.\"<ref name=\"buckley_legacy\" /> The relatively short-lived Ziggy persona proved merely one facet of a career marked by continual reinvention, musical innovation and striking visual presentation.\n\nIn 1975, Bowie achieved his first major American crossover success with the number-one single \"[[Fame (David Bowie song)|Fame]]\" and the hit album ''[[Young Americans (album)|Young Americans]]'', which the singer characterised as \"[[plastic soul]]\". The sound constituted a radical shift in style that initially alienated many of his UK devotees. He then confounded the expectations of both his record label and his American audiences by recording the [[minimalist music|minimalist]] album ''[[Low (David Bowie album)|Low]]'' (1977)\u2014the first of three collaborations with [[Brian Eno]] over the next two years. ''Low'', ''[[\"Heroes\"]]'', and ''[[Lodger (album)|Lodger]]'', the so-called \"Berlin Trilogy\" albums, all reached the UK top five and received lasting critical praise. After uneven commercial success in the late 1970s, Bowie had UK number ones with the 1980 single \"[[Ashes to Ashes (David Bowie song)|Ashes to Ashes]]\", its parent album ''[[Scary Monsters (and Super Creeps)]]'', and \"[[Under Pressure]]\", a 1981 collaboration with [[Queen (band)|Queen]]. He then reached a new commercial peak in 1983 with ''[[Let's Dance (David Bowie album)|Let's Dance]]'', which yielded several hit singles. Throughout the 1990s and 2000s, Bowie continued to experiment with musical styles, including [[blue-eyed soul]], [[industrial music|industrial]], [[adult contemporary music|adult contemporary]], and [[drum and bass|jungle]]. He has not toured since the 2003\u201304 [[Reality Tour]] and has not performed live since 2006. Bowie's latest studio album ''[[The Next Day]]'' was released in March 2013.\n\nDavid Buckley says of Bowie: \"His influence has been unique in popular culture\u2014he has permeated and altered more lives than any comparable figure.\"<ref name=\"buckley_legacy\" /> In the BBC's 2002 poll of the [[100 Greatest Britons]], Bowie was placed at number 29. Throughout his career, he has sold an estimated 140&nbsp;million albums.<ref name=\"abc\">{{cite web |url=http://www.abc.net.au/news/2013-01-08/david-bowie-performs-on-stage/4457258 |title=David Bowie performs on stage |accessdate=6 May 2013 |publisher=ABC News |date=8 January 2013 }}</ref> In the UK, he has been awarded nine Platinum album certifications, 11 Gold and eight Silver, and in the US, five Platinum and seven Gold certifications. In 2004, ''[[Rolling Stone]]'' ranked him 39th on their list of the \"100 Greatest Artists of All Time\", and 23rd on their list of the best singers of all time."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"359180":{"pageid":359180,"ns":0,"title":"Biosphere (musician)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Biosphere\n| image               = Geir_Jenssen_at_Sajeta_2011.jpg\n| caption             = Geir Jenssen performing at Creative Camp Sajeta 2011, [[Tolmin]], [[Slovenia]].\n| background          = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_name          = Geir Jenssen\n| birth_date = {{birth date and age|mf=yes|1962|5|30}}\n| alias               = Bleep, Cosmic Explorer, E-Man\n| origin              = [[Troms\u00f8]], [[Norway]]\n| instrument          = [[Electronic keyboard]], [[synthesizer]]\n| genre               = [[Ambient techno]], [[Drone music|drone]],  [[chillout]], [[ambient house]]\n| occupation          = [[Producer (music)|Producer]]\n| years_active        = 1983\u2013present\n| label               = [[Beatservice Records]], [[Touch Music|Touch]], Biophon Records, [[Apollo Records (Belgium)|Apollo]], [[Origo Sound]], [[Crammed Discs#Sub-labels|SSR Records]], [[Rune Grammofon]]\n| associated_acts     = [[Higher Intelligence Agency]]<br>[[Bel Canto (band)|Bel Canto]]\n| website             = {{URL|http://www.biosphere.no}}\n}}\n\n'''Biosphere''' is the main recording name of '''Geir Jenssen''' (born May 30, 1962),<ref name=\"Thompson\">Thompson, Dave (2000) ''Alternative Rock'', Miller Freeman, ISBN 0-87930-607-6, p.197-198</ref> a Norwegian musician who has released a notable catalogue of [[ambient music|ambient]] [[electronic music]]. His collaborations with musicians around the world have made him \"one of the most sought-after producers in the music industry.\" <ref>http://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=5586671</ref> He currently lives in [[Los Angeles]].\n\nBrook toured as a member of the [[David Sylvian|Sylvian]] and [[Robert Fripp|Fripp]] tour group, with the final concert at the [[Royal Albert Hall]] in December 1994 documented on the album ''[[Damage: Live]]''.<ref>http://www.allmusic.com/artist/michael-brook-mn0000456423/biography</ref> He also opened the concerts with a solo set, featuring the [[Infinite Guitar]] with effects and sequencer backing. Another notable collaboration was ''[[Sleeps with the Fishes]]'' with [[Clan Of Xymox]] member [[Pieter Nooten]] ([[4AD]], 1987). In 1998, he produced the album \"[[Volc\u00e1n: Tributo a Jos\u00e9 Jos\u00e9]]\", a tribute album to singer [[Jose Jose]]. In 2006, the solo album ''RockPaperScissors'' was released, with an ambient remix version following in 2007. Brook toured small venues in Canada and the United States in late January/early February, 2007. In writing about his score for the film 2015 film Brooklyn, [[Variety (magazine)|Variety]] said the film was \"buoyed along by a beautiful Michael Brook score <ref>http://variety.com/2015/film/reviews/sundance-film-review-saoirse-ronan-in-brooklyn-1201419559/</ref> and the [[Hollywood Reporter]] praised his \"evocative scoring.\" M-II]]\n}}\n\n'''Brian Patrick Carroll''' (born May 13, 1969), better known by his stage name '''Buckethead''', is an American [[guitarist]] and multi-instrumentalist who has worked within many genres of music. He has released 159 studio albums, four special releases and one EP. He has also performed on more than 50 other albums by other artists. His music spans such diverse areas as [[progressive metal]], [[funk]], [[blues]], [[jazz]], [[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]], [[Ambient music|ambient]], and [[avant-garde music]].\n\nBuckethead is famous for wearing a [[KFC]] bucket on his head, emblazoned with an orange [[bumper sticker]] reading ''FUNERAL'' in capital black block letters, and an expressionless plain white mask which, according to Buckethead, was inspired by his seeing ''[[Halloween 4: The Return of Michael Myers]]''.<ref name=\"MTV.com\">{{cite web|url=http://www.mtv.com/news/articles/1458813/kurt-loder-meets-gnrs-buckethead.jhtml |title=Beneath The Bucket, Behind The Mask: Kurt Loder Meets GN'R's Buckethead - Music, Celebrity, Artist News |publisher=MTV.com |date=2002-11-21 |accessdate=2013-03-19}}</ref> At one point, he changed to a plain white bucket that no longer bore the KFC logo, but subsequently reverted to his trademark KFC bucket. He also incorporates [[nunchaku]] and [[Robot (dance)|robot dancing]] into his stage performances.<ref>Staff [http://www.spinner.com/tag/Buckethead/ Craziest Costumed Acts: No. 17], ''Spinner'', Oct 19, 2007. Retrieved January 6, 2009</ref><ref>Karevoll, Richard, [http://media.www.theechotimes.com/media/storage/paper347/news/2008/03/03/Ae/A.Closer.Look.At.Buckethead-3260934.shtml A Closer Look at Buckethead], ''The Echo Times'', March 3, 2008. Retrieved January 6, 2009</ref><ref name=mtv>{{cite web|url = http://www.mtv.com/news/articles/1458813/20021121/guns_n_roses.jhtml |title = Beneath The Bucket, Behind The Mask: Kurt Loder Meets GN'R's Buckethead|accessdate = 2007-12-09 |author=Loder, Kurt |date=  November 21, 2002|publisher = MTV}}</ref>\n\nAs an instrumentalist, Buckethead has received critical acclaim for his [[electric guitar]] playing, and is considered one of today's more innovative guitarists.<ref>Cooper, Sean, [{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p60553/biography|pure_url=yes}} Buckethead Biography], ''AllMusic''. Vikernes began making music in 1988, but it was not until 1991 that he recorded his first demos as Burzum. The word \"burzum\" means \"darkness\" in the [[Black Speech]], a [[fictional language]] crafted by [[J. R. R. Tolkien]].<ref name=\"story1\">{{cite web |url=http://www.burzum.org/eng/library/a_burzum_story01.shtml |title=A Burzum Story: Part I |last=Vikernes |first=Varg |authorlink=Varg Vikernes |date=December 2004 |work=burzum.org |accessdate=25 May 2013}}</ref> The project became a part of the [[early Norwegian black metal scene]] and one of the most influential acts in [[black metal]].<ref>{{cite video |people=[[Sam Dunn|Dunn, Sam]] |year=2005 |title=[[Metal: A Headbanger's Journey]] |medium=motion picture |location=Canada}}</ref> Vikernes recorded the first four Burzum albums between January 1992 and March 1993. However, the releases were spread out, with many months between the recording and the release of each album. In May 1994, Vikernes was sentenced to 21 years in prison for the murder of [[Mayhem (band)|Mayhem]] guitarist [[Euronymous|\u00d8ystein 'Euronymous' Aarseth]] and the arson of three churches.\n\nWhile imprisoned, Vikernes recorded two [[dark ambient]] albums using only [[synthesizer]]s, as he did not have access to drums, guitar or bass. Since his release from prison in 2009, he has recorded three further black metal albums and another ambient/electronic album.\n\nAlthough Vikernes is known for his political views, he does not use Burzum to promote those views. Burzum has never played live and Vikernes says he has no intention of doing so."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2349187":{"pageid":2349187,"ns":0,"title":"Ray Buttigieg","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{BLP primary sources|date=April 2009}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = Ray Buttigieg\n| image               = \n| image_size          = \n| landscape           = <!-- yes, if wide image, otherwise leave blank -->\n| alt                 = \n| caption             = \n| background          = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_name          = \n| birth_date          = {{birth date and age|1955|05|01}}\n| birth_place         = [[Gozo]], [[Malta]]\n| origin              = [[New York City]], [[New York]], [[United States]]\n| death_date          = <!-- {{death date and age|YYYY|MM|DD|YYYY|MM|DD}} (death date 1st) -->\n| death_place         = \n| genre               = [[Rock music|Rock]]\n| occupation          = [[Poet]], [[musician]]\n| instrument          = [[Guitar]]\n| years_active        = <!-- YYYY\u2013YYYY (or \u2013present) -->\n| label               = \n| associated_acts     = [[Cykx]]\n| website             = {{URL|http://www.raybuttigieg.com}}\n}}\n'''Ray Buttigieg''' (born May 1, 1955 in [[Gozo]], [[Malta]]) is a [[poet]] and [[musician]].\n\nHe attended [[Qala, Malta|Qala]] primary school, then the Lyceum in Victoria, Gozo. Bach]] assembled phrase-by-phrase on a [[Moog synthesizer]], at the time a relatively new and unknown instrument. The album earned three [[Grammy Awards]] in 1969. Other classical recordings followed.\n\nCarlos later began releasing original compositions, including the first-ever album of synthesized environmental sounds, ''[[Sonic Seasonings]]'' (1972) and an album exploring [[Alternate tunings#Alternative tunings|alternate tunings]] ''[[Beauty in the Beast]]'' (1986). They have recorded albums in a wide variety of styles ranging from experimental music to [[progressive rock]], all of which had an avant-garde edge. Cluster was active from 1971 until 2010, releasing a total of 15 albums, including two collaborations with [[Brian Eno]]. Musician, writer and rock historian [[Julian Cope]] places three Cluster albums in his Krautrock Top 50<ref name=\"Cope\">{{cite web\n | last = Cope\n | first = Julian\n | authorlink =Julian Cope\n | title =A Krautrock Top 50\n | publisher = Shrimp's Krautrock Page\n | url = http://www.midsuffolk.unisonplus.net/Top%2050.htm#Cluster\n | accessdate = 2007-10-29}}</ref> and \"The Wire\" places Cluster's self-titled debut album in their \"One Hundred Records That Set The World On Fire\".<ref name=\"Wire\">{{cite web\n | last = Roy\n | first = Daryl Stephen\n |author2=Uncle Fester\n | title = 100 Records That Set The World On Fire (while no one was listening)\n | publisher =The Wire\n | year = 1992\n | url =http://www.rocklistmusic.co.uk/thewire.html#onfire\n | accessdate = 2007-10-29 |archiveurl = http://web.archive.org/web/20071019022442/http://www.rocklistmusic.co.uk/thewire.html#onfire <!-- Bot retrieved archive --> |archivedate = 2007-10-19}}</ref>\n\nAfter a decade long hiatus Cluster reunited in April, [[2007 in music|2007]]. They performed at the opening of [[documenta]] 12, a major [[art exhibition|exhibition]] of [[modern art|modern]] and [[contemporary art]] held every five years in [[Kassel]], Germany  on June 15, 2007.<ref name=\"documenta\">{{cite web\n | title = 50 Years of Documenta 1955-2005\n | work = Book Description\n | publisher = Edmunds Enterprises of America, Inc.\n | year = 2007\n | url = http://www.edmunds-enterprises.com/linux/modules/products/product_detail.php?mode=Books&ASIN=3865211461\n | accessdate = 2008-02-20 }}</ref> In late 2007 Cluster performed at concerts across Europe<ref name=\"Roedelius-news\">{{cite web\n | last = Roedelius\n | first = Hans-Joachim\n | authorlink = Hans-Joachim Roedelius\n | title = News\n | work = Official Website\n | year = 2007\n | url = http://www.roedelius.com/ \n | accessdate = 2008-02-19}}</ref> and played the United States in 2008 for the first time since 1996.<ref name=\"No Fun\">{{cite web\n | title = No Fun Fest 2008\n | year = 2008\n | url = http://www.nofunfest.com/2008.html\n | accessdate =2008-02-19}}</ref>\n\nCluster disbanded at the end of 2010.  Their final concert was on December 5 of that year.<ref name=\"final\">{{cite web\n | title = Dieter Moebius..\n | year = 2011\n | url = http://www.dietermoebius.de/main.html\n | accessdate = 2011-02-23}}</ref>\nIn 2011, Roedelius recruited Onnen Bock to reactivate Cluster under the name of \"Qluster\". Their debut release came in the form of a trilogy entitled ''Rufen - Fragen - Antworten'' (''Calling - Questioning - Responding''), containing a piano record, a live documentary and a normal record.<ref name=\"qluster.info\">{{cite web|url=http://www.qluster.info |title=Qluster |publisher=Qluster.info |date= |accessdate=2014-07-03}}</ref> In January 2013, Qluster released their fourth record ''Lauschen'' (''Eavesdropping''), a live record with world musician Armin Metz.<ref>{{cite web|author=surver:net http://www.surver.net/ |url=http://www.indigo.de/news/vorschau |title=News Vorschau |publisher=indigo.de |date= |accessdate=2014-07-03}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"174846":{"pageid":174846,"ns":0,"title":"Cocteau Twins","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use dmy dates|date=December 2011}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name = Cocteau Twins\n| landscape = yes\n| background = group_or_band\n| image = Cocteau Twins promo sheet.jpg\n| caption = {{hlist|[[Robin Guthrie]]|[[Elizabeth Fraser]]|[[Simon Raymonde]]}}\n| origin = [[Grangemouth]], Scotland\n| genre = {{startplainlist}}\n* [[Alternative rock]]\n* [[Ethereal wave]]\n* [[Post-punk]]\n* [[Gothic rock]]&#x2009;<ref>{{cite book |author=Reynolds, Simon |title=Rip It Up and Start Again: Postpunk 1978-1984 |page=423 |publisher=London: Faber and Faber, 2005 |isbn=0-571-21569-6}}</ref>\n* {{nowrap|[[Dream pop]]&#x2009;<!--About.com considered reliable source as Anthony Carew is listed among their critics:--><ref>{{cite web |url=http://altmusic.about.com/od/top10lists/tp/Shoegaze-Albums.htm |title=Top 10 Shoegaze Albums |publisher=[[About.com]] |accessdate=5 February 2015 |author=Carew, Anthony}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal |url=https://books.google.com.tr/books?id=FSsEAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA31&dq=%22Cocteau+Twins%22+%22dream+pop%22&hl=tr&sa=X&ei=8uXTVM6RDsL2UJDDgsgD&ved=0CDgQ6AEwBQ#v=onepage&q=%22Cocteau%20Twins%22%20%22dream%20pop%22&f=false |title=Delays - The original members were [[Elizabeth Fraser]] (vocals), [[Robin Guthrie]] (guitar, drum machine) and [[Will Heggie]] (bass guitar), who was replaced by multi-instrumentalist [[Simon Raymonde]] early in the band's career.\n\nWhile the entire band earned much critical praise, Elizabeth Fraser's distinctive soprano vocals received the most attention. \"Jhonn Balance\"&mdash;and his partner [[Peter Christopherson]], aka \"Sleazy\".<ref name=\"AbrAhAdAbrA\">{{cite news | url=http://maldoror.com/artists/coil/abrahadabra1.htm | title=Coil Interview: The Price of Existence is Eternal Warfare | work=AbrAhAdAbrA | issue=1 | date=23 January 1985 | accessdate=19 April 2010}}</ref> The duo worked together on a series of releases before Balance chose the name Coil, which he claimed to be inspired by the [[omnipresence]] of the [[Electromagnetic coil|coil]]'s shape in nature. Today, Coil remains one of the most influential and best-known [[industrial music]] groups.\n\nThe group's first official release as Coil was a  1984 12\" album titled ''[[How to Destroy Angels (song)|How to Destroy Angels]]'' released on the Belgian [[Les Disques du Cr\u00e9puscule]]'s sublabel LAYLAH Antirecords. Following the 12\"s success, [[Some Bizarre Records]] produced two albums, ''[[Scatology (album)|Scatology]]'', ''[[Horse Rotorvator]]'' and Coil departed SomeBizzare Label and Produced ''[[Love's Secret Domain]]'', which met with little commercial success, but were praised as innovative due to their blend of industrial music and [[acid house]].<ref name=\"Liar Society\">{{cite web\n| url = http://liarsociety.tripod.com/blog/index.blog?from=20041130\n| archiveurl = http://web.archive.org/web/20080206210600/http://liarsociety.tripod.com/blog/index.blog?from=20041130\n| archivedate = 6 February 2008\n| title = Coil: Scatology, Horse Rotorvator, Love's Secret Domain\n| publisher = Liar Society \n| date=2004-10-30\n| accessdate=12 February 2007\n}}</ref><ref name=\"NME 1985\">{{Cite news\n | last =Kopf\n | first = Biba\n | author-link =\n | last2 =\n | first2 =\n | author2-link =\n | title = The Soil And Spoil Tactics Of Coil\n | newspaper = NME\n | pages =\n | date = 20 April 1985\n | url =\n | postscript =<!--None--> }}</ref>\n\nIn 1985, the group began working on a series of soundtracks, amongst them music for the first ''[[Hellraiser]]'' movie based on the novel ''The Hellbound Heart'' by their acquaintance at that time, [[Clive Barker]]. The group's first live performance in 16 years occurred in 1999, and began a series of mini-tours that would last until 2004.<ref name=\"Brainwashed Live Archive\">{{cite web\n| url = http://www.brainwashed.com/coil/live/\n| title = Live Archive\n| publisher = brainwashed.com \n| date=2004\n| accessdate=12 February 2007\n}}</ref> Following the death of John Balance on 13 November 2004, Christopherson announced via their official record label website [[Threshold House]] that Coil as an entity had ceased to exist."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"5314368":{"pageid":5314368,"ns":0,"title":"B.J. The group was founded by Paul Lemos, the group's only consistent member. Most of Controlled Bleeding's released recordings feature two main collaborators, Chris Moriarty and vocalist Joe Papa, who both died in the late 2000s.\n\nSince their first full-length release in 1983, Controlled Bleeding have released over 30 albums spanning several different genres, many of which were released on notable independent labels. Their cross-genre approach combined with the out-of-print status of many of the group's releases is reminiscent of the work of other experimental and cross-genre groups of the 80s and 90s such as [[Coil (band)|Coil]] and [[Swans (band)|Swans]]."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"72735":{"pageid":72735,"ns":0,"title":"Cusco","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{About|the city in Peru}}\n{{Infobox ({{lang-es|link=no|Cuzco}}, {{IPA-es|\u02c8kusko|}}; {{lang-qu|Qusqu ''or'' Qosqo}}, {{IPA-qu|\u02c8q\u0254sq\u0254|IPA}}), is a city in southeastern [[Peru]], near the [[Sacred Valley|Urubamba Valley]] of the [[Andes]] mountain range. It is the capital of the [[Cusco Region]] as well as the [[Cusco Province]]. In 2013, the city had a population of 435,114. Located on the eastern end of the Knot of Cuzco, its elevation is around {{convert|3400|m|ft|abbr=on}}.\n\nThe site was the historic capital of the [[Inca Empire]] from the 13th into the 16th century until the Spanish conquest. In 1983 Cusco was declared a [[World Heritage Site]] by [[UNESCO]]. It has become a major tourist destination, receiving nearly 2&nbsp;million visitors a year. He disclaims any religious meaning in the [[stage name]]; he describes it as short for his full name, and the [[full stop]] or period as indicating that status as an abbreviation.{{Citation needed|date=July 2009}} \n\nchrist. performs as a solo [[electronic music]] artist, and his music is often likened to that of the (also Scottish) electronic group [[Boards of Canada]]. In fact, credited as ''Chris H.'', he was an early participant in the nebulous [[Hexagon Sun]] collective from which Boards of Canada emerged, and was a collaborator with the group until approximately 1995. He appeared on the ''[[Twoism]]'' album, reissued by [[Warp Records|Warp]] in 2002.<ref>[http://www.matadorrecords.com/boards_of_canada/biography.html Matador Records]</ref> Horne\u2019s departure was amicable and he thanks the duo on his ''[[Pylonesque EP]]'' issued on the [[Benbecula Records]] label in 2001. He followed this release with a full length album ''Metamorphic Reproduction Miracle'' on the same label which was very well received within the genre.<ref>[http://www.themilkfactory.co.uk/reviews/christ_mrm.htm themilkfactory.co.uk]</ref><ref>[http://www.dustedmagazine.com/reviews/929 Dusted Magazine] (14 Aug 2003)</ref>\n\nchrist. has toured the UK, Europe and Japan and performed a live session for [[John Peel]] at Maida Vale studios in London on 17 December 2003. This session became notable among Peel\u2019s fans as being the only known occasion upon which the legendary DJ requested an encore.<ref>[http://web.archive.org/web/20110721052925/http://www.benbecula.com/artists/christ..shtml Benbecula Records] (archived 21 Jul 2011)</ref> He released his fourth full length album, his = \n| genre               = [[Celtic music|Celtic]], [[folk music|folk]]\n| occupation          = Instrumentalist, composer, choral director\n| instrument          = [[Hammered dulcimer]], [[spoon Velez]]\n| website             = <!-- {{URL|example.com}} -->\n| notable_instruments = \n}}\n'''Malcolm Dalglish''' (born  August 14, 1952) is an [[United States of America|American]] [[hammered dulcimer]] player and builder, composer, and choral director.\n\nA virtuoso performer on the hammer dulcimer, he is a former member of the folk/Celtic trio Metamora and has performed frequently with the percussionist [[Glen Velez]]. In addition to the dulcimer, Dalglish also plays the [[spoon (musical instrument)|spoon]]s and [[Bones (instrument)|bones]] (both traditional American percussion instruments).  Beginning in the mid-1970s he honed his playing at Hap's Irish Pub in Cincinnati in a duo with flutist and concertina player Grey Larsen.  He also composes prolifically for choir, and many of his compositions are for choir with dulcimer accompaniment. He has received more than 50 commissions to compose for choirs around the world. He played the hammered dulcimer in the score for the 1981 film ''[[Tuck Everlasting (1981 film)|Tuck Everlasting]]''. Several of his songs with the Ooolite choral group come from the poetic work of [[Wendell Berry]].\n\nDalglish attended [[Oberlin College]] and the [[University of Cincinnati College-Conservatory of Music]]. He lives in [[Bloomington, Indiana|Bloomington]], [[Indiana]], where his publishing company, Ooolitic Music, is based."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"3574081":{"pageid":3574081,"ns":0,"title":"David Darling (musician)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{About|the American musician|other persons with the same name|David Darling (disambiguation){{!}}David Darling}}\n\n'''David Darling''' (born March 3, 1941) is an American [[cello|cellist]] and [[composer]]. His tracks have been included in numerous compilation albums such as the 2007 ''[[In Search of Sunrise 6: Ibiza]]'' CD. The February 2008 issue of ''[[Mixmag]]''{{'}}s music magazine included a free CD which was titled ''MixMag Presents: The Hottest New Name In Dance! DEADMAU5 Tech-Trance-Electro-Madness'', mixed by Zimmerman. Tracks have also been included and presented on [[Armin van Buuren]]'s ''[[A State of Trance]]'' radio show. His debut album, ''[[Get Scraped]]'', was released in 2005, followed by others in the next few years.\n\nAs well as his own solo releases, Zimmerman has worked alongside other DJs and producers, such as [[Kaskade]], MC Flipside, [[Rob Swire]] of [[Knife Party]] and [[Pendulum (band)|Pendulum]], [[Wolfgang Gartner]], Bighorse, and on a number of releases, he has partnered with [[Melleefresh]]. An early 12\" single produced on vinyl titled \"I Don't Want No Other\" was released by Joel Zimmerman under the alias \"Dred and Karma\".<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.discogs.com/artist/Dred+And+Karma |title=Dred And Karma Discography at Discogs |publisher=discogs |accessdate=June 18, 2013}}</ref> The 2006 album titled ''[[deadmau5 Circa 1998\u20132002]]'' was released using the alias \"Halcyon441\". He has performed in live and exclusive outdoor settings, including [[Banff National Park]], since 2000 and has released music on various international recording labels.<ref>[http://www.nytimes.com/2010/06/20/arts/music/20guitar.html New York Times, Steve Smith]</ref><ref>Allmusic, Ned Raggett.[{{Allmusic|class=album|id=r1714351|pure_url=yes}} All Music review]</ref><ref>Pitchfork.[http://pitchfork.com/reviews/albums/14427-rural-route-no-2 Pitchfork Review]</ref>\n\nHis work has been described as \"compositions that are patience incarnate\"<ref>Pitchfork Review on Fervency (2009)[http://pitchfork.com/reviews/albums/13417-fervency Pitchfork Review: \"Fervency\"]</ref> and \"encourage an emotional response even as its seemingly infinite, creeping swirl and hum threatens to numb. A difficult feat.\"<ref>Just Press Play Review on Kyle Bobby Dunn (2010)[http://www.justpressplay.net/music-reviews/38-reviews/6755-a-young-persons-guide-to-kyle-bobby-dunn.html JustPressPlay Review: \"A Young Person's Guide\"]</ref>\nIt is music that often \"captures a mood somewhere between sadness and strength; it's the sound of a respite that occurs after having survived an ordeal; it's sound as memory, as memorial.\"<ref>Bring Me the Head of Kyle Bobby Dunn Review (2012)[http://thefanzine.com/waver-change-bring-me-the-head-of-kyle-bobby-dunn/ The Fanzine Review: ''Bring Me the Head'']</ref>\n\nThe austere, tempered tonal shifts featured in many of his compositions subtly echo the work of minimalist forerunners like [[Morton Feldman]] and [[LaMonte Young]]. At the same time Dunn occasionally intersperses quaint, almost chamberal touches which evoke more traditionally classical sources.<ref>Mark Lesseraux, DOA Review of Young Person's Guide [http://www.adequacy.net/2010/07/guest-review-mark-lesseraux-reviews-kyle-bobby-dunns-a-young-persons-guide-to-kyle-bobby-dunn DOA Review by Mark Earthstar was encouraged by [[Krautrock]]/[[Kosmische Musik]]/electronic music artist, composer, and producer [[Klaus Schulze]] to relocate to [[Germany]] where they were signed by [[Sky Records]].  Schulze produced their second and most successful album, ''[[French Skyline]]''.  Earthstar is notable as the only American band who participated in Germany's Kosmische Musik/electronic music scene while still at its height.<ref name=\"Expose\">{{cite web\n  | last = Rea\n  | first = Dennis\n  | authorlink = Dennis Rea\n  |author2=Melton, Jeff\n  | title = Expos\u00e9 Magazine interview\n  | publisher = Expos\u00e9 Magazine\n  | date = December 2001\n  | url = http://www.dennisrea.com/expose.html\n  | accessdate = 2007-10-24}}</ref>\n\nThe Earthstar entry in the New Gibraltar Encyclopedia of Progressive Rock describes the wall of sound on the second and third albums:  \"[Group leader Craig] Wuest's vision propels these two albums, his desire apparently is to create music that doesn't necessarily suggest a particular instrument, rather creates a new texture. Therefore, though there are credits for flute, guitar, bass, violin, viola, French horn, sitar and vocals, it's pretty hard to distinguish any of these...\"<ref name=\"GEPR\">{{cite web\n  | last = Rea\n  | first = Dennis\n  | authorlink = Dennis Rea\n  |author2=other uncredited contributors\n  | title = New Gibraltar Encyclopedia of Progressive Rock, EA-EL\n  | date = 2005-01-20\n  | url = http://www.gepr.net/ea.html\n  | accessdate = 2007-10-24}}</ref>  Earthstar's style on ''French Skyline'' has been compared to Wolfgang Bock, Sangiuliano,<ref name=\"Groove1\">{{cite web\n  | last = Rijkens\n  | first = Paul\n  | title = Earthstar - French Skyline\n  | work = review\n  | publisher = Groove Unlimited\n  | year = 1999\n  | url = http://www.groove.nl/cd/2/28864.html\n  | accessdate = 2007-10-24}}</ref> and Klaus Schulze's own recordings.<ref name=\"Groove2\">{{cite web\n  | last = Jenkins\n  | first = Mark\n  | title = Earthstar - French Skyline\n  | work = review\n  | publisher = E-Mix Magazine\n  | year = 1999\n  | url = http://www.groove.nl/cd/2/28864.html\n  | accessdate = 2007-10-24}}</ref>  Other albums have a softer style with more distinct instrumentation.\n\nEarthstar is also notable for [[Craig Wuest]]'s heavy use of the [[Mellotron]] and the rare [[Birotron]], a variation on the Mellotron that can sustain notes beyond eight seconds.<ref name=\"Mellotron\">{{cite web\n  | title = Planet Mellotron Reviews: E1\n  | url = http://www.planetmellotron.com/reve1.htm#earthstar\n  | accessdate = 2007-10-24}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"7963285":{"pageid":7963285,"ns":0,"title":"Danielle Egnew","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=October 2013}}\n{{Infobox person\n|name        = Danielle Egnew\n|image       =\n|caption     =\n|birth_date  = {{Birth date|1969|2|28}}\n|birth_place = Billings, Montana\n|death_date  = <!-- {{Death date and age|YYYY|MM|DD|YYYY|MM|DD}} -->\n|death_place =\n|other_names =\n|known_for   =\n|occupation  = [[psychic]], musician, actress, media personality\n|nationality = American\n}}\n\n'''Danielle Egnew''' is a musician, actress, media personality, activist and self-described psychic known in the areas of music, film, radio and television for both performing and producing in all four genres. He trained at the [[Milan Conservatory|Conservatorio Verdi]] in Milan and under composer [[Luciano Berio]] in the early 1980s. Einaudi began his career as a classical composer, and soon began incorporating other styles and genres\u2014including  [[pop music|pop]], [[rock music|rock]], [[world music]], and [[folk music]].<ref name=\"telegraph\"/>\n\nEinaudi composed the scores for a number of films and trailers, including ''[[The Intouchables]]'' and ''[[I'm Still Here (2010 film)|I'm Still Here]]'', the TV miniseries ''[[Doctor Zhivago (TV miniseries)|Doctor Zhivago]]'', and ''Acquario'' in 1996, for which he won the [[Grolla d'oro]] for best soundtrack. He has also released a number of solo albums of piano and orchestra, notably ''[[I Giorni]]'' in 2001, ''[[Nightbook]]'' in 2009, and ''[[In a Time Lapse]]'' in 2013."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"3682878":{"pageid":3682878,"ns":0,"title":"Eluvium (musician)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{For|the geological or soil science term|Eluvium}}\n{{BLP sources|date=May 2013}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name = Eluvium\n| birth_name = Matthew Cooper\n| birth_date = \n| birth_place = [[Tennessee]], United States\n| origin = [[Portland, Oregon]]<br/>[[Seattle]], [[Washington (state)|Washington]]\n| genre = [[Ambient music|Ambient]], [[piano]], [[Minimal music|minimalism]], [[Experimental music|experimental]]\n| background = solo_singer\n| label = [[Temporary Residence Limited]], Watership Sounds\n| years_active = 2003\u2013present\n| associated_acts = [[Inventions (band)|Inventions]]\n| website = [http://www.eluvium.net/ www.eluvium.net]\n| image = File:EluviumMFNW.JPG\n| caption = Eluvium performing in Portland, Oregon\n}}\n\n'''Eluvium''' is the [[moniker]] of the American [[Ambient music|ambient]] recording artist Matthew Cooper, who currently resides in [[Portland, Oregon]].  Cooper, who was born in [[Tennessee]] and raised in [[Louisville, Kentucky]], before relocating to the [[Pacific Northwest|Northwest]], is known for blending various genres of [[experimental music]] including [[Electronic music|electronic]], [[Minimal music|minimalism]] and [[piano]]. His albums often feature artwork and photographs by Jeannie Paske.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.obsoleteworld.com/ |title=Obsolete World |publisher=Obsolete World |date= |accessdate=2013-05-22}}</ref>\n\nEluvium is currently signed to the [[record label]], [[Temporary Residence Limited]].\n<gallery>\nImage:\nImage:|Caption2\n</gallery>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"8734427":{"pageid":8734427,"ns":0,"title":"Emerald Web","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"'''Emerald Web''' was an American musical duo, made up of the husband-wife team of '''Bob Stohl''' and '''Kat Epple'''. Founded in 1978 and active through the 1980s, the Florida-based Stohl and Epple composed and recorded music in the New Age and electronica genres. In addition to recording their music and performing in concert, Emerald Web composed many television soundtracks, including National Geographic, PBS Nova, CNN,  Apple Computers, NASA and Carl Sagan's documentary films, winning several [[Emmy Award]]s. They also composed music for a wide range of other applications, from films to planetarium shows. They received a [[Grammy]] nomination in 1986 for their album ''Catspaw''.\n\nThey were known for innovative synthesizer orchestration and created a unique blend of \"electronic space music\" and acoustic instruments. Both Epple and Stohl were also flautists; their flute-dominated music achieved a distinctive sound among New Age artists. Stohl was also noted for his musicianship on the Lyricon, a woodwind/synthesizer hybrid.\n\nThe partnership ended with Stohl's death by drowning in 1990, at the age of 34. Epple has continued to compose and record under her own name, as a solo artist and with the ensemble White Crow (1997). She also played flute on [[Devin Townsend]]'s record ''[[Ghost (The Devin Townsend Project album)|Ghost]]''. On her own and as part of Emerald Web, Epple has won eight Emmys and ten [[Addy Awards]] for work in composing music for television."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"25129814":{"pageid":25129814,"ns":0,"title":"Emeralds (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Emeralds\n| image           = Emeralds-Riga.jpg\n| caption         = Emeralds\n| background      = non_performing_personnel\n| alias           =\n| origin          = [[Cleveland]], [[Ohio]], [[United States|U.S.]]\n| genre           = [[Ambient music|Ambient]]<br>[[electronic music]]\n| years_active    = 2006\u20132013\n| label           = [[Editions Mego]]\n| current_members = John Elliott<br/>[[Steve Hauschildt]]<br/>[[Mark McGuire (musician)|Mark McGuire]]\n| past_members    = \n}}\n'''Emeralds''' was an American [[electronic music]] trio founded in 2006 by members John Elliott, Steve Hauschildt and Mark McGuire. Records|Warner Bros.]], [[Warp Records|Warp]]\n|associated_acts = [[Roxy Music]], [[David Bowie]], [[Coldplay]], [[Talking Heads]], [[Robert Fripp]], [[Cluster (band)|Cluster]], [[Devo]], [[U2]], [[David Byrne]], [[Robert Wyatt]], [[801 (band)|801]], [[Genesis (band)|Genesis]], [[Damon Albarn]], [[Karl Hyde]], [[Fred Frith]]\n|website             = {{URL|http://brian-eno.net/}}\n{{Extra music sample|type=single |filename=Brian Eno - Dune Prophecy Theme.ogg |format=[[Ogg]] |title=Dune Prophecy Theme}}\n}}\n\n'''Brian Peter George St. John le Baptiste de la Salle Eno''',<ref>Estrella, Espie: [http://musiced.about.com/od/historyofmusic/p/ambientmusic.htm Ambient Music, about.com]</ref> [[Royal Designers for Industry|RDI]]<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.thersa.org/about-us/media/press-releases/brian-eno-one-of-12-new-royal-designers-for-industry |title=Brian Eno one of 12 new Royal Designers for Industry |publisher=RSA |accessdate=20 November 2012}}</ref> ({{IPAc-en|\u02c8|i\u02d0|n|o\u028a}}; born 15 May 1948 and originally christened '''Brian Peter George Eno'''), professionally known as '''Brian Eno''' or simply '''Eno''',<ref>{{cite web\n|url= http://www.motherjones.com/media/2012/11/brian-eno-lux-profile-interview-generative-art\n|title= Finding Eno\n|author=  Andrew Marantz|date= 31 December 2012\n|work=  Culture\n|publisher= Mother Jones\n|accessdate=  5 January 2013\n|quote= <nowiki>Because short, vowel-heavy nouns are in finite supply, the makers of crossword puzzles resort to familiar [names, [but m]ost of these people are known for exactly one thing.... [ENO] is an exception to the rule.</nowiki>\n}}</ref> is an English musician, composer, record producer, singer, and visual artist, known as one of the principal innovators of [[ambient music]].<ref>[[AllMusic]], Explore Music, \"[{{Allmusic|class=explore|id=style/d226|pure_url=yes}} Ambient]\"</ref>\n\nEno was a student of [[Roy Ascott]] on his ''Groundcourse'' at [[Ipswich]] Civic College. He then studied at [[Colchester Institute]] art school in Essex, England, taking inspiration from [[minimalism|minimalist]] painting. During his time on the art course at the Institute, he also gained experience in playing and making music through teaching sessions held in the adjacent music school. He joined the band [[Roxy Music]] as synthesiser player in the early 1970s. Roxy Music's success in the [[glam rock]] scene came quickly, but Eno soon became tired of touring and of conflicts with lead singer [[Bryan Ferry]].\n\nEno's solo music has explored more [[experimental music]]al styles and ambient music. It has also been immensely influential, pioneering ambient and [[generative music]],<ref name=\"ankeny\">Jason Ankeny, [{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p74178|pure_url=yes}} ((( Brian Eno &gt; Biography )))], allmusic</ref> innovating production techniques, and emphasising \"theory over practice\".<ref name=\"ankeny\" /> He also introduced the concept of [[chance music]] to popular audiences, partially through collaborations with other musicians.<ref>Prendergast, Mark ''The Ambient Century'', Bloomsbury UK, 2000. ISBN 0-7475-4213-9</ref> Eno has also worked as an influential music and album producer. By the end of the 1970s, Eno had worked with [[Robert Fripp]] on the LPs ''[[No Pussyfooting]]'' and ''[[Evening Star (album)|Evening Star]]'', [[David Bowie]] on the seminal \"[[Berlin Trilogy]]\" and helped popularise the American band [[Devo]] and the punk-influenced \"[[No Wave]]\" genre. He produced and performed on three albums by [[Talking Heads]], including ''[[Remain in Light]]'' (1980), and produced seven albums for [[U2]], including ''[[The Joshua Tree]]'' (1987). Eno has also worked on records by [[James (band)|James]], [[Laurie Anderson (performance artist)|Laurie Anderson]], [[Coldplay]], [[Paul Simon]], [[Grace Jones]], [[James Blake (musician)|James Blake]] and [[Slowdive]], among others.\n\nEno pursues multimedia ventures in parallel to his music career, including [[art installation]]s, a regular column on society and innovation in ''[[Prospect (magazine)|Prospect]]'' magazine, and \"[[Oblique Strategies]]\" (written with [[Peter Schmidt (artist)|Peter Schmidt]]), a deck of cards in which cryptic remarks or random insights are intended to resolve dilemmas. Eno continues to collaborate with other musicians, produce records, release his own music, and write."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1138559":{"pageid":1138559,"ns":0,"title":"Roger Eno","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{BLP sources|date= June 2012}}\n'''Roger Eugene Eno''' was born in [[Woodbridge, Suffolk|Woodbridge]], [[England]] in 1959. He is known primarily as an [[ambient music]] [[composer]].<ref>{{cite book|last=Gagn\u00e9|first=Nicole V.|title=Historical dictionary of modern and contemporary classical music|year=2012|publisher=Scarecrow Press|location=Lanham, Md.|isbn=9780810879621|pages=91|url=http://books.google.com/books?id=dTnN4bLQSD4C&pg=PA91&lpg=PA91&dq=composer+%22Roger+Eno%22&source=bl&ots=VjUM4853O5&sig=7YvC3_IMwCIiaioBQuU64jOsj1I&hl=en&sa=X&ei=RIUDUIr8IImK2wX8tJDACw&ved=0CE0Q6AEwBQ#v=onepage&q=composer%20%22Roger%20Eno%22&f=false}}</ref>    \n\nHe began [[euphonium]] lessons at 12, and at 16 entered Colchester College to study music. On graduating, and after a period of [[busking]] in London (where he briefly shared a house with artists [[Mark Wallinger]] and [[Andy Dog]]), he returned to Colchester to run a music therapy course at a local hospital for the mentally handicapped.\n\nHis first recording experience was in 1983 with his brother [[Brian Eno]] and [[Daniel Lanois]] for the album ''Apollo'' at Lanois\u2019 Grant Avenue Studios in Canada. His first solo album, ''Voices'', was released in 1985.  \n\nAlthough mainly regarded as a pianist, Roger Eno is in fact a multi-instrumentalist and keen singer, as demonstrated on his later solo albums and collaborations. He has worked with several key artists apart from his brother including [[Bill Nelson (musician)|Bill Nelson]], [[No-Man]], [[Lol Hammond]], [[Mads Arp]], [[Peter Hammill]], [[Tim Bowness]], and [[Michael Brook]], the most successful of which was probably his co-written album, ''The Familiar'', with [[Kate St John]].\n\nEno performs live on occasion and continues to write soundtracks. Much of his music has been used in films, including ''[[For All Mankind]]'', ''[[Nine and a Half Weeks]]'', ''[[Warm Summer Rain]]'' and ''[[The Jacket]]'', while tracks have been used in advertisements, including for Nissan and for Japan Railways.\n\nEno has recently recorded solo albums for, and established an online shop via, the UK-based internet label [[Burning Shed]]. In 2007, he contributed to the ''Mid/Air'' LP by [[Dive Index]], a collaborative music project of composer/producer Will Thomas.\n\nIn 2013 Eno released a new album, ''Endless City / Concrete Garden '', under the name Roger Eno / Plumbline.<ref>http://www.rogereno.com/new-for-2013.php</ref>\n\nA collection of Eno's work from 1988 to 1998, ''Little Things Left Behind'', was released in November 2013.<ref>http://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/p01n98hq</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"9482":{"pageid":9482,"ns":0,"title":"Enya","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Other uses}}\n{{Use British English|date=November 2012}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=July 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Enya\n| alias           = Enya Brennan\n| background      = solo_singer\n| image           = enyasweet.jpg\n| caption         = Enya in 2001 at the premiere of ''[[Sweet November (2001 film)|Sweet November]]'' in New York\n| birth_name      = Eithne N\u00ed Bhraon\u00e1in\n| birth_date      = {{Birth date and age|df=yes|1961|5|17}}\n| birth_place     = [[Gweedore]], [[County Donegal]], [[Ireland]]\n| occupation      = [[Singer-songwriter]], [[musician|instrumentalist]], [[Record producer|producer]]\n| instrument      = [[Vocals]], [[piano]], [[synthesiser]]\n| genre           = [[Celtic music|Celtic]], [[World music|world]], [[New-age music|new-age]]<ref>{{cite web|last=Thomas |first=Stephen |url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/enya-p4197 |title=Enya |work=AllMusic |date=17 May 1961 |accessdate=11 May 2012}}</ref>\n| years_active    = 1980\u2013present\n| label           =[[Warner Bros. His hometown is [[Staten Island]], [[New York]]. He plays several instruments including the [[flute]], [[percussion]], [[synthesizer]] and [[Keyboard instrument|keyboards]]. In the New Age genre, his music is generally sounds of nature combined with flute melodies and other instruments for [[ambient music|ambient]] and [[meditation|meditative]] purposes.\n\nIn 1979, he and his wife, harpist Dudley Evenson, founded the independent record company Soundings of the Planet outside of [[Tucson, Arizona]]. Originally a poet-performer in Pennsylvania, he relocated to San Francisco at the beginning of the 1980s.  He was a member of Thessalonians and the original Melting Euphoria, had a solo project called Spaceship Eyes, and since 1996 has led the [[Spirits Burning]] space rock collective. Various cable and TV network programs have also used Falcone's music.''<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.home.earthlink.net/~falcone/filmtv.html |title=Film and TV Discography of Don Falcone |publisher=Home.earthlink.net |date= |accessdate=2014-04-09}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1800136":{"pageid":1800136,"ns":0,"title":"Falling Up (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=July 2013}}\n{{refimprove|date=February 2012}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = Falling Up\n| image               = FallingUp2004.jpg\n| caption             = The original six members of Falling Up (2004)\n| image_size          = 250px\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[Albany, Oregon|Albany]], [[Oregon]], United States\n| genre               = [[Christian rock]], [[hard rock]], [[experimental rock]], [[post-grunge]], [[ambient pop]], [[nu metal]], [[art rock]], [[indie rock]]\n| years_active        = 2001\u2013present\n| label               = [[BEC Recordings|BEC]], Independent\n| associated_acts     = \n| website             = {{URL|http://www.fallinguplives.com/}}\n| current_members     = Jessy Ribordy<br />Jeremy Miller<br />Josh Shroy<br />Nick Lambert\n| past_members        = [[Archers Rise|Tom Cox]]<br />Michael \"DJ Wax Wizard\" Humphrey<br />[[Joseph Kisselburgh]]<br />Adam Taylor<br />Micah Sannan<br />Andrew \"A-Dub\" Wadlow\n}}\n\n'''Falling Up''' is an American [[experimental rock]] band from [[Albany, Oregon|Albany]], [[Oregon]]. Falling Up formed in October 2001,<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.linkedin.com/in/jessyribordy |title=Jessy Ribordy's LinkedIn Page |author= Jessy Ribordy |quote= Singer/Songwriter/Guitarist/Producer, Falling Up, October 2001 \u2013 Present (9 years 9 months) |accessdate=June 12, 2011}}</ref> and released their debut album called ''[[Crashings]]'' in 2004. They were signed to [[BEC Recordings]] until 2010 when they went independent. The band's name is derived from the first song they wrote, which refers to how imperfect people are, but how sufficient the grace of [[God]] is to compensate for it. In harmony with their name, their lyrics are heavily [[divine grace|grace]]-themed.\n\nAs well as going through several different band line-ups (with at least one different one per album), Falling Up has gone through several transformations in terms of musical style mainly due to a constantly changing line-up, in which certain members who played instruments on previous albums left the band. For example, the band's original turntablists, Andrew Wadlow and Michael Humphrey, left after their first two albums, which caused them to morph into a more [[electronic rock]] sound with the welcome of keyboardist Adam Taylor (who did not play turntables). With their debut, ''Crashings'', the band introduced a [[nu metal]]-influenced style with [[raprock]] elements they referred to as \"core-rock\".<ref>Falling Up - Christian Music Today</ref> Later on, Falling Up moved more in the direction of melodic rock, and experimented with [[electronic music|electronic and synthetic music]], which gradually morphed into an overall [[experimental rock]] sound. Currently, Falling Up describes their style as experimental rock, [[Ambient pop]]<ref>{{cite web|author=US |url=http://www.myspace.com/fallingup |title=Falling Up &#124; Gratis muziek, tourneedata, foto's, video's |publisher=Myspace.com |date= |accessdate=November 17, 2011}}</ref> and [[Indie rock]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.facebook.com/fallingup |title=Falling Up |publisher=Facebook |date=June 28, 2011 |accessdate=November 17, 2011}}</ref>  As of 2015, lead singer Jessy Ribordy, bassist Jeremy Miller and drummer Josh Shroy are the only three original members of the band."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"7371422":{"pageid":7371422,"ns":0,"title":"Falling You","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Falling You\n| image                 = \n| caption            = \n| image_size            = \n| background          = group_or_band\n| alias               = \n| origin              = [[San Francisco, California]]\n| genre               = [[Ambient music|ambient]]\n| years_active        = 1998 - Present\n| label               = [[Fossil Dungeon]]<br/>[[Magnatune]]\n| associated_acts     = \n| website                 = [http://www.fallingyou.com/ www.fallingyou.com]\n| current_members     = John Zorro Zorko\n| past_members        = \n| notable_instruments = \n}}\n\n'''Falling You''' is an [[Ambient music|ambient]]/electronic project based in [[San Francisco, California]]. Falling You's instrumental work tends toward dark ambient soundscapes which borders on electronica. Other tracks utilize ethereal female vocals. John Michael Zorko is the primary composer for Falling You. Notable vocalists include Dru Allen ([[This Ascension]]/[[Mirabilis (band)|Mirabilis]]), Aimee Page, Jennifer McPeak, [[Sara Ayers]], Krista Tortora (Full Blown Kirk), Victoria Lloyd ([[Claire Voyant (band)|Claire Voyant]]), Suzanne Perry ([[Love Spirals Downwards]]), Amanda Kramer ([[Golden Palominos]]), Shikhee ([[Android Lust]]) and Erica Mulkey (Unwoman). The band's debut CD, ''Mercy'', in 1998 featured vocals by Jennifer McPeak exclusively. ''Touch'', ''Human'', ''Faith'', ''Adore'', and the most recent release, ''Blush'', feature vocals by a variety of female artists. As a general rule the lyrics to the songs are written by the vocalist, working in collaboration with Zorko to make a fit for his composition.\n\nThe work of Falling You tends to center, thematically, on some core part of the human condition.\n\nZorko's music has also been featured in documentaries and television commercials.\n\nTouring is difficult for the band because of the logistics of so many From 1971 to 1987 he was a member of the electronic group [[Tangerine Dream]]. Initially a drummer with The Agitation, later renamed [[Agitation Free]], his primary focus eventually shifted to keyboards and synthesizers as the group moved away from its [[psychedelic rock]] origins. While he was not the first musician to use an [[analog sequencer]], he was probably the first to turn it into a live performance instrument, thus laying the rhythmic foundation for classic [[Tangerine Dream]] pieces and indeed for the whole [[Berlin School of electronic music|Berlin school]] sound.\n\nAfter his departure from the group, he founded the [[Sonic Images]] record label, a [[New Age music]] label called [[Earthtone]] and the [[Berlin Symphonic Film Orchestra]], and produced a number of solo music works. After leaving Tangerine Dream, his only live concert was on 9 October 1991 at the Astoria Theatre in London. He performed on stage with [http://DingDingMusic.com Edgar Rothermich] (aka Richard E. Roth) who is also his producer and engineer on all his solo projects and film music after 1990.\n\nFranke moved to Los Angeles in 1991 to pursue film work. In 1995 he scored the [[AFI Conservatory|AFI]] short, ''[[Requiem (1995 film)|Requiem]]''. He may be best known for composing the music for the science fiction television series ''[[Babylon 5]]'', as well as the score of the [[anime]] movie ''[[Tenchi Muyo! in Love]]'' and in 2005 the music for German musical ''[[Ludwig\u00b2]]'' (with [[Konstantin Wecker]])."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"4071203":{"pageid":4071203,"ns":0,"title":"Freescha","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist  <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = Freescha\n| image                 = <!-- Image with unknown copyright status removed: [[image:Freescha2.jpg|300px|Freescha]] -->\n| caption            = <!-- From Freescha's MySpace Website -->\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[San Fernando Valley]], California, USA\n| genre               = [[Intelligent dance music|IDM]]\n| years_active        = 1999 &ndash; \n| label               = [[AttackNine Records|AttackNine]]\n| website                 = http://www.attacknine.com/\n| current_members     = currently regrowing members\n}}'''Freescha''' is the musical collaboration of '''Nick Huntington''' and '''Michael McGroarty''', based in the [[San Fernando Valley]], [[California]]. [[progressive rock]] band [[King Crimson]], Fripp has been the only member to have played in all of King Crimson's line-ups from the late 1960s to the early 2010s. He has also worked extensively as a [[studio musician]], notably with singer [[David Bowie]] on the albums ''[[\"Heroes\"]]'' and ''[[Scary Monsters]]'', and contributed sounds to the [[Windows Vista]] [[operating system]]. musical artist\n| name                = John Frusciante\n| image               = JohnFruscianteAugust2006.jpg\n| caption             = John Frusciante in 2006\n| background          = solo_singer\n| birth_name          = John Anthony Frusciante\n| alias               = Trickfinger\n| birth_date          = {{Birth date and age|mf=yes|1970|03|05}}\n| birth_place         = [[Queens]], [[New York
