[[Swahili Blonde|Kimono Kult]], [[Fugazi]], [[Duran Duran]]\n| website             = {{URL|http://www.johnfrusciante.com/}}\n| notable_instruments = {{unbulleted list|1962 [[Fender Stratocaster]]|1963 [[Fender Telecaster]]|1955 [[Gretsch White Falcon]]|1962 [[Fender Jaguar]]|1969 [[Gibson Les Paul Custom]]|Yamaha SG}}\n}}\n\n'''John Anthony Frusciante''' ({{IPAc-en|audio=Frusciante.ogg|f|r|u\u02d0|\u02c8|\u0283|\u0251\u02d0|n|t|i}}; born March 5, 1970) is an American guitarist, singer, producer and composer. He is best known as the former guitarist of the [[Rock music|rock]] band [[Red Hot Chili Peppers]], from 1988 until 1992, and again from 1998 until 2009. He recorded five studio albums with them.\n\nFrusciante has an active solo career, having released eleven solo albums and five EPs; his recordings include elements ranging from [[experimental rock]] and [[ambient music]] to [[New wave music|new wave]] and [[electronica]]. In 2015, Frusciante will release his debut [[acid house]] album under his alias, [[Trickfinger]]. He has also recorded with numerous other artists, including [[The Mars Volta]], for whom he was a studio guitarist (and occasional live performer) from 2002 until 2008; [[Josh Klinghoffer]] and [[Joe Lally]], with whom he released two albums as [[Ataxia (band)|Ataxia]]; and various collaborations with both Klinghoffer and [[Omar Rodr\u00edguez-L\u00f3pez]].\n\nAt the age of eighteen, he joined the Red Hot Chili Peppers, first appearing on the band's 1989 album, ''[[Mother's Milk]]''. The group's follow-up album, ''[[Blood Sugar Sex Magik]]'' (1991), was a breakthrough success. Frusciante became overwhelmed by the band's new popularity and quit in 1992. He became a recluse and entered a long period of drug addiction, during which he released his first solo recordings: ''[[Niandra Lades and Usually Just a T-Shirt]]'' (1994) and ''[[Smile from the Streets You Hold]]'' (1997). In 1998, he successfully completed drug rehabilitation and rejoined the Red Hot Chili Peppers.  Their next album, ''[[Californication (album)|Californication]]'' (1999) would eventually go on to sell 16 million copies.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://webcache.googleusercontent.com/search?q=cache:wINBkbq55DIJ:prince.org/msg/8/304825+Billboard+Magazine:+300+Best+Selling+Albums+(Worldwide)+green+day&cd=1&hl=es&ct=clnk&gl=pe|title=Billboard Magazine: 300 Best Selling Albums (Worldwide)|accessdate=December 9, 2011|publisher=Prince.org (Google Web Cache)}}</ref> His album ''[[To Record Only Water for Ten Days]]'' was made in 2001. A fourth album with the Chili Peppers, ''[[By the Way]]'' was released in 2002. On a creative spree, Frusciante released six solo albums in 2004; each album explored different recording techniques and genres. 2006 saw the release of his fifth and final album with the Chili Peppers, ''[[Stadium Arcadium]]''. In 2009, Frusciante released ''[[The Empyrean]]'', which features [[Flea (musician)|Flea]] and Josh Klinghoffer, and announced he had again parted ways with the Chili Peppers.\n\nHe has produced and/or recorded with the [[Wu-Tang Clan]], [[The Mars Volta]] and Omar Rodriguez Lopez, [[Swahili Blonde]], [[Black Knights (rap group)|Black Knights]], [[The Bicycle Thief (band)|The Bicycle Thief]], [[Glenn Hughes]], [[Ziggy Marley]], [[Johnny Cash]], [[George Clinton (funk musician)|George Clinton]], and others.\n\nFrusciante has received critical recognition for his guitar playing, ranking at number 18 on ''[[Rolling Stone]]''{{'}}s list of \"The 100 Greatest Guitarists of All Time\" in 2003;<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.rollingstone.com/music/lists/100-greatest-guitarists-of-all-time-19691231/john-frusciante-19691231 |title=18 John Frusciante |publisher=Rolling Stone |accessdate=June 4, 2011}}</ref> and again in a second list published in 2011, where he ranked at number 72.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.rollingstone.com/music/lists/100-greatest-guitarists-20111123/john-frusciante-19691231|title=72 John Frusciante |publisher=Rolling Stone |accessdate=November 24, 2011}}</ref> He was ranked as number 42 in [[Gibson Guitar Corporation|Gibson]]'s list of the \"50 Best Guitarists of All Time\". He was voted \"The Best Guitarist of the Last 30 Years\" in a 2010 BBC poll called \"The Axe Factor\".<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/6music/news/20100409_axefactor.shtml |title=6Music News \u2013 Chilis star wins Axe Factor |publisher=BBC |date=2010-04-30 |accessdate=2010-09-17}}</ref> Frusciante was inducted into the [[Rock and Roll Hall of Fame]] as a member of the Red Hot Chili Peppers on April 14, 2012 although he did not attend the ceremony."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"5715557":{"pageid":5715557,"ns":0,"title":"Future Sound of English singer-songwriter, musician and humanitarian activist who rose to fame as the lead vocalist and [[flautist]] of the [[progressive rock]] band [[Genesis (band)|Genesis]].<ref>[http://www.petergabriel.com/features/Peter_Gabriel_Biography/] {{dead link|date=September 2014}}</ref> After leaving Genesis, Gabriel went on to a successful solo career, with \"[[Solsbury Hill (song)|Solsbury Hill]]\" his first single. His 1986 album, ''[[So (album)|So]]'', is his most commercially successful, and is certified triple platinum in the UK and five times platinum in the U.S.<ref name=\"BPI\"/><ref name=\"RIAA\"/> The album's biggest hit, \"[[Sledgehammer (Peter Gabriel song)|Sledgehammer]]\", won a record nine [[MTV Video Music Award|MTV Awards]] at the [[1987 MTV Video Music Awards]], and it remains the most played music video in the history of MTV.<ref name=\"Time\"/>\n\nGabriel has been a champion of [[world music]] for much of his career. He co-founded the [[World of Music, Arts and Dance|WOMAD]] festival in 1982.<ref name=\"Lynskey 2007\">{{cite news | url= http://www.theguardian.com/music/2012/jul/26/peter-gabriel-30-years-womad | title= Peter Gabriel on 30 years of WOMAD \u2013 and mixing music with politics | publisher=The Guardian | date=26 July 2012 | accessdate=25 February 2014}}</ref> He has continued to focus on producing and promoting world music through his [[Real World Records]] label. He has also pioneered digital distribution methods for music, co-founding [[OD2]], one of the first online music download services.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://edition.cnn.com/2004/TECH/07/20/peter.gabriel/|title=Peter Gabriel on the digital revolution | publisher=CNN|date=22 July 2004|accessdate=25 February 2014}}</ref> Gabriel has been involved in numerous humanitarian efforts. In 1980, he released the anti-[[apartheid]] single \"[[Biko (song)|Biko]]\".<ref name=\"Lynskey 2007\"/> He has participated in several human rights benefit concerts, including [[Amnesty International]]'s ''[[Human Rights Now!]]'' tour in 1988, and co-founded the [[Witness (human rights group)|WITNESS]] human rights organisation in 1992.<ref name=\"Lynskey 2007\"/> Gabriel developed [[The Elders (organization)|The Elders]] with [[Richard Branson]], which was launched by [[Nelson Mandela]] in 2007.<ref>{{cite news | url= http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/1557921/Nelson-Mandela-launches-Elders-to-save-world.html | title= Nelson Mandela launches Elders to save world | publisher=Telegraph Online | date=19 July 2007 | accessdate=19 March 2014}}</ref>\n\nGabriel has won three [[Brit Awards]]\u2014winning Best British Male in 1987,<ref name=\"BritAwards\"/> six [[Grammy Award]]s,<ref>{{cite first Pioneer Award at the [[BT Digital Music Awards]],<ref>{{cite news | url= http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/entertainment/5405450.stm | title= Lily Allen wins web music award | work=BBC News | date=4 October 2006 | accessdate=23 June 2013}}</ref> the ''[[Q (magazine)|Q]]'' magazine Lifetime Achievement,<ref>{{cite news | url= work=BBC News | date=24 May 2007 | accessdate=6 March 2015}}</ref> and the [[Polar Music Prize]].<ref>{{cite news|url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/entertainment/8045524.stm|title=Gabriel shares Polar 2015}}</ref> and ''[[Time (magazine)|TIME]]'' magazine named Gabriel one of the 100 most influential people in the world.<ref>{{cite He is considered one of the most influential music makers of the late 20th century.<ref>Naxos Classical Music Spotlight podcast: Philip Glass Heroes Symphony</ref><ref>{{citation |periodical=[[New York Magazine]] |url=http://nymag.com/news/features/influentials/16903/ |title=The Most Influential People in Classical and Dance |date=May 8, 2006 |accessdate=November 10, 2008 |postscript=<!--none--> }}</ref><ref>{{citation |title=The Guardian Profile: Philip Glass |url=http://www.guardian.co.uk/Archive/Article/0,4273,4306156,00.html |date=November 24, 2001 |first=John |last=O'Mahony |accessdate=November 10, 2008 |periodical=[[The Guardian]] |postscript=<!--none--> |location=London}}</ref> His music is also often controversially described as ''[[minimal music]]'', along with the work of the other \"major minimalists\" [[La Monte Young]], [[Terry Riley]] and [[Steve Reich]].<ref>Richardson, John (1999), ''Singing Archaeology: Philip Glass's Akhnaten'', University Press of New England, p. 21</ref>\n\nGlass has distanced himself from the \"minimalist\" label, describing himself instead as a composer of \"music with repetitive structures\".<ref name=bio>{{citation |url=http://www.philipglass.com/bio.php |periodical=PhilipGlass.com |title=Biography |accessdate=November 10, 2008 |postscript=<!--none--> }}</ref> Though his early mature music shares much with what is normally called \"minimalist\", he has since evolved stylistically.<ref>{{citation |url=http://nymag.com/nymetro/arts/music/pop/reviews/485/ |title=Is Glass Half Empty? |periodical=[[New York Magazine]] |first=Ethan |last=Smith |accessdate=November 10, 2008 |postscript=<!--none--> }}</ref><ref name=appomattox>{{citation |url=http://www.nytimes.com/2007/09/23/arts/music/23smit.html |periodical=[[The New York Times]] |title=If Grant Had Been Singing at Appomattox |date=September 23, 2007 |first=Steve |last=Smith |postscript=<!--none--> }}</ref> Currently, he describes himself as a \"classicist\", pointing out that he is trained in [[harmony]] and [[counterpoint]] and studied such composers as [[Franz Schubert]], [[Johann Sebastian Bach]] and [[Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart]] with [[Nadia Boulanger]].<ref>{{citation|title=The Sound of Glass|first=Belinda|last=McKoen|periodical=[[The Irish Times]]|date=June 28, 2008|accessdate=November 10, 2008|url=http://www.irishtimes.com/newspaper/weekend/2008/0628/1214567621837.html|postscript=<!--none--> }} {{Subscription required}}</ref>\n\nGlass is a prolific composer: he has written works for the musical group which he founded, the [[Philip Glass Ensemble]] (with which he still performs on keyboards), as well as operas, musical theatre works, ten [[symphony|symphonies]], eleven concertos, solo works, chamber music including [[string quartet]]s and instrumental sonatas, and [[film score]]s. Three of his film scores have been nominated for [[Academy Award]]s."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"3163822":{"pageid":3163822,"ns":0,"title":"Global Communication","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{about|the electronic music group|the general topic of global communication|International communication}}\n{{Refimprove|date=January 2010}}\n{{Infobox musical artist<!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = Global Communication\n| image               = \n| caption             =  \n| image_size          = \n| alias               = Chameleon, Jedi Knights, Link & E621, Reload, Secret Ingredients\n| background          = group_or_band\n| genre               = {{flatlist|\n* [[Ambient music|Ambient]]\n* [[Industrial music|industrial]]\n* [[electronica]]\n* [[deep house]]\n* [[downtempo]]\n}}\n| origin              = [[Yeovil]],  [[England]]\n| years_active        = 1992\u2013present\n| label               = Dedicated / Evolution / Universal Language Productions Ltd.\n| associated_acts     = \n| current_members     = [[Mark Pritchard (music producer)|Mark Pritchard]]<br />[[Tom Middleton]] \n| website             = \n}}\n\n'''Global Communication''' is an [[electronic music]] act, comprising [[Tom Middleton]] and [[Mark Pritchard (music producer)|Mark Pritchard]]. Their first LP, ''[[76:14]]'', is an acclaimed album from the ambient and 1990s electronic music genres.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.guardian.co.uk/music/2007/nov/19/1000tohearbeforeyoudie4 |title=Artists beginning with G &#124; Music &#124; guardian.co.uk |publisher=Guardian |date= 3 December 2007|accessdate=9 April 2012 |location=London}}</ref> Beyond their work as Global Communication, they have also recorded as [[Jedi Knights (band)|Jedi Knights]], Secret Ingredients, The Chameleon, Link & E621 and [[Mark Pritchard (music producer)|Reload]]; have done remixes for various artists under each of their aliases, including a 1993 Reload remix of \"On\" by [[Aphex Twin]] and a 1997 [[Jedi Knights (band)|Jedi Knights]] remix of \"Home\" by [[Depeche Mode]]. They founded the [[Evolution Records]] and Universal Language Productions labels.\n\nPritchard has also recorded solo as [[Reload (band)|Reload]], Link, Harmonic 313, Troubleman, NY Connection, [[William Parrott]] and Roberto Edwardo Turner (The Returner). His other collaborative efforts include Harmonic 33 and [[Use of Weapons]] with Dave Brinkworth, Series 7 with Stephen Horne, [[Shaft (rave)|Shaft]] with Adrian Hughes, Vertigo with [[Danny Breaks]], The 28 East Boyz with Kevin Hann, Chaos & Julia Set with Dominic Fripp, Mystic Institute with Paul Kent, Pulusha with [[Kirsty Hawkshaw]] and [[Africa Hitech|Africa HiTech]] with [[Steve Spacek]].\n\nMiddleton has also recorded as Cosmos, AMBA, The Modwheel, The Rebus Project, Schizophrenia, E621 and Spiritcatcher. He has worked collaboratively with [[Matthew Herbert]] and Mark Darby of [[Mighty Force Records]], releasing an eponymous EP as Fog City. As Schizophrenia, Middleton collaborated with [[Aphex Twin]] on a track on the ''[[Analogue Bubblebath]]'' EP. He is currently{{when|date=March 2014}} releasing records under his own name, and has released some DJ mix compilations."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"681318":{"pageid":681318,"ns":0,"title":"Global Goon","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n|name            = Global Goon\n|image           =\n|caption         = \n|image_size      = \n|background      = solo_singer\n|birth_name      = Jonne Hawke\n|alias           = \n| birth_date     = 1967\n|death_date      = \n|origin          = [[Merseyside]], [[United Kingdom|UK]]\n|genre           = [[Electronic music]]\n|occupation      = \n|years_active    = 1988\u2013present\n|label           = [[Rephlex]], [[Audio Dregs]], [[J-HOK]], [[W\u00e9M\u00e8]]\n|associated_acts = \n}}\n\n'''Global Goon''''s Jonathan Hawk is a former programmer from [[Lydiate]] who earned a recording contract with Rephlex Records<ref>{{cite news| last =| first =| title =And the rest, New releases, Compilations and reissues| page =68| publisher =''[[The Observer]]''| date =2003-11-16}}</ref> before moving to London and being Richard D. James' (aka [[Aphex Twin]])'s housemate. He had been making electronic music using SoundEdit 16 while supporting himself with various programming jobs. After moving into a shared house with James, [[Squarepusher|Tom Jenkinson]], [[Cylob|Chris Jeffs]] and [[Grant Wilson-Claridge]], he released his first album ''[[Goon (album)|Goon]]'' on [[Rephlex]] in 1996. Rumors that Goon actually was an alias for Aphex Twin persisted even after the release of ''[[Cradle of History]]'' two years later. After releasing [[Vatican Nitez]] four years later, he left the [[Rephlex]] label and started his own label [[J-HOK records]], which he released 3 albums on.<ref>J-HOK Discography http://www.discogs.com/label/J-HOK+records</ref> He also released one album on [[Audio Dregs]], and two albums and one [[Extended play|EP]] on [[W\u00e9M\u00e8]].<ref>W\u00e9M\u00e8 Discography http://www.discogs.com/label/W%C3%A9M%C3%A8+Records</ref>\nGlobal Goon has also been rumored to have released 5 acid records under the alias '''Syntheme''' on both [[Planet Mu]] and [[W\u00e9M\u00e8]] between 2007 & 2009, but this remains unconfirmed and Syntheme is also known as Louise Helena Wood, from Brighton, UK. <ref>http://www.planet.mu/discography/ZIQ213</ref>\n\nMusic critics have characterized Global Goon's style as [[ambient music]] and \"easy listening [[fusion (music)|fusion]]\".<ref>{{cite news| last =Pride| first =Dominic| title =London| page =45| publisher =''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]''| date =1997-03-22}}</ref> From [[Bessemer Cocktail]] and after, his music took a turn towards [[acid house]] rather than the easy listening [[downtempo]]."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"8865562":{"pageid":8865562,"ns":0,"title":"God Is An Astronaut","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#REDIRECT [[God Is an Astronaut]] {{R from other capitalization}}"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"158471":{"pageid":158471,"ns":0,"title":"Godspeed You! Black Emperor''' is a [[Canadian]] [[post-rock]] band which originated in [[Montreal]], [[Quebec]] in 1994. They release their recordings through [[Constellation Records (Canada)|Constellation]], an [[independent record label]] also located in Montreal.\n\nAfter the release of their [[F\u266fA\u266f\u221e|debut album]] in 1997, the group toured regularly from 1998 to 2002. In 2003, the band announced an indefinite hiatus in order for band members to pursue other musical interests. In the intervening period, the group was occasionally rumored to have broken up,<ref name=\"nmemis\">{{cite web|url=http://www.nme.com/news/godspeed-you-black-emperor/34219|title=Godspeed You! Black Emperor quit over Iraq|accessdate=2008-02-17|publisher=NME|year=2008}}</ref><ref name=\"pitchforkhiatus\">{{cite web|url=http://www.pitchforkmedia.com/article/news/48600-godspeed-still-on-hiatus-not-completely-broken-up|archiveurl=http://web.archive.org/web/20080212174307/http://www.pitchforkmedia.com/article/news/48600-godspeed-still-on-hiatus-not-completely-broken-up|title=Godspeed Still on Hiatus, Not Completely Broken Up|date=2008-02-11|archivedate=2008-02-12|accessdate=2009-10-08|publisher=[[Pitchfork Media]]|last=Phillips|first=Amy}}</ref> but the band finally reconvened for a tour beginning in late 2010. In October 2012, the band released their fourth album, ''[['Allelujah! Don't Bend! Ascend!]]''. In March 2015, they released their fifth album, ''[['Asunder, Sweet and Other Distress']]''.\n\nEven though the band has never broken into the mainstream, they have gained an extremely dedicated [[cult following]], and remain very influential in the [[post-rock]] genre.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://thekey.xpn.org/2013/09/16/just-announced-post-rock-cult-faves-godspeed-you-black-emperor-headlining-union-transfer/ |title=Just Announced: Post-rock cult faves Godspeed You! Gerber regularly DJs across the globe at events in Detroit, Berlin, Ibiza, Miami, and the UK.<ref>IMO Records. http://www.imorecords.co.uk/house-2/house-artists/guy-gerber-biography/  \"Guy Gerber Biography\"], [[IMO Records]] Retrieved on 1 March 2011.</ref>\n\nAt the age of 15, Gerber was a member of the Israeli Under-16 national football team but soon developed a passion for music and found himself drawn to English guitar acts like [[Joy Division]] and Irish guitar acts like [[My Bloody Valentine (band)|My Bloody Valentine]]. Consequently, his harmonic, shoe-gaze inspired sound was a style that saw Gerber record for various European electronic labels including \u2018Stoppage Time\u2019 for [[John Digweed]]\u2019s Bedrock imprint.\n\nGerber\u2019s first full length album \u2018Late Bloomers\u2019 was released on [[Sven V\u00e4th]]\u2019s Cocoon imprint in June 2007 and featured two worldwide club hits in \u2018Belly Dancing\u2019 and \u2018Sea Of Sand\u2019 which he recorded with his Israeli production friend Shlomi Aber. In addition to his productions, Guy also found time to remix [[New Order]] and [[Dominik Eulberg]] as well as setting up his own label Supplement Facts. More recently, he\u2019s remixed \u2018The L Word\u2019 by Deniz Kurtel and \u2018Hungry For The Power\u2019 by [[Azari & III]].\n\nNow living in Madrid, Supplement Facts has just celebrated its 5th anniversary with the compilation album \u2018Heartbeats\u2019. As well as releasing Gerber\u2019s own productions like \u2018Disorientation\u2019, Supplement Facts is also home to exclusive music by Lee Curtiss, David K, Michel Cleis and Varoslav feat dOP.\n\nIn {{Nihongo||\u5e2b\u5320|\"Shish\u014d\"}}) is a Japanese music artist and composer.\n\nIn 1965, he started playing guitar, inspired by [[The Ventures]], and joined a band with \"older people\" the following year. In 1972, he enrolled at [[Tokyo Designer Gakuin College]]. From 1972 to 1978, he performed in his first band Mandrake, a progressive rock band influenced by [[King Crimson]], [[Yes (band)|Yes]], [[Black Sabbath]] and [[Pink Floyd]]. In 1979 he formed a [[experimental rock|experimental]]/[[electronic rock]] band called [[P-Model]], along with two former members of Mandrake and a fan of the band/close friend. They released a string of albums through the 1980s, and in 1989, Hirasawa began releasing solo work, while also continuing to work with the reactivated P-MODEL beginning in 1992. The P-MODEL project continued until 2000; in 2004 Hirasawa started a new unit known as KAKU P-MODEL, which is effectively a solo continuation of P-MODEL.<ref name=\"ANS\">Morgan, Jonah. \"[http://www.animenewsservice.com/archives/hirasawa.htm ANS Exclusive Interview: Berserk Soundtrack Composer Susumu Hirasawa]\". His compositional style is characterized by [[polymodality|polymodal]] architectonics, [[microtonality|polymictrotonality]] and the usage of [[Digital data|digital]] technique to enhance sonic means of expression,<ref>Blanick\u00fd J., Auster M.: [http://www.vladimirhirsch.com/e_biography.html Vladim\u00edr Hirsch biography]</ref> where modern classical elements fuse within  [[experimental music|experimental]] [[soundscape]]s. Originally writing for movies and television, he later moved into composing for video games. He has been described as being \"internationally recognized as one of the A-list orchestral composers in the video games industry\".<ref name=\"M4GLineageint\"/> During his career to date, Zur has composed the music to over 50 video games, 15 television shows, and 10 movies, as well as many movie trailers. His style could be described as [[ambient music|ambient]] with a heavy [[minimalist music|minimalist]] influence. = [http://www.irisarri.org/ irisarri.org]\n| associated_acts     = [[The Sight Below]]<br>[[Biosphere (musician)|Biosphere]]<br>[[Benoit Pioulard]]<br>[[Orcas (duo)|ORCAS]]<br>[[Simon Scott [[United States of America|American]] composer, [[multi-instrumentalist]], [[Record producer|producer]] and media artist based in [[Seattle, Washington]]. He is predominantly associated with [[Minimalist music|post-minimalist]], [[drone music|drone]] and [[ambient music|electronic]] music, exploring textural aesthetics for over half a decade. His [[Klangfarbenmelodie|pointillist]] compositions lean towards [[ostinato]] motifs that tap into [[minimalist]] ideals while his studio production style is characterized by dense layers of [[reverb]] and [[Delay (audio effect)|delay]], suggesting a blurred cinematic quality, like half-remembered dreams full of elegiac beauty. [[Bowed guitar]] textures, deep pulsing bass tones, field recordings, submerged piano notes, melancholic strings and subtle electronic counterpoints all contribute and converge equally in his music to create an oceanic experience that contrasts the epic and subdued, ''\"like an ambient symphony recording that\u2019s been rescued from attic entombment after half a century.\u201d''<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.textura.org/reviews/irisarri_reverie.htm |title=textura |publisher=textura |date= |accessdate=2014-02-28}}</ref>\n\nHis compositions were once described by [[The Wire (magazine)|The Wire]] contributing writer Jefferson Petrey as \"''a dual perspective close-up focus on the micro textures of rustling static-filled sonic surfaces with the wide-open distant tree lined horizons of sunset at dusk''.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://americantypewriter.net/irisarri.html |title=Artists - Rafael Anton Irisarri |publisher=American Typewriter |date= |accessdate=2014-01-08}}</ref>  [[Popmatters]] depicted his music as ''\u201csensual, propulsive, and shrouded in mercurial darkness\u201d''<ref>{{cite web|last=Newmark |first=Mike |url=http://www.popmatters.com/pm/review/131718-the-sight-below-it-all-falls-apart/ |title=The Sight Below: It All Falls Apart |publisher=PopMatters |date= |accessdate=2014-01-08}}</ref> while [[Drowned In Sound]] chronicled ''\u201chis ear for a soul-crushing melody continues to shine through the album\u2019s dense caverns of reverb.\u201d'' Chris Brosman from online tastemaker [[Pitchfork Media]] referred to his production work as ''\u201ca beautifully bleak cloud of sound\u201d''.,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://pitchfork.com/forkcast/13979-new-dawn-fades-joy-division-cover-ft-tiny-vipers/ |title=\"New Dawn Fades\" [Joy Division cover; ft. Tiny Vipers&#93; &#124; Forkcast Archive |publisher=Pitchfork |date=2010-03-02 |accessdate=2014-01-08}}</ref> while music journalist Patric Fallon praised his compositions as ''\"dense, panoramic soundscapes.\"''<ref>{{cite web|last=Fallon |first=Patric |url=http://blogs.sfweekly.com/shookdown/2010/09/thats_my_jam_the_sight_belows.php |title=That's My Jam!: The Sight Below's Blurry Soundscapes |publisher=Blogs.sfweekly.com |date=2010-09-08 |accessdate=2014-01-08}}</ref>\n\nIrisarri is also known as the main member of [[electronic music]]/[[shoegaze]] act [[The Sight Below]], and signed to American label [[Ghostly International]]."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"3157572":{"pageid":3157572,"ns":0,"title":"Ishq","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{About|the word Ishq|other uses}}\n{{Refimprove|date=June 2013}}\n'''{{transl|sem|\u02bbIshq}}''' is an Arabic word used in Arabic as well as many other languages. ({{lang-ar|\u0639\u0634\u0642}}; in [[Somali language |Somali]]: '''caashaq''' or ('''cishqi''') in [[Persian language|Persian]]: '''eshgh'''; in {{lang-ur|}} '''ishq'''; in [[Dari]]: '''eshq'''; in [[Pashto language|Pashto]]: '''eshq'''; in [[Turkish language|Turkish]]: '''a\u015fk''' and in [[Azerbaijani language|Azerbaijani]]: '''e\u015fq'''), means \"love\".<ref>M. Heydari-Malayeri [http://aramis.obspm.fr/~heydari/dictionary/esq_eng.html On the origin of the word e\u0161q ]</ref> The word is derived from ''\u2018ashiqah'', a [[vine]]: the common belief is that when love takes its root in the heart of a lover, everything other than God is effaced.<ref>[http://www.nfie.com/mirza.html Din al-Muhabbat]</ref> In Islam's [[Sufi]] and mystic doctrine it is a concept which refers to \"divine love\" or \"a creature's love for its creator\"; i.e. [[Human|man]]'s love for [[God]]."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1201811":{"pageid":1201811,"ns":0,"title":"Ishvara","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{EngvarB|date=April 2015}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=April 2015}}\n{{Hinduism}}\n\n'''Ishvara''' ([[Sanskrit]]: \u0908\u0936\u094d\u0935\u0930, ''{{IAST|\u012a\u015bvara}}'') is a concept in [[Hinduism]], with a wide range of meanings that depends of the era and the school of Hinduism.<ref name=mmwizvara/><ref name=riepe/> In ancient texts of Indian philosophy, ''Ishvara'' means supreme soul, [[Brahman]] (Highest Reality), ruler, king or husband depending on the context.<ref name=mmwizvara/> In medieval era texts, ''Ishvara'' means God, Supreme Being, personal god, or special Self depending on the school of Hinduism.<ref name=riepe/><ref name=ianw/><ref name=mirceaelaide73/>\n\nIn [[Shaivism]], ''Ishvara'' is synonymous with \"[[Shiva]]\", as the \"Supreme lord over other Gods\" in the [[Hinduism|pluralistic sense]], or as an [[Ishta-deva]] in [[religious pluralism|pluralistic]] thought. In [[Vaishnavism]], it is synonymous with [[Vishnu]].<ref name=olilea/> In traditional [[Bhakti]] movements, Ishvara is one or more deities of an individual's preference from Hinduism's polytheistic canon of deities. In modern sectarian movements such as [[Arya Samaj]] and [[Brahmoism]], Ishvara takes the form of a monotheistic God.<ref name=rkpr/> In [[Raja yoga|Yoga]] school of Hinduism, it is any \"personal deity\" or \"spiritual inspiration\".<ref name=lpfl/> In [[Advaita Vedanta]] school, Ishvara is a monistic Universal Absolute that connects and is the Oneness in everyone and everything.<ref name=lance/><ref name=jkoller/>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"22915363":{"pageid":22915363,"ns":0,"title":"Jacaszek","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox Jarre","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use dmy dates|date=August 2013}}\n{{Good article}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name = Jean Michel Jarre\n| image = Jean Michel Jarre 2008.jpg\n| caption = Jarre in Milan, 2008\n| background = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_date = {{birth date and age|df=yes|1948|8|24}}\n| origin = [[Lyon]], France\n| instrument = Synthesizer, piano, [[Electronic organ|organ]], [[laser harp]], [[accordion]], guitar, bass guitar\n| genre = [[Ambient music|Ambient]], [[New-age music|new-age]], [[electronic music|electronic]], [[Trance music|trance]], [[progressive rock]]\n| occupation = Composer, musician, artist, producer\n| years_active = 1972\u2013present\n| label = [[Disques Dreyfus]]/[[BMG Rights Management]]/[[Sony Music|Sony]], [[Polydor Records|Polydor]]/[[PolyGram]], [[Epic Records|Epic]]/[[Sony Music Entertainment|SME]], [[Warner Bros. Records|Warner Bros.]], [[EMI]]\n| website = {{URL|www.jeanmicheljarre.com}}\n}}\n'''Jean Michel Jarre''' (born '''Jean-Michel Andr\u00e9 Jarre'''; 24 August 1948) is a French composer, [[Performing arts|performer]], and music producer. He is a pioneer in the [[electronic music|electronic]], [[ambient music|ambient]], and [[New-age music|new-age]] genres, and known as an organiser of outdoor [[spectacle]]s of his music featuring lights, [[laser lighting display|laser displays]], and [[fireworks]].\n\nJarre was raised in Lyon by his mother and grandparents, and trained on the piano. From an early age he was introduced to a variety of art forms, including those of street performers, [[jazz]] musicians, and the artist [[Pierre Soulages]]. He played guitar in a band, but his musical style was perhaps most heavily influenced by [[Pierre Schaeffer]], a pioneer of [[musique concr\u00e8te]] at the [[Groupe de Recherches Musicales]].\n\nHis first mainstream success was the 1976 album ''[[Oxyg\u00e8ne]]''. Recorded in a makeshift studio at his home, the album sold an estimated 12&nbsp;million copies. ''Oxyg\u00e8ne'' was followed in 1978 by ''[[Equinoxe|\u00c9quinoxe]]'', and in 1979 Jarre performed to a record-breaking audience of more than a million people at the [[Place de la Concorde]], a record he has since broken three times. More albums were to follow, but his 1979 concert served as a blueprint for his future performances around the world. Several of his albums have been released to coincide with large-scale outdoor events, and he is now perhaps as well known as a performer as well as a musician.\n\nAs of 2004 Jarre had sold an estimated 80&nbsp;million albums. He was the first Western musician officially invited to perform in the [[China|People's Republic of China]], and holds the world record for the largest-ever audience at an outdoor event."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"36678493":{"pageid":36678493,"ns":0,"title":"Job Karma","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{multiple issues|\n{{Orphan|date=February 2013}}\n{{BLP sources|date=August 2012}}\n}}\n\n{{Infobox musical artist\n |name                  = Job Karma\n |background            = group_or_band\n |years_active          = 1997-present \n |origin                = [[Wroc\u0142aw]], [[Poland]]\n |genre                 = [[Industrial music|industrial]], [[Ambient music|ambient]]\n |current_members       = Maciej Frett <br /> Aureliusz Pisarzewski <br /> Arkadiusz Bagi\u0144ski\n |past_members          = Jacek Groszek\n |www                   = http://www.jobkarma.pl}}\n\n'''Job Karma''' is a post-[[Industrial music|industrial]]-[[Ambient music|ambient]] band from [[Wroc\u0142aw]]. It was created in [[1998 in music|1998]] by Maciej Frett (born 1973) and Aureliusz Pisarzewski (born 1974). In the first period (before 1999) Jacek Groszek (born 1973) was also a member of the band.\n\nPerformances of the group have the form of [[audiovisual art]]. Visuals are done by Arkadiusz Bagi\u0144ski (born 1969) \u2013 an artist dealing with drawings, [[performance]]s and [[visual arts]].\n\nJob Karma makes their music using [[sound generator]]s and electric analogue-digital instruments, the band also fits [[trance music|trance]] rhythms, ambient [[Texture (music)|textures]], [[Sampling (music)|samples]], fragments of movie dialogues and archival radio transmissions into it.\n\nThematically the Job Karma's compositions are focused on negative aspects and dangers of modern [[civilization]], addressing social, political and religious issues.\n\nFrom [[2000 in music|2000]] the band realizes the project \u201eRytua\u0142\u201d (Ritual), in which during live performances they join the music and music materials together with sacral and industrial architecture.\n\nFrom [[2011 in music|2001]] Maciej Frett and Arkadiusz Bagi\u0144ski are the organisers of the [[Wroc\u0142aw Industrial Festival]].<ref>[http://industrialart.eu/festival/ Wroclaw Industrial Festival]</ref>\n\nThe musicians have good connections to the band [[In The Nursery]]<ref name=\"Nursery\">{{cite web | url=http://www.inthenursery.com/news.php | title=11.02.11 live concert at Sheffield City Hall Ballroom on 5th May 2011 | publisher=In The Nursery website | date=11.02.2011 | accessdate=November 19, 2012}}</ref> and the [[Sheffield]] based record label Redroom.<ref name=\"Redroom\"/> Their 2005 album ''Strike'' included a cover version of the track ''Radioactivity'' by [[Kraftwerk]] and a ''I'll Watch You Drown'' remix  by Matt Howden of Redroom studios.<ref>{{cite web | url=http://www.discogs.com/Job-Karma-Strike/release/471147 | title=Job Karma \u2013 Strike; Label: Ars Benevola Mater \u2013 ABM11 | publisher=Discogs | accessdate=November 19, 2012}}</ref>\n\nMatt Howden and Job Karma have released a new album in May 2012, ''Anthems Flesh'', under the band name  ''7JK - Sieben Vs. Job Karma''.<ref name=\"Redroom\">{{cite web | url=http://www.discogs.com/7JK-Anthems-Flesh/release/3546805 | title=7JK \u2013 Anthems Flesh | publisher=Discogs | date=25 May 2012 | accessdate=November 19, 2012}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1976839":{"pageid":1976839,"ns":0,"title":"Jonn Serrie","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{For|the American concert accordionist, organist and educator|John Serry, Sr.}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = Jonn Serrie\n| image               = Jonn_Serrie_20110312.jpg\n| caption             =\n| background          = non_performing_personnel\n| birth_name          = \n| birth_date          = \n| death_date          = \n| origin              = [[Atlanta]], Georgia, United States \n| instrument          = \n| genre               = [[Space music]], [[New-age music|new-age]]\n| occupation          = composer\n| years_active        = 1980s\u2013present\n| label               = [[Miramar (record label)|Miramar]], [[New World Music]], [[Valley Entertainment]]\n| associated_acts     = [[Gary Stroutsos]], [[Steve Roach (musician)|Steve Roach]]\n| website             = {{URL|http://www.thousandstar.com}}\n| notable_instruments = \n}}\n'''Jonn Serrie''' is an American composer of [[space music]], a genre of ambient [[electronic music]], and [[New Age]] music. {{URL|bradleyjoseph.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Bradley Joseph''' (born 1965) is an American composer, arranger, and producer of contemporary  instrumental music. His compositions include works for orchestra, quartet, and solo piano, while his musical style ranges from \"quietly pensive mood music to a rich orchestration of classical depth and breadth\".<ref name=\"NaplesDailyNews\"/>\n\nActive since 1983, Joseph has performed in front of more than a half million people around the world.<ref name=\"st.croix\"/>  He played various instruments in rock bands throughout the [[Midwestern United States|Midwest]] until 1989 when [[Greece|Greek]] composer [[Yanni]] hired him for his core band after hearing a tape of his original compositions. He was a featured concert keyboardist with Yanni through six major tours, most recently in 2003 for the 60-city ''[[Ethnicity (Yanni album)|Ethnicity]]'' tour.  He appears in the multi-platinum album and concert film, ''[[Yanni Live at the Acropolis]]''. Joseph also spent four years as [[musical director]] and lead keyboardist for [[Sheena Easton]], including a 1995 performance on ''[[The Tonight Show with Jay Leno]]''.\n\nJoseph is the founder of the Robbins Island Music label.  His solo career began when he independently released ''[[Hear the Masses]],'' featuring many of his Yanni bandmates. This debut was followed by ''[[Rapture (Bradley Joseph album)|Rapture]]'', an instrumental album recorded with a 50-piece orchestra in which Joseph wrote and conducted all of the scores. It was released on the [[Narada Productions|Narada]] label and reached [[Zone Music Reporter|ZMR]] Airwaves Top 30.  A number of subsequent recordings including ''[[Christmas Around the World]]'' and ''[[One Deep Breath]]'' also held positions on ZMR's Top 100 radio chart, with the most recent being ''[[Paint the Sky]]'' which debuted at #15 in April 2013.    ''Paint the Sky'' was nominated for Best Neo-Classical Album in the 10th annual ZMR Music Awards.<ref name=\"ZMR Nom\">{{cite web | url=http://www.zonemusicreporter.com/admin/nominees_site.asp | title=The 10th Annual ZMR Music Award Nominees | publisher=zonemusicreporter.com | accessdate=27 March 2014}}</ref>  He has produced numerous CDs/DVDs and piano books. Educated at Eggars Grammar School, Alton, in Hampshire, he joined the BBC as a tape editor before moving on to become a studio manager for [[BBC Radio 1]]. In 1970 he joined the Radiophonic Workshop where he remained until 1981. His initial work was mostly signature tunes for BBC radio and TV programmes before going on to record incidental music for programmes including ''[[The Changes (TV series)|The Changes]]'', two versions of ''[[The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy]]:'' the [[The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy (radio series)|second radio series]] and the [[The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy (TV series)|TV adaptation]], as well as several serials of ''[[Doctor Who]]''. His work on the latter series included incidental music for the following serials (in order of transmission):\n* ''[[Meglos]]''\n* ''[[Full Circle (Doctor Who)|Full Circle]]''\n* ''[[State of Decay]]''\n* ''[[Logopolis]]''\n* ''[[Castrovalva (Doctor Who)|Castrovalva]]''\n* ''[[The Visitation (Doctor Who)|The Visitation]]''\n* ''[[Mawdryn Undead]]''\n* ''[[Frontios]]''\nOther well-known series which contained music composed by Paddy Kingsland are [[Michael Palin: Around the World in 80 Days|Around the World in 80 Days]] and [[Pole to Pole]], both travel series by [[Michael Palin]]. Paddy Kingsland also composed music for many schools' television series including Words and Pictures, Rat-a-tat-tat, Watch, Numbercrew, Storytime, English Express, Music Makers, [[Hotch Potch House]] and the [[Look and Read]] stories \"Joe and the Sheep Rustlers\" and \"The Boy from Space\". Since leaving the BBC, composed music for the [[KPM Musichouse|KPM]] music library, television, commercials and corporate videos. He also owns his own studio, PK Studios. He is currently composing the music for the CITV series ''[[Blips (TV series)|Blips]]'' produced by [[Ragdoll Productions]].\n\nIn 1973, ''[[Fourth Dimension (Radiophonic album)|Fourth Dimension]]'', a compilation of his early signature tune work for the Radiophonic Workshop, was released and in 2002 his incidental scores for the ''Doctor Who'' serials \"Meglos\" and \"Full Circle\" featured as part of the [[Doctor Who at the BBC Radiophonic Workshop Volume 4: Meglos & Full Circle|Doctor Who at the BBC Radiophonic Workshop]] compilation series. Eight albums of his library music work have been issued by KPM."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"10843865":{"pageid":10843865,"ns":0,"title":"Kitaro","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#REDIRECT [[Kitar\u014d]]{{r from title without diacritics}}"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"4968179":{"pageid":4968179,"ns":0,"title":"The KLF","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Redirect|KLF}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = The KLF\n| image                 = \n| background          = group_or_band\n| alias               = The Justified Ancients of Mu Mu<br />The JAMs<br />The Timelords\n| origin              = London, England\n| genre               = [[House (music)|House]], [[Techno music|techno]], [[acid house]], [[Hip hop music|hip hop]], [[alternative dance]], [[ambient house]], [[Avant-garde music|avant-garde]]<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.digitalinberlin.de/tag/the-klf/ |title=The KLF &#124; |publisher=Digitalinberlin.de |date=2013-12-14 |accessdate=2014-01-21}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.stewarthomesociety.org/klf.htm |title=the (un)real history of the pop avant-garde |publisher=Stewarthomesociety.org |date= |accessdate=2014-01-21}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://inlog.org/2011/05/20/bill-drummond-the-klf-announced-for-debate-and-the17-project-for-incubate-2011/ |title=Incubate Blog \u00bb Blog Archive \u00bb Bill Drummond (The KLF) announced for debate and The17 project for Incubate 2011 |publisher=Inlog.org |date= |accessdate=2014-01-21}}</ref>\n| years_active        = 1987\u20131992 <br><small>(Reunions: 1995 and 1997)</small>\n| label               = [[KLF Communications]], [[Arista Records|Arista]], and other international licensees\n| associated_acts     = [[The K Foundation]], [[Disco 2000]], [[Fuck the Millennium|2K]]\n| past_members        = [[Bill Drummond]]<br />[[Jimmy Cauty]]\n}}\n\n'''The KLF''' (also known as '''The Justified Ancients of Mu Mu''', '''The Timelords''' and other names) were a [[United Kingdom|British]] [[acid house]] band of the late 1980s and early 1990s.<ref>IMO Records. [http://www.imorecords.co.uk/house-2/house-artists/klf-biography/ \"The KLF Biography\"]{{dead link|date=January 2014}}, ''[[IMO Records]]' Retrieved on 29 February 2011.</ref>\n\nBeginning in 1987, [[Bill Drummond]] (alias King Boy D) and [[Jimmy Cauty]] (alias Rockman Rock) released [[hip hop music|hip hop]]-inspired and [[sampling (music)|sample]]-heavy records as '''The Justified Ancients of Mu Mu''', and on one occasion (the British number one hit [[single (music)|single]] \"[[Doctorin' the Tardis]]\") as '''The Timelords'''.  The KLF released a series of international hits on their own KLF Communications record label, and became the biggest-selling singles act in the world for 1991.<ref name=\"AMG\">Bush, J., KLF biography, ''[[Allmusic]]'' ([{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p4694/biography|pure_url=yes}} link])</ref> The duo also published a cynical book, ''[[The Manual|The Manual (How to Have a Number One the Easy Way)]]'', and worked on a road movie called ''[[The White Room (film)|The White Room]]''.\n\nFrom the outset, they adopted the philosophy espoused by esoteric novel series ''[[The Illuminatus! Trilogy]]'', gaining notoriety for various [[anarchism|anarchic]] [[Situationist International|situationist]] manifestations, including the [[vandalism|defacement]] of billboard adverts, the posting of prominent cryptic advertisements in ''[[NME]]'' magazine and the mainstream press, and highly distinctive and unusual performances on ''[[Top of the Pops]]''. Their most notorious performance was a collaboration with [[Extreme Noise Terror]] at the February 1992 [[Brit Awards|BRIT Awards]], where they fired [[machine gun]] [[Blank (cartridge)|blanks]] into the audience and dumped a dead sheep at the aftershow party. This performance announced The KLF's departure from the music business, and in May 1992 the duo [[Deletion (music industry)|deleted]] their entire back catalogue.\n\nWith The KLF's profits, Drummond and Cauty established the [[K Foundation]] and sought to subvert the [[art world]], staging an [[K Foundation art award|alternative art award]] for the worst artist of the year and [[K Foundation Burn a Million Quid|burning one million pounds sterling]]. Drummond and Cauty remained true to their word of May 1992; the KLF Communications catalogue remains deleted in the UK, but ''[[The White Room]]'' is still being pressed in the US by [[Arista Records|Arista]]. They have released a small number of new tracks since then, as the K Foundation, [[The One World Orchestra]] and most recently, in 1997, as [[Fuck the Millennium|2K]]."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1749168":{"pageid":1749168,"ns":0,"title":"Thomas K\u00f6ner","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"[[File:ThomasKoener Goethe-Institut Boston 22-10-2010 bySusannaBolle.jpg|thumb|K\u00f6ner after a performance at <br/> [[Goethe-Institut]] Boston (2010)]]\n'''Thomas K\u00f6ner''' (born 1965 in [[Bochum]], [[Germany]]) is a multimedia artist whose main interest lies in combining visual and auditory experiences. The group's simplified lyrics are at times sung through a [[vocoder]] or generated by [[speech synthesis|computer-speech software]]. Kraftwerk were one of the first groups to popularize electronic music and are considered [[Innovator|pioneers]] in the field.\n\nIn the 1970s and early 1980s, Kraftwerk's distinctive sound was revolutionary, and has had a lasting effect across many genres of modern music.<ref>Petridis, Alexis. He  studied [[classical guitar]], arrangement and [[Musical composition|composition]] in [[Saint Petersburg]] and later immigrated to [[Canada]]. In the 1980s and 1990s he worked as a guitarist for the Russian State [[concert]] company Lenconcert and the Old Petersburg [[musical theatre|music theater]]. He has given recitals in Russia, Ukraine, Estonia, USA and Canada. Krylov has recorded and performed for Russian, US and Canadian radio and television. He has composed original [[new flamenco]] and [[New Age music]] for films in Russia and the USA. Born Edward Larry Gordon in [[Philadelphia]], he studied violin, piano, trombone and voice in his early years in New Jersey.  He attended [[Howard University]], a [[historically black university]] in [[Washington, D.C.]] on a scholarship to study composition and [[piano]].  After studying at [[Howard University|Howard]], he spent time in [[New York City|New York]] pursuing a career as a stand-up [[comedian]] and [[actor]]. \n\nIn the early seventies he began to study Eastern [[mysticism]] and believed he'd found a new path for his music and his life.  It was also at this time he bought his first [[zither]] from a local [[pawn shop]].  Converting it to an [[electronic instrument]], he began to experiment using the instrument like a piano.  By 1978, he developed enough skill to begin [[busking]] in the parks and on the sidewalks of New York.\n\nThe following year he was \"discovered\" by [[Brian Eno]] while playing in Washington Square Park.  The result was his most widely-recognized release, [[Day of Radiance|Ambient 3: Day of Radiance]], the third installment of [[Brian Eno| Brian Eno's]] Ambient series.  This was his first album released under the name of Laraaji.\n\nThis international exposure led to many requests for longer versions of his compositions which he supplied to many meditation groups on cassette tapes.  It also resulted in an expansion of his mystic studies with such gurus as [[Swami Satchidananda]] and [[Shri Brahmananda Sarasvati]], founder of the Ananda Ashram in Monroe, New York.\n\nAnother product of Laraaji's increasing enlightenment was the creation of the Laughter Meditation Workshops which he still presents around the globe."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"262673":{"pageid":262673,"ns":0,"title":"Bill Laswell","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=July        = \n| associated_acts     = Method Of Defiance, [[The Golden Palominos]], [[Praxis (band)|Praxis]], [[Massacre (experimental band)|Massacre]], [[Material (band)|Material]], [[Buckethead]], Bass]]<ref>{{cite web | url=http://soundcolourvibration.com/2013/05/23/bill-laswell-interview-feature/ | title=Q&A with Bill Laswell | accessdate=April 12, 2015}}</ref>\n}}\n\n'''Bill Laswell''' (born February 12, 1955, [[Salem, Illinois]], and raised in [[Albion, Michigan]]) is an American bassist, producer and [[record label]] owner.\n\nLaswell ranks among the most prolific of modern musicians, being involved in hundreds of recordings with many collaborators from all over the world. Laswell's music draws upon many different [[musical genre|genres]], most notably [[funk]], various [[world music]], [[jazz]], [[Dub music|dub]] and [[ambient music|ambient]] styles. He has also played or produced music from the noisier, more aggressive end of the rock spectrum, such as [[hardcore punk]] and [[heavy metal music|metal]].\n\nAccording to music critic Chris Brazier, \"Laswell's pet concept is 'collision music' which involves bringing together musicians from wildly divergent but complementary spheres and seeing what comes out.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.silent-watcher.net/billlaswell/ |title=THE Bill Laswell Pages |publisher=Silent-watcher.net |date=March 22, 2012 |accessdate=2012-04-03}}</ref> The credo of one record label run by Laswell, and which typifies much of his work, is \"Nothing Is True, Everything Is Permitted.\" Though projects arranged by Laswell may be credited under the same name and often feature the same roster of musicians, the styles and themes explored on different albums can vary dramatically: [[Material (band)|Material]] began as a noisy [[dance music]] project, but subsequent releases have been centered on [[hip hop]], [[jazz]], or backing [[spoken word]] readings by beat generation icon [[William S. Burroughs]]. Similarly, most versions of [[Praxis (band)|Praxis]] have featured guitarist [[Buckethead]], but have explored different permutations with each new album.\n\nThough some artists have chafed against Laswell's distinctive recording and production style (most noticeably some of his for-hire production gigs including [[Mot\u00f6rhead]], [[Swans (band)|Swans]] and [[White Zombie (band)|White Zombie]]) many other collaborations, such as with pianist [[Herbie Hancock]] and singer [[Iggy Pop]] have been lengthier and recurring. He has also worked extensively with his wife, Ethiopian singer [[Gigi (singer)|Gigi]]."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"3615642":{"pageid":3615642,"ns":0,"title":"Thomas Leer","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Thomas Leer\n| image                 = \n| caption            = \n| image_size            = \n| background          = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_name          = Thomas Wishart\n| alias               = \n| birth_place         =[[Port Glasgow]], [[Scotland]]\n| birth_date          = 1953\n| death_date                = \n| origin              = \n| instrument          = [[Singing|Vocals]], [[Keyboard instrument|keyboards]]\n| genre               = [[Synthpop]], [[New wave music|new wave]]\n| occupation          = \n| years_active        = 1978\u2013present\n| label               = \n| associated_acts     = Pressure, [[Act (band)|Act]]\n| website                 = http://www.thomasleer.co.uk/\n| current_members     = \n| past_members        = \n| notable_instruments = \n}}\n'''Thomas Leer''' (born '''Thomas Wishart''', 1953, [[Port Glasgow]], [[Scotland]]) is a Scottish musician who as well as releasing a number of albums and singles in his own right, was also one half (the other being [[Claudia Br\u00fccken]]) of the 1980s [[electropop]] band [[Act (band)|Act]]. The name Loscil is taken from the \"looping oscillator\" function (loscil) in [[Csound]]. Scott Morgan was also the drummer for the Vancouver indie band [[Destroyer (band)|Destroyer]].\n\nA self-released album titled ''A New Demonstration of Thermodynamic Tendencies'' caught the attention of [[experimental music]] label  [[Kranky Records|Kranky]], who signed Morgan on to release his debut album ''Triple Point'' in 2001. The album features six tracks off his first independent release as well as four new tracks.\n\nloscil followed up the release with ''Submers'', an aquatic-themed album. Each track on the album is named after a [[submarine]]. The last track on the album was produced in honour of the people who died on the [[Russian submarine K-141 Kursk]].\n\nHis 2004 album ''First Narrows'' (a reference to the official name of the Vancouver bridge, also known as [[Lions' Gate Bridge]]) marked the incorporation of improvised performances by a number of guest musicians:<ref>[http://www.straight.com/content.cfm?id=3135] {{dead link|date=December 2014}}</ref> Nyla Raney, [[cello]]; Tim Loewen, [[guitar]]; and Jason Zumpano, [[Rhodes piano]]. Consequently, the songs on ''First Narrows'' are more organic and looser in nature than Morgan's previous work.\n\nEight of his songs were featured on the film score of the 2004 documentary, ''[[ScaredSacred]]'', by the award-winning documentary filmmaker, [[Velcrow Ripper]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.scaredsacred.org/credits_music.php|title=Scared Sacred: Music Credits|publisher=Scaredsacred.org|accessdate=19 December 2014}}</ref>\n\nIn 2005, Morgan released ''Stases'', a collection of drones based upon the backgrounds of his work for Kranky Records. The album was made available as a free download-only release from One Records.\n\nThe theme of his fourth major album, released in 2006, continues the conceptual ascent each album has taken, from the sub-atomic level (''Triple Point'') and watery depths (''Submers'') to the surface (''First Narrows'') and the sky (''Plume'').\n\n''Plume'' continues Morgan's musical integration of other musicians' work into his ambient compositions, including Josh August Lindstrom on vibes and [[xylophone]] and Krista Michelle Marshall and Stephen Michael Wood on ebow guitar (as well as Zumpano again on piano)."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"41299536":{"pageid":41299536,"ns":0,"title":"Lotus Plaza","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#REDIRECT [[Lockett Pundt]]\n{{R from move}}"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1988961":{"pageid":1988961,"ns":0,"title":"Lull (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{multiple issues|\n{{Unreferenced|date=June 2009}}\n{{Notability|date=June 2009}}\n}}\n{{merge|Mick Harris|date=January 2012}}'''Lull''' is a [[dark ambient]] side-project of [[Mick Harris]]. \nLull was conceived in late '91 by former [[Napalm Death]] drummer Mick Harris (who also created the ambient dub outfit [[Scorn (band)|Scorn]]) in an attempt to create music that would stretch, if not forsake entirely, the structures of conventional music by developing and exploring sound without beats. Harris' initial foray as Lull into low frequency sound exploration was issued in late '92 under the title Dreamt About Dreaming on the respected underground [[Sentrax]] label. In between his Scorn commitments, the ever prolific Harris continued to develop Lull by recording and releasing scores of 7's and compilation tracks, as well as two more full-lengths that each punctuated another stage of his progression.\nLull favours sombre, minimalistic drones that create a dark, other-worldly atmosphere. Its sound is generally amusical, and very experimental. Borrowing heavily from early works of [[Brian Eno]], Lull's music can be considered either background or foreground listening. \nA similar-sounding album entitled ''Somnific Flux'' was recorded by Harris and [[Bill Laswell]] in 1995."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"3381932":{"pageid":3381932,"ns":0,"title":"Luminaria","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Other uses}}\n{{distinguish|Luminaria (vigil fire)}}\n{{Too few opinions|date=December 2012}}\n[[File:Farolitos, old church, Jemez State Monument.jpg|thumb|Farolitos, old mission church, [[Jemez State Monument]] ]]\n[[File:Luminarias.jpg|thumb|A typical luminaria display in [[Albuquerque, New Mexico]]]]\n\nA '''luminaria''' or '''farolito'''{{#tag:ref|\"But farolitos and luminarias have come to mean the same thing in late 20th-century New Mexico parlance...\"<ref name=steinberg>{{cite news | last=Steinberg | first=David | title=You say luminaria, I say farolito | newspaper=Albuquerque Journal | date=December 19, 1997 | location=NM | page=E16}}</ref>|group=\"nb\"}} (see ''[[#Naming controversy|naming controversy]]'' section below) is a small [[paper lantern]] (commonly a candle set in some sand inside a paper bag) which is of significance in [[New Mexico]] and in southwest [[United States]] at [[Christmas]] time, especially on [[Christmas Eve]]. These paper lanterns have to some extent replaced the older tradition of the [[luminaria (vigil fire)|vigil fire luminaria]] with which they became confused.\n\nYet another form of ''luminaria'', a small torch or large candle, is carried by the leader of the procession of [[Las Posadas]],<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.reporternews.com/news/2009/dec/06/luminarias-symbolize-lighting-way-for-christ/ |title=Katrina Wright: Luminarias symbolize lighting way for Christ child \u00bb Abilene Reporter-News |publisher=Reporternews.com |date= |accessdate=2012-04-27}}</ref> a nine-day holiday running December 16\u201324.\n\nElectrically-lit luminarias are also used, consisting of a string of standard incandescent \"Christmas lights\" with the bulbs covered with a tan plastic sleeve, made to about the size and shape of a small paper bag."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"4196118":{"pageid":4196118,"ns":0,"title":"Lusine","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"'''Lusine''' (also '''L'usine''' and '''Lusine ICL''') is the stage name of '''Jeff McIlwain''', an [[Ambient music|ambient]]/[[intelligent dance music|IDM]] musician. Originally a Texas native, McIlwain now resides in Seattle. In 1998, he attended [[California Institute of the Arts]] to study 20th century electronic music and sound design for music and film. He is often credited for creating the [[dark ambient]] genre with albums recorded under the name '''Lustmord'''. His experimental work has been described as \"not traditionally 'musical'\" with \"more clearly visual aspects\".<ref name=oxhand>{{Citation|last1=Richardson |first1=John |last2=Gorbman |first2=Claudia |last3=Vernallis |first3=Carol |url=https://books.google.com.ar/books?id=Y8JpAgAAQBAJ&pg=PA367#v=onepage&q&f=false |title=The Oxford Handbook of New Audiovisual Aesthetics |page=367 |publisher=[[Oxford University Press]] |year=2013 |isbn=978-0-19-973386-6}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1253127":{"pageid":1253127,"ns":0,"title":"Ray Lynch","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{BLP refimprove|date=February 2015}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=August 2013}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n|name            = Ray Lynch\n|image             = Raylynchphoto.jpg\n|image_size        = 250px\n|background      = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n\n|origin          = [[Salt Lake City, Utah]]\n|birth_date = July 3, 1943 (age 71)\n|instrument      = Classical Guitar, [[Lute]], [[Keyboard instrument|Piano]], Keyboards\n|genre           = [[Adult Alternative]], [[New-age music|New-age]], [[Instrumental music|Instrumental]], [[Classical music|Classical]]\n|occupation      = Composer, Musician, Mathematician, Author\n\n|years_active    = c. 1980\u2013present\n|label           = Ray Lynch Productions <br />[[Windham Hill Records]]\n|website         = {{URL|http://www.raylynch.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Raymond \"Ray\" Lynch''' is a classically trained guitarist and lutenist. He was born in Salt Lake City, [[Utah]] to a musical and artistic family.<ref name=lynch>[http://www.raylynch.com/up_close_and_personal/index.html Ray Lynch's official site: \"Up Close and Personal\"]</ref> His mother was a classical pianist and watercolor artist. At age 6, Lynch began studying the piano until age 12, where he was inspired by the music of [[Andr\u00e9s Segovia]]\u2019s classical recordings and decided to pursue a career in music. He attended both [[St. Stephen's Episcopal School, Austin, Texas|St. Stephen's Episcopal School]] as well as [[Austin High School (Austin, Texas)|Austin High School]] in [[Austin, Texas]], then attended the main campus of [[University of Texas]] for one year before moving to [[Barcelona, Spain]] where he apprenticed to the classical guitar teacher, Eduardo Sainz de la Maza, for three years.<ref name=lynch/> Leaving Spain, Lynch then returned to the [[University of Texas]] where he studied music composition. While at college Lynch was invited to New York City to join The Renaissance Quartet where he performed the classical guitar and [[lute]] for several years.<ref name=lynch/>\n\nIn the early days of his musical career, Lynch began writing instrumental recordings that blended classical and electronic components into melodic soundscapes. His debut album, ''[[The Sky of Mind]]'' (1983) artfully meshed his early classical music training with spatial melodies, and the album became an underground success. When Lynch released his second album ''[[Deep Breakfast]]'' (1984), he and his wife Kathleen sold over 50,000 albums out of their small apartment in [[San Rafael, California]] before licensing the music to a distributor.<ref name=lynch/> ''[[Deep Breakfast]]'' has sold over 1.4 million copies without the benefits of live performances or videos, and was the first independently released album to be certified Platinum by the R.I.A.A.<ref name=riaa>[http://www.riaa.com/goldandplatinumdata.php?resultpage=1&table=SEARCH_RESULTS&title=Deep%20Breakfast&artist=Ray%20Lynch&startMonth=1&endMonth=1&startYear=1958&endYear=2007&sort=Artist&perPage=25 RIAA Gold & Platinum Database]</ref> \"The Oh Of Pleasure\" from the album was used for years as the theme for [[Art Bell]]'s ''Dreamland'' radio show.\n\nLynch's third album ''[[No Blue Thing]]'' (1989) won two [[Billboard Awards]], and in 1993, Lynch followed up with his fourth album, the classical ''[[Nothing Above My Shoulders but the Evening]]'' featuring members of the [[San Francisco Symphony]]. Lynch's fifth and most recent album, ''[[Ray Lynch: Best Of, Volume One]]'' (1998) is a retrospective of his work and includes three new music tracks.\n\n{{listen\n | header       = Further song samples appear on each album page.\n | filename     = Celestial Soda Pop.ogg\n | title        = \"Celestial Soda Pop\"\n | description  = Without live performances or videos Lynch's second album ''[[Deep Breakfast]]'' was the first independently released album to be certified Gold by the R.I.A.A. [[Viacom]] |date=4 September 2007 |accessdate=4 September 2013}}</ref>\n| years_active    = 2001\u2013present\n| label           = [[Na\u00efve Records|Na\u00efve]], [[Mute Records|Mute]], [[Virgin Records|Virgin]]\n| associated_acts = [[Team Ghost]]\n| website         = {{URL|ilovem83.com}}\n| current_members = \n* Anthony Gonzalez\n* [[Morgan Kibby]]\n* Jordan Lawlor\n* Lo\u00efc Maurin\n* Ian Young\n| past_members    = \n* Nicolas Fromageau\n* Pierre-Marie Maulini\n* Yann Gonzalez\n* Phillip Kern\n}}\n\n'''M83''' is a French [[electronic music]] band led by Anthony Gonzalez and currently based in Los Angeles. Formed in 2001 in  [[Antibes]], France, the band initially was a duo featuring Nicolas Fromageau. They have released six albums and two soundtracks, including the Grammy-nominated ''[[Hurry Up, We're Dreaming]]''.\n\nGonzalez and Fromageau parted ways shortly after touring for their second album ''[[Dead Cities, Red Seas & Lost Ghosts]]'',<ref name=\"AMG\">[{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p561410|pure_url=yes}} allmusic ((( M83 - Overview )))]</ref> with Gonzalez now recording primarily on his own, often with the help of his brother Yann Gonzalez, vocalist/keyboardist [[Morgan Kibby]], and drummer Lo\u00efc Maurin. In 2011, Gonzalez posted an open audition on the M83 website for a multi-instrumentalist who could join the band. Nineteen-year-old Jordan Lawlor won the audition. Fromageau formed a new band in 2009 called [[Team Ghost]] and has released two albums to date."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"3127947":{"pageid":3127947,"ns":0,"title":"Maeror Tri","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{multiple issues|\n{{unreferenced|date=October 2011}}\n{{notability|date=October 2011}}\n}}\n\n[[File:Maeror Tri logo.svg|thumb|Logo of Maeror tri, authored by Helge Siehl.]]\n\n[[File:1000sch\u00f8en & Troum.jpg|thumb|Helge Siehl and Stefan Knappe performing as a part of 1000sch\u00f8en and Troum, respectively.]]\n\n'''Maeror Tri''' was an [[ambient music|ambient]], [[noise music|noise]] and [[drone music]] band from Germany founded in the 1980s which consisted of Stefan \"Baraka H\" Knappe, Martin \"GLIT[s]CH\" Gitschel and Helge Siehl.\n\nIn a way similar to [[Zoviet France]], they used only live instruments to produce music with enormous amount of effects applied. They disbanded in the late 1990s after releasing a number of limited-edition records. They released music on labels such as [[Old Europa Cafe]], [[Ant-Zen]], [[Staalplaat]], and [[Soleilmoon]].\n\nStefan and Martin continued under the name of [[Troum]], while Helge is recording as Tausendschoen. Stefan Knappe is also the founder and owner of [[Drone Records]].\n\nGerman band Maeror Tri was founded in April 1988 by Stefan Knappe. The group consisted of three members who only used electric guitars and tons of processing devices to create their droning soundscapes. Their music borrowed elements from Industrial, [[Avant-garde|Avantgarde]], Minimalism and [[New Age]] meditation to reach a new form of transcendentalism.\n\nVery little is known about their origins, even the identity of the band\u2019s members remains vague, except for Stefan Knappe, the group's spokesperson and also owner of the label Drone Records. Nevertheless it is for sure that all three members origin from the city [[Leer]] in northern Germany and know each other since their time in school.\n\nThe name they chose is probably an incorrect Latin expression that may be better translated as \"The Mourning Three\" or \"The Grieving Three\".\n\n\"Dedicated To A New Dawn\", their first cassette, was self-released on their own Baracken Records in 1988, soon followed by many more cassette works on labels like ZNS, Tonspur and Audiofile, and a lot of compilations appearances.\n\nIn 1993 Korm Plastics (a label ran by Frans de Waard) released the very first \"overground\" Maeror Tri album \"Multiple Personality Disorder\" a concept CD divided in four long parts recorded back in 1991 that fully showcase their mastery in distorting and layering guitar sounds. It was soon followed by \"Meditamentum\", a collection of selected tape tracks recorded from 1988 to 1993.\n\n\"Myein\", a monumental work recorded between 1992 and 1993, was released on americal label ND in 1995. This work presented three long tracks that well exemplify some of the aspects of their art: the gothic droning of \"Phlogiston\", the ambient-electronica of \"Desiderium\", and the cosmic doodling of the 47 minutes long title track.\n\n\"Language of Flames and Sound\", released on Italian label Old Europa Cafe in 1996, continued to chronicle the group's evolution into more abstract domains.\n\nIn late 1996, as the group was about to break into the growing experimental electronica scene, one member of the band, Helge Siehl, decided to quit, leaving Knappe and his other partner to continue as the duo Troum.\n\n\"Mort aux Vaches\", a symphony in three movements and the group's installment in Staalplaat's series of experimental electronica, and \"Emotional Engramm\" (on Iris Light), probably their most accessible recording, were both released posthumous in 1997.\n\nArchive material has continued to surface over the years after the group ceased to exist: a second volume of \"Meditamentum\", released on Manifold in 1999, salvaged more material from the early years limited edition cassettes, while the \"Hypnotikum I\" and \"Hypnotikum II\" LPs are valid examples of the group's live attitude."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"3902740":{"pageid":3902740,"ns":0,"title":"Main (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{refimprove|date=February 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = Main\n| image                 = \n| caption            = \n| image_size            = \n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = \n| genre               = [[Ambient music]], [[experimental music]], [[post-rock]], [[dark ambient]], [[alternative rock]], [[indie rock]]<ref name=\"genres\">{{cite web|url={{Allmusic|class=artist|id=main-p44814|pure_url=yes}}|title=Allmusic entry for Main|publisher=Allmusic|accessdate=2 December 2010}}</ref>\n| years_active        = 1991 - They combined ambient sound with layers of electric guitars and dark, foreboding emotional overtones. In 2006, Hampson announced that ''Main'' had effectively been  disbanded in favour of his solo work.\n\nIn October 2010, Hampson announced that he would be reactivating ''Main'', and that along with his solo acousmatic work, he would start performing and recording in a more collaborative process with other sound artists.\n\nIn 2011, the German composer [[Stephan Mathieu]] joined Hampson for a current incarnation of ''Main''."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1687997":{"pageid":1687997,"ns":0,"title":"Makyo","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{For|the French comics creator|Makyo (comics)}}\nThe term {{nihongo|'''makyo'''|\u9b54\u5883|maky\u014d}} is a [[Zen]] term that means \u201cghost cave\u201d or \u201cdevil\u2019s cave.\u201d It is a figurative reference to the kind of self-delusion that results from clinging to an experience and making a conceptual \u201cnest\u201d out of it for oneself. Makyo is essentially synonymous with illusion, but especially in reference to experiences that can occur within meditation practice.\n\nIn Philip Kapleau's ''The Three Pillars of Zen'',<ref>{{cite book\n| last = Kapleau\n| first = Philip\n| authorlink = Philip Kapleau\n| title = The Three Pillars of Zen\n| year = 1967 }}</ref> Yasutani Roshi explained the term as the combination of '''''ma''''' meaning devil and '''''kyo''''' meaning the objective world.  This character for \u201cdevil\u201d can also refer to [[Mara (demon)|Mara]], the Buddhist \u201ctempter\u201d figure; and the character ''kyo'' can mean simply region, condition or place. Makyo refers to the hallucinations and perceptual distortions that can arise during the course of meditation and can be mistaken by the practitioner as \"seeing the true nature\" or [[kensho]]. [[Zen master]]s warn their meditating students to ignore sensory distortions. These can occur in the form of visions and perceptual distortions, but they can also be experiences of blank, trance-like absorption states. In the Zen school, it is understood that neither category of experience \u2013 however fascinating they may be \u2013 is a true and final enlightenment.\n\nContemplative literature contains numerous descriptions of the perceptual distortion produced by meditation. It is characterized in some schools as \"going to the movies,\" a sign of spiritual intensity but a phenomenon that is considered distinctly inferior to the clear insight of settled practice. In some [[Hindu]] schools it is regarded as a product of the sukshma sharira, or \"experience body,\" in its unstable state, and in that respect is seen to be another form of [[Maya (illusion)|maya]], which is the illusory nature of the world as apprehended by ordinary consciousness.\n\nTibetan contemplative literature uses the parallel term ''nyam'', which fall into three categories, usually listed as clarity, bliss, and non-conceptuality.  Many types of meditation phenomena can be classed under this rubric, and are generally tied to the reorganization of the body's subtle energies that can occur in meditation.  See Dudjom Lingpa, (cited in Wallace, the Attention Revolution), and Padmasambhava (in Treasures from the Juniper Ridge) for more specific examples.  Robert Aitken Roshi classifies speaking in tongues as \"elaborate makyo\" (Taking the Path of Zen)."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"707989":{"pageid":707989,"ns":0,"title":"Mana ERG","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"'''Mana ERG''' is the musical project of ex recording engineer and multi-instrumentalist Bruno De Angelis. Born in Rome and grown up in London, he gained experience by recording and producing bands playing very different genres. This had a direct influence on his music, a genre-defying blend of industrial, ethereal, ebm, electronica, and rock elements.\nBruno's closest collaborators, who also assist him in the production, are Joe Erber (piano and keyboards) and Tiberio (guitars), but quite often they are joined by special guests such as soprano Deborah Roberts, who, with her crystal clear and yet warm vocals, adds an ethereal and dream-like touch to the sound. Other notable friends and collaborators are sound manipulator Antonym, Russian composer Artemiy Artemiev, [[Dieter Moebius]], and Attrition's mastermind Martin Bowes."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"582787":{"pageid":582787,"ns":0,"title":"Mannheim Steamroller","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Refimprove|date=December 2010}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Mannheim Steamroller\n| image               = \n| caption             = \n| image_size          = \n| background          = group_or_band\n| alias               = \n| origin              = [[Omaha]], [[Nebraska]]\n| genre               = [[Holiday]], [[symphonic pop]]\n| years_active        = 1974\u2013present\n| label               = [[American Gramaphone]]\n| associated_acts     = \n| website             = [http://mannheimsteamroller.com/ MannheimSteamroller.com] \n| current_members     = [[Chip Davis]]<br />Bobby Jenkins<br />[[Jackson Berkey]]<br />Almeda Berkey<br />Roxanne Layton<br />Ron Cooley<br />[[Arnie Roth]]<br />Chuck Penington<br />[[Tom Sharpe (musician)|Tom Sharpe]]\n| past_members        = \n}}\n'''Mannheim Steamroller''' is an American music group, founded by [[Chip Davis]], that is known primarily for its series of ''[[Fresh Aire]]'' albums, which blend classical music and rock, and for its modern recordings of [[Christmas music]]. [[composer]], music producer, [[Classical music|classical]] [[Crossover (music)|crossover]] [[violin]]ist, visual artist and writer from [[Germany]], now located in [[California]]. She received her US green card based on her achievements in the musical field. Mar\u00e9 has performed as a classical violinist since her early childhood, and has done numerous performances at concert halls and major museums, such as National Gallery Berlin,<ref>[http://www.smb.museum/smb/kalender/details.php?objID=11363&typeId=11&n=1&datum=26.08.2006 Staatliche Museen zu Berlin - What's on<!-- Bot generated title -->]</ref> [[Kunsthaus Z\u00fcrich]], Kunsthallen Brandts,<ref>[http://www.brandts.dk/default.asp?id=139750&detail=true&itemid=140199 Tidligere udstillinger// Kunsthallen Brandts<!-- Bot generated title -->]</ref> and Kunstmuseet Trapholt. In 2006 she started to compose and produce her own music (Electronic / Pop / World / Celtic new age / Classical crossover). Songs consist of [[soundscape]]s, sometimes employing \"[[found sound]]\",  and are frequently accompanied by guest vocalists. The bands' vocals are most often in English, although each release also includes compositions performed in Italian as well, often by Visone himself.  Guest vocalists have included [[Paul Beauchamp]] of the band [[Gullinkambi]], [[Fabrizio Madonese Palumbo]] of the bands [[Larsen (band)|Larsen]] and [[(r)]] and [[G.B. Jones]].
