             = [http://www.a-wave.com/system7/ a-wave.com/system7]\n| current_members     = [[Steve Hillage]]<br />[[Miquette Giraudy]]\n\n}}\n\n'''System 7''' are a British [[ambient music|ambient]] [[electronic dance music|dance]] band. Due to the existence of another band called System Seven they were initially billed as '''777''' in North America. [[System 7]] was the name of the current [[Macintosh Operating System]] at the time of the band's formation.\n\n[[Steve Hillage]] and [[Miquette Giraudy]], both formerly of [[Gong (band)|Gong]], formed System 7 after hearing the likes of [[the Orb]] playing Hillage's 1979 ambient record ''[[Rainbow Dome Musick]]''. They soon became part of the underground dance scene in London. While Hillage and Giraudy form the core of System 7, it is more of an extended collaborative project with artists such as [[Carl Craig]], [[Laurent Garnier]], [[Derrick May (musician)|Derrick May]], [[Alex Paterson]] (of The Orb), and [[Martin Glover|Youth]]. System 7 makes extensive use of Hillage's [[electric guitar]]s.\n\nHillage and Giraudy later launched a spin-off project called ''Mirror System'',<ref>[http://www.a-wave.com/mirrorsystem/ A-wave.com/mirrorsystem]</ref> and have also worked under the name ''Groovy Intent''."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"19361":{"pageid":19361,"ns":0,"title":"Moby","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{other uses}}\n{{BLP sources|date=September 2014}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=May 2012}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name =  Moby\n| image = Moby 1.jpg\n| image_size = 230\n| alt = Moby looking to the camera\n| caption = Moby in 2009\n| background = solo_singer\n| birth_date = {{Birth date and age|mf=yes|1965|9|11}}\n| birth_place =[[Harlem]], [[New&nbsp;York City]]\n| birth_name = Richard Melville Hall\n| origin = [[Darien, Connecticut]], U.S\n| instrument = [[Phonograph|Turntables]], keyboards, [[synthesizer]], [[drum machine]], vocals, guitar, bass&nbsp;guitar, drums\n| genre = [[Electronica]], [[trip hop]], [[house music|house]], [[downtempo]], [[ambient music|ambient]], [[alternative rock]], [[techno]], [[punk rock]], [[electronic rock]]\n| occupation = DJ, singer-songwriter, musician, photographer, animal activist\n| years_active = 1984\u2013present\n| label = [[Mute Records|Mute]], [[V2 Records|V2]]/[[Bertelsmann Music Group|BMG]], [[XL Recordings|XL]], [[Elektra Records|Elektra]], [[Instinct Records|Instinct]], [[Rhythm King Records|Outer&nbsp;Rhythm]], [[Virgin Records|Virgin]]/[[EMI Records|EMI]]\n| associated_acts = [[Myl\u00e8ne&nbsp;Farmer]]\n| website = {{url|http://moby.com/}}\n}}\n'''Richard Melville Hall''' (born September 11, 1965),<ref name=\"Mobybio\">{{cite web | url = http://www.moby.com/biography | title = biography | work=moby.com | accessdate =April 25, 2008}}</ref> known by his stage name '''Moby''', is an American singer-songwriter, musician, DJ and photographer. He is well known for his [[electronic music]], [[vegan]] lifestyle, and support of [[animal rights]]. Moby has sold over 20 million albums worldwide.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=wrV5VW60xxY |title=Moby on Q TV |date=October 26, 2009 |publisher=YouTube |accessdate=September 28, 2011}}</ref> [[AllMusic]] considers him \"one of the most important [[dance music]] figures of the early '90s, helping bring the music to a mainstream audience both in the UK and in America\".<ref>{{cite web | url = http://www.allmusic.com/artist/p13697 | title = Moby |author=Stephen Thomas Erlewine |work=Allmusic |accessdate=September 28, 2011}}</ref>\n\nMoby gained attention in the early 1990s with his [[electronic dance music]] work, which experimented in the [[techno]] and [[breakbeat hardcore]] genres. With his fifth studio album, the [[electronica]] and [[house music|house]]-influenced ''[[Play (Moby album)|Play]]'', he gained international success. Originally released in mid-1999, the album sold 6,000 copies in its first week, and it re-entered the charts in early 2000 and became an unexpected hit, producing eight singles and selling over 10 million copies worldwide.<ref name=moby-didnt-feel-pressure>{{cite web | first = Jerry | last = Armor | url = http://music.yahoo.com/read/news/12054910 | archiveurl = http://web.archive.org/web/20061213050246/http://music.yahoo.com/read/news/12054910 | archivedate = 2006-12-13 | title = Moby Didn't Feel Pressure To Follow Up 'Play,' '18' Bows At Number Four | work=[[Yahoo! Music]] | accessdate =February 23, 2007 | date = May 22, 2002}}</ref> Moby followed the album in 2002 with ''[[18 (Moby album)|18]]'', which was also successful, selling over 5 million copies worldwide and receiving mostly positive reviews, though some criticized it for being too similar to ''Play''.\n\nHis next major release, 2005's mostly upbeat ''[[Hotel (album)|Hotel]]'' was a stylistic departure, incorporating more [[alternative rock]] elements than previous albums, and received mixed reviews. It sold around 2 million copies worldwide. After 2008's [[Electronic dance music|dance]]-influenced ''[[Last Night (Moby album)|Last Night]]'' (2008), he returned to the [[downtempo]] electronica of ''Play'' and ''18'' with 2009's mostly-ambient ''[[Wait for Me (Moby album)|Wait for Me]]'', finding higher critical acclaim and moderate sales, as well as 2011's ''[[Destroyed (Moby album)|Destroyed]]''. Moby's latest album, ''[[Innocents (Moby album)|Innocents]]'', was released on October 1, 2013.\n\nMoby has also co-written, produced, and remixed music for [[Michael Jackson]], [[David Bowie]], [[Daft Punk]], [[Myl\u00e8ne Farmer]], [[Brian Eno]], [[Pet Shop Boys]], [[Britney Spears]], [[New Order (band)|New Order]], [[Public Enemy (band)|Public Enemy]], [[Guns N' Roses]], [[Metallica]], [[Soundgarden]], and others.<ref>{{cite interview |subject=Moby |url=http://thequietus.com/articles/06224-moby-interview-destroyed |title=\"The Humility That Comes From Being Hated\": Moby Interviewed |work=The Quietus |interviewer=Stephen Dalton |date=May 9, 2011 |accessdate=September 28, 2011}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"6983668":{"pageid":6983668,"ns":0,"title":"Moodswings (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{unreferenced|date=February 2009}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Moodswings\n| image                 =\n| caption            = cover of first album ''Moodfood''\n| image_size            = 250\n| background          = group_or_band\n| alias               = \n| origin              = [[UK]]\n| genre               = [[Electronic music]]<br/>[[Ambient music|Ambient]]<br/>[[Trance music]]\n| years_active        = 1992&ndash;present\n| label               = [[Water Music Records|Water Music]]/[[Var\u00e8se Sarabande Records|Var\u00e8se Sarabande]]/[[Universal Music Group|Universal Records]]<br/>[[Arista Records|Arista]]/[[Bertelsmann Music Group|BMG Records]]\n| associated_acts     = [[The Smiths]]\n| website                 = \n| current_members     = James F.T. Grant Showbiz was a onetime roadie and guitar tech who later produced albums by [[The Smiths]], [[Billy Bragg]], [[Silverfish]], and [[Gong]]. James Hood was a former drummer for [[The Pretenders]], [[The Impossible Dreamers]], [[Kid Creole & the Coconuts]] and [[Jeff Beck]]. After Showbiz and Hood teamed up in 1989, the duo released the album ''[[Moodfood]]'' ([[Arista Records|Arista/BMG]], 1992), which scored a hit with a remade single of \"Spiritual High ([[State of Independence]]) Pt. II,\" which featured vocals by [[Chrissie Hynde]] ([[The Pretenders]]).  \"Spiritual High Pt. III,\" from the same album, featured [[sampling (music)|samples]] from [[Martin Luther King Jr.]]'s \"[[I Have a Dream]]\" speech. \"Spiritual High II\" was played during the closing credits of the 1992 [[Bridget Fonda]] film ''[[Single White Female]]'', and was included on The Pretenders' 2000 album ''[[Greatest Hits (The Pretenders)|Greatest Hits]]''.\n\nThe ''Live at Leeds'' EP ([[Arista Records|Arista]]) followed in 1994 (with artwork styled after the album by [[the Who]] of the [[Live at Leeds|same name]]), and in 1997, the group released ''Psychedelicatessen'' ([[Arista Records|Arista/BMG]]), which featured vocals from [[Tanita Tikaram]], on the song \"Oh Happy Day'. Grant Showbiz was a member of Moodswings up until the album ''Horizontal'', which James Hood solo-produced ([[Var\u00e8se Sarabande]], 2002). [[Julee Cruise]] sings vocals on two tracks from ''Horizontal'': \"Seems to Remind Me\" and \"Into the Blue.\" James Hood contributed \"Storm in a Teacup\" from the same album for the 2005 documentary ''Do You Believe? At the age of 17, he was awarded a 1970 [[Broadcast Music Incorporated|BMI]] Student Composer Award for his orchestral work ''Ilium, New York, Is Divided Into Three Parts''. He attended Berklee College of Music in Boston from 1971 to 1975. In 1976, he moved to New York to become a noted studio musician, arranger and producer for a wide range of well-known artists, including [[Rihanna]], [[Aaron Neville]], [[Michael Franks (musician)|Michael Franks]], [[Carly Simon]], [[Natalie Cole]], [[Diana Krall]], [[Steely Dan]], [[Paul Simon]], [[James Taylor]], [[Chaka Khan]], [[Eric Clapton]], [[Madonna (entertainer)|Madonna]], [[Diana Ross]], [[Donald Fagen]], [[Brian Wilson]], [[Aztec Camera]], [[Chromeo]], and countless others. He performed on keyboards in 1981 for [[The Concert in Central Park|Simon and Garfunkel's Concert In The Park]].\n\nIn 1985, he played keyboards in a New-York-based group called [[Joe Cool (band)|Joe Cool]] with Will Lee, Jeff Mironov and Christopher Parker. They released one album, ''Party Animals'', on the Pony/Canyon label in Japan, followed by a Japanese tour. Mounsey also released three solo albums as a recording artist: ''Dig'' (Sona Gaia, 1990), and two self-released albums on his own Monkeyville label, ''Back in the Pool'' and ''Mango Theory.'' \nMounsey toured as musical director and pianist for [[Idina Menzel]] in her Pops Symphony tour, for which he created nearly all of the  arrangements.\n\nHe has also composed widely for film and television, including the 1988 Mike Nichols film ''[[Working Girl]]'' (with [[Carly Simon]]), the film ''[[Bright Lights, Big City (film)|Bright Lights, Big City]]'' (with [[Donald Fagen]]), and the HBO hit series ''[[Sex and the City]]''.<ref name=rob/> Mounsey also wrote two themes for the television show ''[[Guiding Light]]''. He is a six-time [[Grammy Award]] nominee, and a winner of two [[Emmy Awards]].<ref name=rob/>  He is a [[Zen]] Buddhist who resides in [[Brooklyn]], [[New York]].\n\nRob Mounsey is represented by Joe D'Ambrosio Management Inc."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2855930":{"pageid":2855930,"ns":0,"title":"Murcof","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist  <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = Murcof\n| image                 = Murcof.jpg\n| caption            = Murcof performing at Sonar Festival, Barcelona, June 15th 2007\n| background          = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_name          = Fernando Corona Murillo\n| Also known as       = Terrestre\n| birth_date                = {{birth date and age|1970|7|26|df=y}}\n|birth_place =  [[Tijuana]], [[Mexico]]\n| death_date                = \n| instrument          = [[Laptop]], [[piano]], [[cello]], [[synthesizer]]\n| genre               = [[Electronica]], [[Ambient music|ambient]], [[contemporary classical music]], [[glitch music]], [[minimal techno]], [[Intelligent dance music|IDM]]\n| occupation          = composer, musician, record producer, mastering engineer\n| years_active        = 2001-present\n| label               = Static Discos, [[The Leaf Label]], Context, InFin\u00e9, [[Blue Note Records]]\n| associated_acts     = Vortex, Elohim, Alvores, Terrestre, [[Nortec Collective]], Sonios, Murcof & Erik Truffaz, Murcof & Francesco Tristano, Wixarika project, Murcof & Philippe Petit, Murcof & Simon Geilfus, Murcof & Vanessa Wagner \n| website                 = [http://www.murcof.com/ www.murcof.com]\n| notable_instruments = \n}}\n'''Murcof''' is the performing and recording name of Mexican [[electronica]] artist '''Fernando Corona'''.\nCorona was born in 1970 in [[Tijuana]], [[Mexico]] and raised in Ensenada. From 1974 to 1985 he travelled around the world to study African, Indian, and Near & Far Eastern music, to make field recordings and collect musical instruments. He recorded LPs and CDs for different European labels (including Raw Materials, Recommended Records, Vict\u00f2, Lowlands, and [[Island Records]]).\n\nMusci composed and played music for videos (Studio Equatore, Miguel Soares), commercial spots ([[Levi's]], [[Nike, Inc.|Nike]], [[Bulgari]], [[IBM]], United Way), dance (Tanzfabrik Berlin, Los Angeles Choreographer & dancers), live soundtracks for silent movies (''[[Rain (1929 film)|Regen]]'' and ''[[The Bridge (1928 film)|The Bridge]]'', both directed by [[Joris Ivens]]; ''[[The Phantom of the Opera (1925 film)|The Phantom of the Opera]]'', directed by [[Rupert Julian]]; ''[[Vampyr]]'', directed by [[Friedrich Wilhelm Murnau]]; ''[[Manhatta]]'', directed by [[Paul Strand]]; ''[[Safety Last!]]'', directed by [[Fred C. Newmeyer]] with [[Harold Lloyd]]; ''[[Der Golem (film)|Der Golem]]'', directed by Carl Boese and [[Paul Wegener]], ''Saturnino Farandol\u00e0'', directed by Marcel Perez and [[Luigi Maggi]]; ''[[The Crowd (1928 film)|The Crowd]]'', directed by [[King Vidor]]; and ''Belfagor'', directed by Henri Desfontains), poems (with Massimo Cavallaro for Piera degli Esposti), and theater (with Massimo Cavallaro for [[Antonio Albanese]]).\n\nHe made soundtracks for movies (with Giovanni Venosta) for [[Silvio Soldini]]'s movie ''L'aria serena dell'Ovest'', Alessandro Amaducci's movie ''Spoonriver'', Stefano Canzio's video ''Sua Intermittenza'', Andrea Gropplero's movie ''Pidjin'', Monica Castiglioni's movie ''Rita incontra una amica''. Inspired by the music of [[Eberhard Weber]], [[Miles Davis]], [[Antonio Carlos Jobim]], [[Fr\u00e9d\u00e9ric Chopin|Chopin]], [[Wendy Carlos]], [[Tangerine Dream]] and [[Pink Floyd]], he also composed which he personally is not involved in the music making).\n\nPete Namlook has released many solo albums, as well as collaboration albums with notable artists such as [[Klaus Schulze]], [[Bill Laswell]], [[Geir Jenssen]] (alias [[Biosphere (musician)|Biosphere]]), [[Atom Heart]], [[Richie Hawtin]], [[Tetsu Inoue]], [[Uwe Schmidt|Dr. Atmo]], and [[Tying Tiffany]].\n\n\"Namlook\" is [[ambient music|ambient]] American music and [[Bali]]nese [[gamelan]].<ref>[http://www.lbpost.com/sander/6924 Local Artist Loren Nerell Plays Immersion Fest Saturday], ''LBPost.com'', October 16, 2009</ref>\n\nAs a composer, Loren has written music for film, theater, dance, and interactive multi-media. He has performed with the [[Kronos Quartet]],<ref>[http://www.musicology.ucla.edu/index.php?option=com_content&view=article&id=1171:kronos-quartet&catid=93&Itemid=226 Kronos Quartet to Hold Residency at Ethnomusicology] Department of Ethnomusicology Newsletter, Vol. 9 No. 1 Winter 1994</ref> has recorded six albums of original work,<ref>[http://www.spiderbytes.com/ambientrance/ner-is.htm Loren Nerell: Indonesian Soundscapes], Spiderbytes.com, May 1999</ref> has appeared on several compilations such as ''Dali: The Endless Enigma'', ''Soundscape Gallery 3'', and ''Weightless, Effortless'', and has made guest appearances on recordings such as [[Steve Roach (musician)|Steve Roach]]'s ''Artifacts'',<ref>[http://www.discogs.com/Steve-Roach-Artifacts/release/23615 Steve Roach \u2013 Artifacts ], ''Discogs.com''</ref> [[Paul Haslinger]]'s ''World Without Rules'',<ref>[http://www.discogs.com/Paul-Haslinger-World-Without-Rules/release/180090 Paul Haslinger \u2013 World Without Rules], ''Discogs.com''</ref> [[Djam Karet]]'s ''Collaborator'',<ref>[http://www.discogs.com/Djam-Karet-Collaborations/release/1262708, Djam Karet \u2013 Collaborator], ''Discogs.com''</ref>  and [[L. Subramaniam]]'s ''Global Fusion''. He spent several months in [[Java]] and Bali studying native styles of gamelan music, some of which he has performed in the greater Los Angeles area with other gamelan enthusiasts.\n\nLoren Nerell was born in [[Long Beach, California]]. His early interest in [[electronic music]] began when he heard the [[Tangerine Dream]] album ''[[Rubycon (album)|Rubycon]]''. With it, he crossed over into a world of music that previously did not exist for him. He studied analog synthesis at [[Long Beach City College|Long Beach Community College]] eventually moving to [[San Diego State University]] where he was exposed to tape manipulation and tape composition techniques. He also began performing and studying Balinese gamelan music, and the [[microtonal]] composition of [[Harry Partch]]. From San Diego, Loren moved to [[California State University Dominguez Hills]] where he delved into computer synthesis, utilizing their [[Synclavier]] system.\n\nAfter mastering the techniques he learned in school, he developed his own studio, stocking it with an array of vintage sound modules as well as the latest technology. He has worked in the music industry as a sound designer including a position at Oberheim Electronics, a synthesizer manufacturer, and as a recording engineer.\n\nLoren received a Bachelor of Science degree in Anthropology and Geography from [[Cal Poly Pomona]] and a Master of Arts degree in [[ethnomusicology]] from [[UCLA]]. His thesis is on the ceremonial gamelan music of Bali called lelambatan. Loren currently works in UCLA's Herb Alpert School of Music as a recording technician.  <ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ethnomusic.ucla.edu/loren-nerell-bio-1 |title=Welcome to the UCLA Department of Ethnomusicology |publisher=Ethnomusic.ucla.edu |date= |accessdate=2014-08-05}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1627587":{"pageid":1627587,"ns":0,"title":"Nightnoise","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{EngvarB|date=August 2014}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=August 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Nightnoise\n| image           = Nightnoise.png\n| caption         = Nightnoise in Seville, Spain, 1990\n| image_size      = 250\n| background      = group_or_band\n| alias           =\n| origin          = Ireland\n| genre           = {{Plainlist|\n* [[Folk music of Ireland|Irish traditional]]\n* Classical\n* [[Irish music|Celtic]]\n* [[Jazz]]\n}}\n| years_active    = 1984\u20131997\n| label           = [[Windham Hill Records|Windham Hill]]\n| associated_acts = {{Plainlist|\n* [[Skara Brae (band)|Skara Brae]]\n* [[The Bothy Band]]\n* [[M\u00edche\u00e1l \u00d3 Domhnaill]]\n}}\n| current_members = {{Plainlist|\n* [[Johnny Cunningham]]\n* [[Brian Dunning (flautist)|Brian Dunning]]\n* John Fitzpatrick\n* [[Tr\u00edona N\u00ed Dhomhnaill]]\n* [[M\u00edche\u00e1l \u00d3 Domhnaill]]\n* [[Billy Oskay]]\n}}\n}}\n\n'''Nightnoise''' was a music ensemble active from 1984 to 1997. From left to right: [[Pino Palladino]], [[Ilan Rubin]], [[Trent Reznor]], and [[Alessandro Cortini]].\n| image_size     = 250 <!-- Template states: \"Size for landscape images should be 250.\" -->\n| landscape      = Yes\n| background     = group_or_band\n| origin         = [[Cleveland]], [[Ohio]], [[United States|U.S.]]\n| years_active   = 1988\u2013present <!--Please, do not change without prior talk-page consensus. -->\n| genre          = \n{{flatlist|\n*[[Industrial rock]]\n*[[alternative rock]]\n*[[industrial metal]]\n*[[dark ambient]] <!--Please, do not add genres without prior talk-page consensus. -->}}\n| label          = [[Columbia Records|Columbia]], [[The Null Corporation]], [[Interscope Records|Interscope]], [[Nothing Records|Nothing]], [[TVT Records|TVT]]\n| associated_acts= <!-- Only list acts which have two or more members in common, as per Wikipedia guidelines -->[[How to Destroy Angels (band)|How to Destroy Angels]], [[SONOIO]], [[Tapeworm (band)|Tapeworm]], [[Marilyn Manson (band)|Marilyn Manson]], [[Exotic Birds]], [[Pigface]], [[Jane's Addiction]], [[David Bowie]], [[Gary Numan]], [[Peter Murphy (musician)|Peter Murphy]], [[A Perfect Circle]], [[David Fincher]]\n| website        = {{URL|nin.com|nin.com}}\n| current_members= [[Trent Reznor]]<br />[[Robin Finck]]<br />[[Alessandro Cortini]]<br />[[Ilan Rubin]]\n| past_members   = [[List of Nine Inch Nails band members#Former live members|Former live members]]\n|\n}}\n\n'''Nine Inch Nails''' (abbreviated and stylized as  '''NI\u0418''') is an American [[industrial rock]] band, founded in 1988 by [[Trent Reznor]] in [[Cleveland]], [[Ohio]]. As its main [[producer (music)|producer]], singer, songwriter, and instrumentalist, Reznor is the only official member of the group and remains solely responsible for its direction.<ref name = \"AMG\">{{cite web| author = Huey, Steve| url = http://www.allmusic.com/artist/nine-inch-nails-mn0000351733/biography| title = Nine Inch Nails| accessdate = November 24, 2006| publisher = [[AllMusic]]}}</ref> Nine Inch Nails' music straddles a wide range of genres. After recording a new album, Reznor usually assembles [[Nine Inch Nails live performances|a live band]] to perform with him. The touring band features a revolving lineup that often rearranges songs to fit a live setting. On stage, Nine Inch Nails often employs visual elements to accompany performances, which frequently include light shows.<ref name = \"Reimink\">{{Cite news| last = Reimink| first = Troy| title = Changes in songs, lineup keep Nails sharp| work = [[Grand Rapids Press]]|publisher=[[Booth Newspapers]]| page = D1| date = March 5, 2007}}</ref>\n\n[[Underground music]] audiences warmly received Nine Inch Nails in its early years. Reznor produced several highly influential records in the 1990s that achieved widespread popularity: many Nine Inch Nails songs became radio hits;<ref name = \"Allmusic charts\">{{cite web| url = {{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p5033|pure_url=yes}}| title = Nine inch Nails > Charts & Awards| publisher = [[AllMusic]]| accessdate = August 15, 2009}}</ref> and [[Nine Inch Nails discography|their entire catalog]] has reached record sales exceeding over 20&nbsp;million albums worldwide,<ref name=\"Yahoo!Court\" /> with 10&nbsp;million sales certified in the United States alone.<ref name=\"RIAAbestsellers\" /> In 1997, Reznor appeared in ''[[Time (magazine)|Time]]'' magazine's list of the year's most influential people, and ''Spin'' magazine described him as \"the most vital artist in music.\"<ref name=\"Time\">{{Cite journal| url = http://content.time.com/time/magazine/article/0,9171,986206-18,00.html| title = Time's 25 most influential Americans| journal = [[Time (magazine)|Time]]| publisher = [[Time Inc.]] ([[Time Warner]])| date = April 21, 1997| volume = 149| issue = 16| page = 66| accessdate = April 15, 2008}}</ref>\nIn 2004, ''[[Rolling Stone]]'' placed Nine Inch Nails at 94 on its list of the 100 greatest artists of all time.<ref name=\"Bowie\" /> Despite this acclaim, the band has had several feuds with the corporate side of the recording industry. In 2007, these corporate entanglements resulted in Reznor announcing that Nine Inch Nails would split from its label and release future material independently.<ref name=\"BBFreeAgent\" />\n\nSince 1989, Nine Inch Nails has released eight studio albums. After a hiatus from 2009 to 2013, Nine Inch Nails released ''[[Hesitation Marks]]'', through [[Columbia Records]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://kroq.cbslocal.com/2013/06/05/nine-inch-nails-premieres-came-back-haunted-from-new-album-hesitation-marks/ |title=Nine Inch Nails Premieres 'Came Back Haunted' From New Album 'Hesitation Marks'  |publisher=KROQ|date=June 5, 2013 |accessdate=September 2, 2013}}</ref> Prior to this, ''[[Ghosts I\u2013IV]]'' and ''[[The Slip (album)|The Slip]]'' were both independently released in digital form, with physical releases coming later. The digital release of the latter was made available completely free of charge, and the former, while also available for sale, can be acquired legally through means such as file-sharing due to its Creative Commons license. Nine Inch Nails has been nominated for thirteen [[Grammy Award]]s and won twice for the songs \"[[Wish (Nine Inch Nails song)|Wish]]\" and \"[[Happiness in Slavery]]\", in 1992 and 1996 respectively. In 2014, Nine Inch Nails were named as nominees for induction into the [[Rock and Roll Hall of Fame]], their first year of eligibility.<ref name=\"rollingstone.com\">{{cite web| url=http://www.rollingstone.com/music/news/green-day-nine-inch-nails-smiths-nominated-for-rock-and-roll-hall-of-fame-20141009| title=Green Day, Nine Inch Nails, Smiths Nominated for Rock and Roll Hall of Fame | work=[[Rolling Stone]] | accessdate=January 12, 2014}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2108842":{"pageid":2108842,"ns":0,"title":"No-Man","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use dmy dates|date=August Wilson]] (the latter also of [[Porcupine Tree]]). The band has so far produced six studio albums and a number of singles/outtakes collections (most notably, 2006's career retrospective, ''All The Blue Changes''). The band was once lauded as \"conceivably the most important English group since [[The Smiths]]\" by ''[[Melody Maker]]'' music newspaper.<ref>[http://www.no-man.co.uk/press.html no-man]</ref>\n\nOriginally creating a sample-based proto-[[trip hop]]/[[ambient music|ambient]]/[[electro-pop]]-styled music, No-Man has pursued a more organic, diverse and band-oriented sound in subsequent years. Drawing from a diverse mix of singer-songwriter, [[post rock]], [[minimalist]], [[progressive rock]], [[jazz]] and contemporary [[Ambient music|ambient]] sources for inspiration, No-Man's musical style is distinctive yet difficult to categorise."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2943023":{"pageid":2943023,"ns":0,"title":"Alva Noto","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = Carsten Nicolai\n| image                 = RasterNoton-NotoLive.png|thumb\n| caption            = Carsten Nicolai as ''Noto'', playing live at [[Mutek|MUTEK]] 2004\n| image_size            =\n| background          =non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_name          = Carsten Nicolai\n| alias               = Aleph-1, Alva Noto, Noto\n| birth_place                = [[Chemnitz]], [[Saxony]], [[Germany]]\n| birth_date                = {{Birth year and age|1965}}\n| death_date                =\n| origin              = [[Chemnitz]], [[Saxony]], [[Germany]] and [[Berlin]], [[Germany]]<ref name=\"carstennicolai\">[http://www.carstennicolai.de/?c=biography Carsten Nicolai biography]</ref>\n| instrument          = [[Synthesizer]], [[electronic keyboard|keyboards]], [[laptop]], [[guitar]], [[percussion]]\n| genre               = [[Electronica]], [[Glitch (music)|glitch]], [[microsound]]\n| occupation          =\n| years_active        =\n| label               = [[Raster-Noton]], [[Mille Plateaux]], Line\n| associated_acts     = [[Noto]], Cyclo, Opto, Signal (german band)|Signal, [[Ryuichi Sakamoto]], [[Ryoji Ikeda]], [[Blixa Bargeld]]\n| website                 = [http://www.alvanoto.com/ www.alvanoto.com]\n| notable_instruments =\n}}\n\n<!-- Do not use the \"dated prod\" template directly; the above line is generated by \"subst:prod|reason\" -->\n'''Carsten Nicolai''' is a [[German people|German]] [[musician]]. He uses the stage names '''Alva Noto''', '''Noto''' and '''Aleph-1'''. He is a member of the music groups '''Diamond Version''' with Olaf Bender (Byetone), '''Signal''' with [[Frank Bretschneider]] and Olaf Bender, '''Cyclo''' with [[Ryoji Ikeda]], and '''Alva Noto + Ryuichi Sakamoto''' with [[Ryuichi Sakamoto]].\n\nNicolai was born in [[Chemnitz]], [[Saxony]], [[Germany]] (then [[Karl-Marx-Stadt]], [[Saxony]], [[East Germany]]) in 1965. He studied architecture and landscape design before pursuing art. In 1999 he founded [[Raster-Noton]].<ref name=\"carstennicolai\"/>\n\nNicolai has recently written an opera, ''[[Sparkie Williams|Sparkie]]: Cage and Beyond'', in collaboration with [[Michael Nyman]].<ref>{{cite news| url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/uk_news/england/tyne/7963007.stm | work=BBC News | title=Linguistic budgie inspires opera | date=2009-03-25 | accessdate=2010-04-23}}</ref>\n\nNicolai has performed and created installations in many of the world's most prestigious spaces including the [[Solomon R. Guggenheim Museum|Guggenheim]], [[New York City|New York]], the [[San Francisco Museum of Modern Art|SF MoMA]], Modern Art Oxford, [[Nippon Telegraph and Telephone|NTT]] [[Tokyo]], [[Tate Modern]] and [[Venice Biennale]], [[Italy]]. As a member (and co-founder) of the Raster-Noton label he was responsible for the acclaimed CD series '20 to 2000' that went on to win the Golden Nica prize at [[Prix Ars Electronica]], 2000.\n\nCarsten Nicolai also works as a visual artist. Using the principles of [[Cymatics]] he often visualizes sound. In 2013, Nicolai participated as a visual artist in ''Noise'', an official collateral show of the ''55th [[Venice Biennale]] of Art'' <ref>[http://www.dearteassociazione.org/www.dearteassociazione.org/NOISE.html ''NOISE'': an exhibition organized by De Arte Association, curated by Marisa Vescovo]</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"9588631":{"pageid":9588631,"ns":0,"title":"Numina (musician)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#redirect [[Jesse Sola]]"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"80664":{"pageid":80664,"ns":0,"title":"Michael Nyman","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{About|the composer/musician Michael Nyman|his eponymous album|Michael Nyman (1981 album)}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=January 2014}}\n{{Use British English|date=January 2014}}\n\n{{BLP sources|date=January 2015}}\n<!-- please do not add an infobox, per [[Wikipedia:WikiProject Classical music/Style guidelines#Biographical infoboxes]]-->\n[[File:Michael Nyman Sant Cugat.jpg|thumb|Nyman in 2010]]\n'''Michael Laurence Nyman''', [[Order of the British Empire|CBE]] (born 23 March 1944) is an English composer of [[minimalist music]], pianist, [[libretto|librettist]] and [[musicologist]], known for numerous film [[soundtrack|scores]] (many written during his lengthy collaboration with the [[film director|filmmaker]] [[Peter Greenaway]]), and his [[multi-platinum]] [[The Piano (soundtrack)|soundtrack album]] to [[Jane Campion]]'s ''[[The Piano]]''. He has additionally written a number of operas, including ''[[The Man Who Mistook His Wife for a Hat (opera)|The Man Who Mistook His Wife for a Hat]]'', ''[[Letters, Riddles and Writs]]'', ''[[Noises, Sounds & Sweet Airs]]'', ''[[Facing Goya]]'', ''[[Man and Boy: Dada]]'', ''[[Love Counts]]'', and ''Sparkie: Cage and Beyond'', and he has written six [[concerti]], four [[string quartet]]s, and many other [[chamber music|chamber]] works, many for his [[Michael Nyman Band]], with and without whom he tours as a performing pianist. Nyman stated that he prefers to write opera rather than other sorts of music.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.musicweb-international.com/classrev/2005/Dec05/Nyman_Interview.htm |title=Michael Nyman - Interview by John Leeman- December 2005 MusicWeb-International |publisher=Musicweb-international.com |date=2005-11-07 |accessdate=2014-08-10}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"407566":{"pageid":407566,"ns":0,"title":"Vidna Obmana","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Vidna Obmana\n| image           =\n| caption        =\n| background      =non_performing_personnel\n| birth_name      = [[Dirk Serries]]\n| birth_date      = 1968 \n| origin          = [[Belgium]]\n| instrument      =\n| genre           = [[Ambient music]]<br>[[Minimal music]]<br>[[Drone music]]\n| occupation      =\n| years_active    = 1984\u20132007\n| label           = [[ND Records]]<br>[[Hypnos Recordings]]<br>[[Soleilmoon Recordings]]<br>[[Projekt Records]]\n| associated_acts = [[Steve Roach (musician)|Steve Roach]]<br>[[Alio Die]]\n| Spouse          =\n| website             = [http://vidnaobmana.be vidnaobmana.be]\n}}\n\n'''''Vidna Obmana<!--\"Vidna Obmana\" per talk page-->''''' (stylized ''vidnaObmana'' on many album covers) is a [[pseudonym]] used by [[Belgium|Belgian]] composer and [[ambient music]]ian [[Dirk Serries]]. The name ''Vidna Obmana'', a phrase in [[Serbian language|Serbian]], literally translates to \"optical illusion\" and was chosen by Serries because he felt it accurately described the music.<ref name=\"VidnaObmana Bio\">{{cite web|url=http://www.vidnaobmana.be/index.php?pg=vidnaobmana|title=Vidna Obmana|accessdate=2009-11-13}}</ref> Serries created music under the Vidna Obmana pseudonym from 1984 until 2007, when he official retired the name.<ref name=\"VidnaObmana\">{{cite web|url=http://www.vidnaobmana.be/|title=Vidna Obmana|accessdate=2009-11-13}}</ref> Most of his current work is released under the ''Fear Falls Burning'' pseudonym.<ref name=\"Fear Falls Burning, History\">{{cite web|url=http://www.fearfallsburning.be/|title=Fear Falls Burning, History|accessdate=2009-11-13}}</ref>\n\nVidna Obmana's music has often been described as anamorphic and organic. He uses the techniques of looping and shaping harmonies, minimizing the configurations to a few notes.<ref>[http://www.moodbook.com/music/vidna-obmana.html Vidna Obmana discography]</ref>\n\nVidna Obmana has collaborated on several occasions with artists such as [[Asmus Tietchens]], [[Brannan Lane]], [[Capriolo Trifoglio]], [[Diego Borotti]], and [[Steve Roach (musician)|Steve Roach]]. Some of these collaborations have become entire projects of their own, such as [[Continuum (music project)|Continuum]] (collaboration with [[Bass Communion]]) and Principle of Silence (collaboration with [[Joris De Backer]]).\n\nVidna Obmana is often cited as one of the more notable dark ambient musicians.<ref>Larry Austin, [http://www.mitpressjournals.org/doi/abs/10.1162/comj.2004.28.4.87?journalCode=comj Center for Experimental Music and Intermedia: Forty Years on the Edge], Computer Music Journal, April 2004</ref><ref>Teresa Gubbins, [http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=DM&p_theme=dm&p_action=search&p_maxdocs=200&p_topdoc=1&p_text_direct-0=0ED3D44AC8478E7C&p_field_direct-0=document_id Vidna Obmana], Dallas Morning News, February 24, 1994</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"24164808":{"pageid":24164808,"ns":0,"title":"Obsil","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n|name = Obsil\n|image =\n|caption =\n|image_size = 200px\n|background = group_or_band\n|alias =\n|origin = [[Siena]], [[Italy]]\n|instrument =\n|genre = [[Ambient music|Ambient]], [[Classical music|Classical]], [[Experimental music|Experimental]]\n|occupation =\n|years_active = 1999 to Present\n|label = [[Psychonavigation Records]] [[Disasters by Choice Records]]\n|associated_acts =\n|website = http://www.obsil.com\n|current_members = Giulio Aldinucci\n|past_members =\n}}\n\n'''Obsil''' is the musical project of the Italian composer [[Giulio Aldinucci]] (born in [[Siena]], 1981). It features amplified guitar which is processed and layered using digital [[music looping|looping]] equipment enabling a single guitar to produce symphonic levels of density. Ombient has in the last 3 years delved deeply into the world of analog synthesis and more recently analog modular synthesis.\n\nMike Hunter also plays in the [[Progressive rock|Progressive]]/[[World Music|World]]/[[Ambient music|Ambient]]/[[Space Rock]] Band known as Brainstatik<ref>http://www.brainstatik.com Brainstatik</ref> (Progressive/World/Ambient/Space Rock Band of which Mike Hunter is a member.\n\nMike Hunter is also a [[Fractal art]]ist.<ref>http://art.ombient.com The Fractal Artwork of Mike Hunter.</ref>\n\nMike Hunter also hosts the long time running FM radio program <ref>http://www.musicwithspace.com</ref> Music With Space on <ref>http://www.wprb.com</ref> WPRB 103.3 FM"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1785332":{"pageid":1785332,"ns":0,"title":"Omni Trio","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#REDIRECT [[Rob Haigh]]"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"15298636":{"pageid":15298636,"ns":0,"title":"On! (band)|Orb (comics)}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=August 2012}}\n{{Use British English|date=August 2012}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = The Orb\n| image           = OrbCopenhagen.jpg\n| caption         = Alex Paterson and Thomas Fehlmann of the Orb at Culture Box in [[Copenhagen]] in 2005.\n| image_size      = \n| background      = group_or_band\n| alias           = \n| origin          = London, England\n| instrument      = \n| genre           = [[Ambient house]], [[house music|house]], [[dub (music)|dub]], [[reggae]], [[ambient (music)|ambient]], [[trip hop]], [[Intelligent dance music|IDM]]\n| occupation      = \n| years_active    = 1988\u2013present\n| label           = [[Big Life]], [[Island Records|Island]], [[Badorb.com]], [[Kompakt]], Malicious Damage, [[Mercury Records|Mercury]], [[MCA Records|MCA]], [[Columbia Records|Columbia]]\n| associated_acts = [[The KLF]], [[Sun Electric]], [[System 7 (band)|System 7]], [[FFWD (album)|FFWD]], [[Martin Glover|Youth]], [[Transit Kings]], [[David Gilmour]]\n| website         = {{url|www.theorb.com}}\n| current_members = [[Alex Paterson]]<br />[[Thomas Fehlmann]]\n| past_members    = [[Jimmy Cauty]]<br />[[Kris Weston]]<br />Andy Falconer<br />[[Andy Hughes]]<br />[[Simon Phillips (producer)|Simon Phillips]]<br /> Nick Burton\n}}\n'''The Orb''' are an English [[electronic music]] group known for spawning the genre of [[ambient house]]. Founded in 1988 by [[Alex Paterson]] and [[The KLF|KLF]] member [[Jimmy Cauty]], The Orb began as [[ambient music|ambient]] and [[dub music|dub]] [[disc jockey|DJs]] in London. Its early performances were inspired by ambient and electronic artists of the 1970s and 1980s, most notably [[Brian Eno]] and [[Kraftwerk]]. Because of its [[Psychedelic experience|trippy]] sound, the Orb developed a cult following among [[nightclub|clubbers]] \"coming down\" from drug-induced highs.<ref name=\"guardian-chills\">{{cite web|work=[[The Guardian]]|last=Hodgkinson |first=Will |date=2003-01-31 |url=http://www.theguardian.com/culture/2003/jan/31/artsfeatures2 |title=Chills and thrills |accessdate=2007-03-20}}</ref> The Orb has maintained its drug-related and [[List of science fiction themes|science fiction themes]] despite personnel changes, including the departure of Cauty and other Orb members [[Kris Weston]], Andy Falconer, [[Simon Phillips (producer)|Simon Phillips]],  Nick Burton and [[Andy Hughes]]. Paterson has been the only permanent member, continuing to work as the Orb with the [[Switzerland|Swiss]]-German producer [[Thomas Fehlmann]] and, later, with [[Killing Joke|Killing Joke's]] [[Martin \"Youth\" Glover]] and Tim Bran of [[Dreadzone]].<ref name=\"amg-dream\">{{cite web|url = http://www.allmusic.com/album/the-dream-mw0000787912 |title = The Dream > Review |work = [[Allmusic]] |accessdate = 2008-06-11 |last = Bush |first = John}}</ref>\n\nAlex Paterson prides the Orb on manipulating obscure samples beyond recognition on its albums and during its concerts; his unauthorised use of other artists' works has led to disputes with musicians, most notably with [[Rickie Lee Jones]].<ref name=\"remixmag-orblivion\">{{cite web|work=[[Remix Magazine]] |last=Silva |first=Joe |date=2001-02-01 |title=Living in Orblivion |url=http://remixmag.com/mag/remix_living_orblivion/ |accessdate=2007-03-20}}</ref> During its live shows of the 1990s, the Orb performed using digital audio tape machines optimised for live mixing and sampling before switching to laptops and digital media. Despite changes in performance method, the Orb maintained its colourful light shows and psychedelic imagery in concert. These visually intensive performances prompted critics to compare the group to [[Pink Floyd]].<ref>[http://homepage.ntlworld.com/david.bennun/musicint/floyd.html Melody Maker, 1993]</ref>\n\nThe Orb's critical and commercial success in the United Kingdom peaked in the early 1990s with the albums ''[[The Orb's Adventures Beyond The Ultraworld]]'' and ''[[U.F.Orb]]'', the latter of which reached #1 on the [[UK Albums Chart|British album charts]] in 1992. This success led to its infamous appearance on ''[[Top of the Pops]]'', where the group showcased its quirky style by playing [[chess]] (an interest of Paterson's since his early youth) while the group's single \"[[Blue Room (The Orb)|Blue Room]]\" ran in the background. The Orb's mid-1990s albums were met with mixed reactions from British critics; however, its work received praise from American publications such as ''[[Rolling Stone]]''. The group experimented with vocalists on its next two albums, which critics generally described as bland and uninspired. The Orb then shifted gears to a [[minimal techno]] style spearheaded by member Thomas Fehlmann, releasing its new material on the record label [[Kompakt]]."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"225040":{"pageid":225040,"ns":0,"title":"William Orbit","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use British English|date=June 2014}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=June 2014}}\n{{multiple issues|\n{{fanpov|date=August 2012}}\n{{BLP sources|date=March 2011}}\n}}\n\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = William Orbit\n| image               =\n| caption             = William Orbit playing guitar and DJ decks live in the back of a London taxi.\n| landscape           = yes\n| image_size          =\n| background          = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_name          = William Mark Wainwright\n| alias               = William Orbit\n| birth_date          = {{birth date and age|1956|12|15|df=y}}\n| death_date          =\n| origin              = [[Shoreditch]], [[London Borough of Hackney|Hackney]], London, England\n| instrument          = [[Keyboard (instrument)|Keyboards]], guitar\n| genre               = [[Electronica]], [[trip hop]], [[Ambient music|ambient]], [[Trance music|trance]], [[house music|house]], [[downtempo]], [[intelligent dance music|IDM]] \n| occupation          = Composer, record producer\n| years_active        = 1982\u2013present\n| label               = [[IRS Records|IRS]], [[EMI]], [[Virgin Records|Virgin]], N-GRAM, [[Maverick Records|Maverick]], [[Sanctuary Records|Sanctuary]], Kobalt, [[Decca Records|Decca]]\n| associated_acts     = [[Torch Song]], [[Bassomatic]], [[The Supernaturals]]\n| website             = {{URL|http://www.williamorbit.com}}\n}}\n'''William Orbit''' (born '''William Mark Wainwright''', 15 December 1956) is an English musician, composer and record producer. They have released numerous vinyl and digital albums, and gigged in the Netherlands, Belgium and France, as well as the UK. The group has gone through three main lineups, all with core members Andrew Hulme and Roger Horberry. Mark One featured Clare Elliott and Tim Horberry; Mark Two included Dan Mudford, Pete Woodhead, Malcolm McGeorge and Joe Gardiner, and Mark Three featured Rob Jenkins.\n\nReviewers and fans have variously described their sound as \"[[post industrial]]\", \"[[fourth world]]\", \"[[ambient music|ambient]]\", \"[[tribal]]\" and \"[[experimental]]\".  None of these are quite right; O Yuki Conjugate's early influences included [[Cabaret Voltaire (band)|Cabaret Voltaire]] and [[23 Skidoo (band)|23 Skidoo]], before they moved to a more organic sound influenced by [[Jon Hassell]] for their first LP and beyond. Their sound is a mashup of all OYC's influences, and - particularly in their early years - frequently featured looping and found percussion. The band described their 2006 release \"The Euphoria of Disobedience\" as <nowiki>''</nowiki>dirty ambient - multi layered, hyper textural and distinctly gritty<nowiki>''</nowiki>.\n\nThe band is currently enjoying a period of hibernation."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1694273":{"pageid":1694273,"ns":0,"title":"Ott (record Formed at the [[University of Vermont]] in 1983 (with the current line-up solidifying in 1985), the band's four members\u2014[[Trey Anastasio]] (guitars, lead vocals), [[Mike Gordon]] (bass, vocals), [[Jon Fishman]] (drums, percussion, vacuum, vocals), and [[Page McConnell]] (keyboards, vocals)\u2014performed together for nearly 20 years before going on hiatus in August 2004. They reunited in March 2009 for a series of three consecutive concerts played in the [[Hampton Coliseum]] in {{USCity|Hampton|Virginia}}, and have since resumed performing regularly.\n\nPhish's music blends elements of a wide variety of genres,<ref>{{cite web |url=http://phish.net/faq/whatisphish|title= What Is Phish? |accessdate=2011-02-09 |work=FAQ Files|publisher=phish.net}}</ref> including [[rock music|rock]], [[progressive rock]], [[psychedelic rock]], [[hard rock]], [[funk]], [[Folk music|folk]], [[jazz]], and [[blues]]. Although the band has received little radio play or mainstream exposure, Phish has developed a large and dedicated following by word of mouth, the exchange of live recordings, and selling over 8 million albums and DVDs in the United States.<ref name=\"news\">{{cite web | title = News Archives | url = http://phish.com/#/news/index.php?year=2009&hash=story460 |publisher=Phish.com | accessdate = 2011-01-28}}</ref> ''[[Rolling Stone]]'' stated that the band helped to \"...spawn a new wave of bands oriented around group improvisation and super-extended [[groove (music)|groove]]s\".<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.rollingstone.com/artists/phish/biography |title=Phish |accessdate=2008-05-11|work=The New Rolling Stone Album Guide|publisher=rollingstone.com}}</ref> They remain a very popular and successful touring act.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.billboard.com/biz/articles/news/5719306/dave-matthews-band-jams-to-top-of-hot-tours-with-40m-phish-with-18m-grande |title=Dave Matthews Band Jams to Top of Hot Tours with $40M, Phish with $18M; Grande Makes First Appearance |publisher=Billboard |date=2013-09-20 |accessdate=2014-04-11}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"5079506":{"pageid":5079506,"ns":0,"title":"Pink Floyd","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use British English|date=January 2014}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=February 2015}}\n{{pp-vandalism|small=yes}}\n{{pp-move-indef}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name = Pink Floyd\n| image = Pink Floyd - all members.jpg\n| caption = Pink Floyd in January 1968, from the only known photo-shoot of all five members. Clockwise from bottom: Gilmour, Mason, Barrett, Waters, Wright\n| alt = A black and white photo of five men standing in front of a brick wall.\n| landscape = \n| background = group_or_band\n| genre = [[Progressive rock]], [[psychedelic rock]], [[art rock]], [[blues rock]]\n| origin = London, England\n| years_active ={{Start date|1965}}\u2013{{End date|1994}}, {{Start date|2012}}\u20132014<br/><small>(one-off reunion: 2005)</small>\n| label = [[Columbia Graphophone Company|EMI Columbia]], [[Harvest Records|Harvest]], [[Capitol Records|Capitol]], [[Columbia Records|Columbia]], [[EMI]], [[Parlophone Records|Parlophone]]\n| website = {{URL|pinkfloyd.com}}\n| current_members = \n| past_members =\n* [[Nick Mason]]\n* [[Roger Waters]]\n* [[Richard Wright (musician)|Richard Wright]]\n* [[Syd Barrett]]\n* [[David Gilmour]]\n}} <!-- Please discuss at that talk page before changing this -->\n<!--NOTE: UK bands by convention of British English here are described as WERE. Do not use WAS!-->\n\n'''Pink Floyd''' were an English [[Rock music|rock]] band formed in London. They achieved international acclaim with their [[progressive rock|progressive]] and [[psychedelic rock|psychedelic]] music. Distinguished by their use of philosophical lyrics, sonic experimentation, extended compositions and elaborate [[Pink Floyd live performances|live shows]], they are one of the most [[List of best-selling music artists|commercially successful]] and musically influential groups in the history of popular music.\n\nPink Floyd were founded in 1965 by students [[Syd Barrett]], [[Nick Mason]], [[Roger Waters]], and [[Richard Wright (musician)|Richard Wright]]. They gained popularity performing in London's underground music scene during the late 1960s, and under Barrett's leadership released two charting singles and a successful debut album, ''[[The Piper at the Gates of Dawn]]'' (1967). [[David Gilmour]] joined as a fifth member in December 1967; Barrett left the band in April 1968 due to deteriorating [[mental health]] exacerbated by drug use. Waters became the band's primary lyricist and, by the mid-1970s, their dominant songwriter, devising the [[concept album|concepts]] behind their critically and commercially successful albums ''[[The Dark Side of the Moon]]'' (1973), ''[[Wish You Were Here (Pink Floyd album)|Wish You Were Here]]'' (1975), ''[[Animals (Pink Floyd album)|Animals]]'' (1977), ''[[The Wall]]'' (1979) and ''[[The Final Cut (album)|The Final Cut]]'' (1983).\n\nWright left Pink Floyd in 1979, followed by Waters in 1985, declaring it a \"spent force\". Gilmour and Mason continued as Pink Floyd; Wright rejoined them as a session musician and, later, a band member. The three produced two more albums, ''[[A Momentary Lapse of Reason]]'' (1987) and ''[[The Division Bell]]'' (1994), and toured until 1994. After nearly two decades of acrimony, Pink Floyd reunited with Waters in 2005 for a performance at the global awareness event [[Live 8]], but Gilmour and Waters have since stated they have no plans to reunite as a band again. Barrett died in 2006 and Wright in 2008. The final Pink Floyd studio album, ''[[The Endless River]],'' recorded without Waters and based on material recorded in 1993\u20131994, was released in November 2014.\n\nPink Floyd were inducted into the US [[Rock and Roll Hall of Fame]] in 1996, and the [[UK Music Hall of Fame]] in 2005. By 2013, the band had sold more than 250 million records worldwide, including 75 million certified units in the United States."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"28065944":{"pageid":28065944,"ns":0,"title":"Pivot (Australian band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#REDIRECT [[PVT (band)]]"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"407876":{"pageid":407876,"ns":0,"title":"Plastikman","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#REDIRECT [[Richie Hawtin]]\n[[Category:Printworthy redirects]]\n[[Category:Redirects from alternative names]]"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"679066":{"pageid":679066,"ns":0,"title":"Popol Vuh (German band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#REDIRECT [[Popol Vuh (band)]] {{R from merge}}"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"364934":{"pageid":364934,"ns":0,"title":"Porcupine Tree","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = Porcupine Tree\n| image               = Porcupine Tree LIVE in ARENA 2007-11-28.jpg\n| caption             = Porcupine Tree live at Arena, [[Pozna\u0144]], Poland<br/>(28 November 2007).\n| image_size          = \n| landscape           = yes\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[Hemel Hempstead]], [[Hertfordshire]], England\n| genre               = [[Progressive rock]],<ref>{{cite web|author=Steven Wilson |url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/steven-wilson-mn0000455886 |title=Steven Wilson &#124; The band began essentially as a solo project for Wilson, who created all of the band's music. However, by 1993, Wilson desired to work in a band environment, and so brought on frequent collaborators [[Richard Barbieri]] on [[Keyboard instrument|keyboard]]s, [[Colin Edwin]] on [[bass guitar|bass]] and [[Chris Maitland]] on drums as permanent band members. With Wilson still in charge of [[guitar]] and [[lead vocals]], this would remain the lineup until 2001, when the band recruited [[Gavin Harrison]] to replace Maitland on drums.\n\nPorcupine Tree's early sound evokes a style of [[psychedelic rock]] comparable to that of [[progressive rock]] band [[Pink Floyd]]. Upon signing with  [[Kscope]] [[record label]] in the late 1990s, the band approached a more mainstream [[alternative rock]] sound. By the early  2000s, the band signed to a [[major record label]] and shifted their sound again, this time in a more [[progressive metal]] direction.\n\nAfter the release and tour in support of their tenth studio album, ''[[The Incident (album)|The Incident]]'', the band became inactive as Wilson began to focus on his solo career. While not formally broken up, they also have no particular reformation plans beyond \"someday\", with members all working on separate projects, and Wilson committing himself to his solo work through most of 2015."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"3269137":{"pageid":3269137,"ns":0,"title":"Puff Dragon","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"'''Puff Dragon''' is a [[downtempo]] and [[ambient music]] project by Steve Good. Originally from [[Wales]], Steve moved to [[Japan]] in 1995, where he currently lives. Steve's other projects include Double Dragon (psychedelic progressive [[trance music]]), as well as two full length albums: Continuum on London's Phantasm Records (2000), Transparent on Hamburg's Plusquam Records (2002,) and many compilation tracks on trance labels such as Iboga, Spiral Trax International, and Flow. The Double Dragon sound was well received by the global trance party scene{{Fact|date=February 2008}}, and Steve has played live and DJ sets on five continents.\n\nAround 2003, with a conscious effort to slow things down, Good created Puff Dragon. The idea was to create relaxing music for comfortable environments - fusing fat beats with dusty, loungy atmospheres, and natural tribal and [[ethnic]] textures.\n\nThe first full length Puff Dragon album - \"Sazanami\" - was released on Dakini Records in November 2005."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"23890246":{"pageid":23890246,"ns":0,"title":"Port Blue","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#REDIRECT [[Adam Young#Port Blue]]"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"3004241":{"pageid":3004241,"ns":0,"title":"Rabbit in the Moon","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{about|the American band|the mythological rabbit|Moon rabbit}}\n{{confused|Rabbit's Moon|Rabbit moon}}\n{{refimprove|date=September 2010}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Rabbit in the Moon \n| background      = group_or_band\n| origin          = [[Tampa]], [[Florida]]\n| genre           = [[House Music|House]] <br/> [[Breakbeat]] <br> [[Electronica]] <br/> [[Drum and Bass]]\n| years_active    = 1991\u20132010\n| label           = [[Hallucination Recordings]]<br>Southbeat\n| associated_acts = DJ Monk\n| website         = [http://www.rabbitinthemoon.com Rabbit in the Moon]\n| current_members = \n| past_members    = Confucius<br />Bunny<br />DJ Monk\n}}\n\n'''Rabbit in the Moon''' was an American [[electronic music]] group. Please do NOT change \"ARE\" to \"IS\". Thank you. --> an English [[Rock music|rock]] band from [[Abingdon-on-Thames|Abingdon]], Oxfordshire, formed in 1985. The band consists of [[Thom Yorke]] (lead vocals, guitar, piano), [[Jonny Greenwood]] (lead guitar, keyboards, other instruments), [[Colin Greenwood]] (bass), [[Phil Selway]] (drums, percussion, backing vocals) and [[Ed O'Brien]] (guitar, backing vocals).\n\nRadiohead released their debut single \"[[Creep (Radiohead song)|Creep]]\" in 1992. It became a worldwide hit after the release of the band's debut album, ''[[Pablo Honey]]'' (1993). Their popularity rose in the United Kingdom with the release of their second album, ''[[The Bends]]'' (1995). Radiohead's third album, ''[[OK Computer]]'' (1997), propelled them to international fame; featuring an expansive sound and themes of [[social alienation|modern alienation]], ''OK Computer'' is often acclaimed as one of the landmark records of the 1990s<ref>Erlewine, Stephen Thomas. \"[http://www.allmusic.com/album/ok-computer-collectors-series-r1493832 OK Computer]\" Allmusic. Retrieved 31 January 2012</ref> and one of the best albums of all time.<ref>http://www.dailymail.co.uk/tvshowbiz/article-345256/Radioheads-album-best-time--OK.html Radiohead's album best of all time \u2013 OK? \u2013 The Daily Mail</ref><ref>[http://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/music/music-news/8219786/Radioheads-OK-Computer-named-best-album-of-the-past-25-years.html Radiohead's OK Computer named best album of the past 25 years \u2013 The Telegraph]</ref>\n\n''[[Kid A]]'' (2000) and ''[[Amnesiac (album)|Amnesiac]]'' (2001) marked a dramatic evolution in Radiohead's musical style, as they incorporated experimental [[electronic music]], [[krautrock]] and [[jazz]] influences. ''[[Hail to the Thief]]'' (2003), a mix of piano and guitar rock, electronics, and lyrics inspired by war, was the band's final album for their record label, [[EMI]]. Radiohead self-released their seventh album ''[[In Rainbows]]'' (2007) as a [[music download|digital download]] for which customers could set their own price, to critical and chart success. Their eighth album, ''[[The King of Limbs]]'' (2011), was an exploration of rhythm and quieter textures, and was also self-released.\n\nRadiohead have sold more than 30 million albums worldwide.<ref>Jonathan, Emma. [http://www.bbc.co.uk/pressoffice/bbcworldwide/worldwidestories/pressreleases/2011/05_may/radiohead.shtml \"BBC Worldwide takes exclusive Radiohead performance to the world\"]. [[BBC]]. 3 May 2011. Retrieved 15 June 2011.</ref> Their work places highly in both listener polls and critics' lists of the best music of the 1990s and 2000s.<ref>{{cite news |title=Radiohead gun for Beatles' Revolver |publisher=BBC News  |date=3 September 2000 |accessdate=28 September 2008 |url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/entertainment/908638.stm}}</ref><ref>{{cite web| title = Radiohead&nbsp;\u2014 In Rainbows Is Overwhelming Critics Choice for Top Album| url = http://www.contactmusic.com/news.nsf/story/in-rainbows-is-overwhelming-critics-choice-for-top-album_1053848| publisher=Contact Music| date = 18 December 2007| accessdate =3 October 2009}}</ref> In 2011, Radiohead were ranked the third best British artists of all time by ''[[Paste (magazine)|Paste]]'', below only the [[the Beatles|Beatles]] and the [[the Rolling Stones|Rolling Stones]].<ref>[http://www.pastemagazine.com/blogs/lists/2011/04/pastes-50-favorite-british-artists-of-all-time.html?p=5 The 50 Best British Artist of All Time \u2013 Paste Magazine]</ref>  In 2005, they were ranked 73rd in ''[[Rolling Stone]]'''s list of \"The Greatest Artists of All Time\"; They specialize in improvisational experimental [[electronic music]], utilising vintage [[synthesizers]] and sampled sounds alongside [[electric guitar]]. They are also leading exponents of the [[mellotron]] keyboard. More recently they have begun to incorporate Bass Guitar and Drums by varying degrees in an attempt to stretch musical boundaries within the confines of a three piece. Their music has been described alternatively as [[ambient music]], [[space rock]], [[Krautrock]], [[New Age]], [[Berlin School of electronic music|Berlin School]], and various other terms, although the band itself prefers the label \"organic music\". A conversation with [[Peter Andersson (composer)|Peter Andersson]] of Raison d'\u00eatre\". - IKonen magazine, 2004</ref>\nDark ambient atmospheres, [[Drone music|drone]] elements, industrial sounds, ecclesiastical hymns are all blended together to constitute the music of Raison d'\u00eatre. Deeply influenced by the writings of C.G.Jung, Raison d'\u00eatre explores the depths of human psyche providing soundtracks for inner voyages towards the Tragic.\n\nThe music produced by Raison d'\u00eatre is variously [[dark ambient]] and [[soundscape]] in nature. For example, synthesizers might play a droning melody over the sound of metal scraping together. [[Jasen Rauch]] and Andrew Hendrix were the rhythm guitarist and drummer, respectively, at the time of the band's formation. Hendrix was replaced by Hayden Lamb in 2006, who was then replaced by Joe Rickard, who left in 2014. Since their inception, the band has consisted of [[Svein Berge]] and [[Torbj\u00f8rn Brundtland]].\n\nBerge and Brundtland were introduced to each other through a mutual friend in Troms\u00f8, Norway. They both enjoyed the same films, music and both shared an interest in electronics. The two experimented with various forms of electronic music, and bought a drum machine together during the [[Troms\u00f8 techno scene]] before going their separate ways. Several years later, the two met up again and formed R\u00f6yksopp during the [[Bergen Wave]]. After experimenting with different genres of electronic music, the band solidified their place in the electronica scene with their 2001 debut album, ''[[Melody A.M.]]'', released on the [[Wall of Sound (record label)|Wall of Sound]] record label.\n\nR\u00f6yksopp consistently experimented with various genres pertaining to [[electronic music]]. Stylistically, the band makes use of various genres, including [[ambient music|ambient]], [[house music]] and [[synthpop]]. The band is also known for its elaborate concert performances, which often feature eccentric outfits.\n\nSince their 1998 debut, the duo gained critical acclaim and popular success around the world. To date, R\u00f6yksopp has been nominated for one [[Grammy Award]], won seven [[Spellemannprisen]] awards, performed worldwide tours, and produced albums which have topped the charts in several countries, including four consecutive number-one albums in their native Norway."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1402655":{"pageid":1402655,"ns":0,"title":"Saafi Brothers","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"The '''Saafi Brothers''' are a [[downtempo]] music project from [[Germany]], consisting of Gabriel Le Mar and [[Michael Kohlbecker]]. [[Talvin&nbsp;Singh]], [[Sketch Show (band)|Sketch&nbsp;Show]]\n}}\n{{Nihongo|'''Ryuichi Sakamoto'''|\u5742\u672c \u9f8d\u4e00|Sakamoto Ry\u016bichi|born January 17, 1952}} ({{IPA-ja|sakamoto \u027dju\u034d\u02d0it\u0255i}}) is a [[Music of Japan|Japanese musician]], activist, composer, record producer, writer, singer, pianist, and actor based in [[Tokyo]] and [[New York City|New York]]. Gaining major success in 1978 as a member of the [[electronic music]] group [[Yellow Magic Orchestra]] (YMO),<ref name=\"allmusic_ymo\"/><ref name=\"guardian_ymo\"/> Sakamoto served on keyboards and sometimes vocals. The band had worldwide hits such as \"[[Yellow Magic Orchestra (album)|Computer Game / Firecracker]]\" (1978), \"[[Behind the Mask (Yellow Magic Orchestra song)|Behind the Mask]]\" (1978) and \"[[Rydeen]]\" (1979),<ref name=\"crawdaddy\"/> later playing a pioneering role in the [[techno]] and [[acid house]] movements of the 1990s.<ref name=\"UGO\"/>\n\nHe concurrently pursued a solo career, releasing the [[Experimental music|experimental]] electronic [[Fusion (music)|fusion]] album ''[[Thousand Knives]]'' (1978), and later released the pioneering album ''B-2 Unit'' (1980), which included the [[electro music|electro]] classic \"Riot in Lagos\".<ref name=\"broughton_2007\"/><ref name=\"mantronik_interview\"/><ref name=\"wire_1996\"/> From thereon, he produced more solo records, collaborated with many international artists, and pursued a wide variety of projects, such as having composed music for the 1992 [[Barcelona Olympics]] opening ceremony. His composition \"Energy Flow\" (1999) (also known as the alternative title of the single disc ''Ura BTTB'') was the first [[instrumental]] number-one single in Japan's [[Oricon]] charts history.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.allbusiness.com/retail-trade/miscellaneous-retail-retail-stores-not/4608556-1.html|title=Sakamoto's 'energy Flow' Enlivens Japan|publisher=[[AllBusiness.com]]|date=July 2, 1999|accessdate=November 29, 2008}}</ref>\n\n''[[Merry Christmas Mr. Lawrence]]'' (1983) marked his debut as a [[film score]] composer and as an actor. The film's score received a [[British Academy Film Awards|BAFTA Award]],<ref name=\"imdb_sakamoto\"/> and its main theme was adapted into a pop single entitled \"[[Forbidden Colours]]\" which became a worldwide hit. For his work as a film composer, he has won a [[Golden Globe Award]] for ''[[The Sheltering Sky (film)|The Sheltering Sky]]'' (1990),<ref name=\"imdb_sakamoto\"/> plus another Golden Globe, [[Grammy Award|Grammy]], and [[Academy Award]] for ''[[The Last Emperor]]'' (1987).<ref name=\"boston_sullivan\">{{citation|title=RYUICHI SAKAMOTO GOES AVANT-CLASSICAL|work=Boston Globe|author=Jim Sullivan|date=February 8, 1998|page=8|url=http://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/boston/access/26130789.html?FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:FT&type=current&date=Feb+08%2C+1998&author=Jim+Sullivan%2C+Globe+Staff&pub=Boston+Globe&desc=RYUICHI+SAKAMOTO+GOES+AVANT-CLASSICAL|accessdate=May 27, 2011}}</ref> In 2009, he was awarded the [[Ordre des Arts et des Lettres]] from France's [[Minister of Culture (France)|Ministry of Culture]] for his musical contributions.<ref name=\"crawdaddy\">{{cite web|title=What Makes A Legend: Ryuichi Sakamoto|author=Denise Sullivan|work=[[Crawdaddy!]]|date=May 13, 2011|url=http://www.crawdaddy.com/index.php/2011/05/13/what-makes-a-legend-ryuichi-sakamoto/|accessdate=May 31, 2011}}</ref> On occasion, Sakamoto has also worked on [[anime]] and [[video game music|video games]] as a composer as well as a [[scenario writer]]."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1513957":{"pageid":1513957,"ns":0,"title":"Karl Over the course of a decade (and over a dozen recordings) <ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.devinsarno.com/discography.html |title= Devin Sarno Discography |accessdate= November 26, 2009 |work= devinsarno.com}}</ref> his music evolved from high volume feedback experimentation to a sonic examination of the meditative properties of low-end [[drone music]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.laweekly.com/2002-04-25/music/memory-train |title= Memory Train|accessdate= November 26, 2009 |author= Greg Burk |date= May 10, 2005|work= L.A. Satie was a colourful figure in the early 20th century Parisian [[avant-garde]]. His work was a precursor to later artistic movements such as [[minimalism]], [[repetitive music]], and the [[Theatre of the Absurd]].<ref>http://www.gresham.ac.uk/lectures-and-events/erik-satie-his-music-the-vision-his-legacy</ref>\n\nAn eccentric, Satie was introduced as a \"gymnopedist\" in 1887, shortly before writing his most famous compositions, the ''[[Gymnop\u00e9dies]]''. Later, he also referred to himself as a \"phonometrician\" (meaning \"someone who measures sounds\") preferring this designation to that of a \"musician\", after having been called \"a clumsy but subtle technician\" in a book on contemporary French composers published in 1911.<ref>\"{{Lang|fr|Je suis phonom\u00e8tre avant d\u2019\u00eatre musicien\" [http://www.eilpianova.fr/les-spectacles/apercus-phonometriques Aper\u00e7us phonom\u00e9triques & autres sous-entendus]}}{{Dead link|date=April 2010}}</ref>\n\nIn addition to his body of music, Satie also left a remarkable set of writings, having contributed work for a range of publications, from the [[dada]]ist ''[[391 (magazine)|391]]'' to the American culture chronicle ''[[Vanity Fair (American magazine 1913\u201336)|Vanity Fair]]''. Although in later life he prided himself on always publishing his work under his own name, in the late 19th century he appears to have used pseudonyms such as '''{{Lang|fr|Virginie Lebeau}}''' and '''{{Lang|fr|Fran\u00e7ois de Paule}}''' in some of his published writings."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1964036":{"pageid":1964036,"ns":0,"title":"Conrad Schnitzler","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n|name = Conrad Schnitzler\n|image =\n|caption =\n|background = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n|birth_name =\n|alias =\n|birth_date = 17 March 1937\n|death_date = 4 August 2011 (aged 74)\n|origin = Germany\n|instrument = [[Tape recorder]], [[synthesizer]], [[cello]], [[violin]], [[Keyboard instrument|keyboards]], [[drum kit|drums]]\n|genre = [[Electronic music]], [[krautrock]], [[Ambient music|ambient]], [[Berlin School of electronic music|Berlin School]], [[New-age music|new-age]]\n|occupation = [[Sound design]]er<br />[[Musician]]<br />[[Foley artist]]<br />[[Performing artist]]\n|years_active = 1960\u20132011\n|label = [[Schnitzler Private Pressing]]\n|associated_acts = [[Tangerine Dream]]<br />Berlin Express<br />[[Eruption (German band)|Eruption]]<br />[[Kluster]]<br />Mi.T.-CON\n|website = http://www.conrad-schnitzler.de\n}}\n'''Conrad (\"Conny\") Schnitzler''' (17 March 1937 \u2013 4 August 2011) was a prolific German [[experimental music]]ian. [[Germans|German]] [[electronic music]] [[composer]] and [[electronic musician|musician]]. He also used the alias '''Richard Wahnfried'''. He was briefly a member of the electronic bands [[Tangerine Dream]] and [[Ash Ra Tempel]] before launching a solo career consisting of more than 60 albums released across five decades.\nIn 2002, two Klaus Schulze albums (''[[Mirage (Klaus Schulze album)|Mirage]]'' and ''[[Timewind]]'') were included in 25 Most Influential Ambient Albums Of All Time."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"972407":{"pageid":972407,"ns":0,"title":"Scorn (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Unreferenced|date=June 2009}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name             = Scorn\n| image              = \n| caption         = Left-Right: Nicholas Bullen, Mick Harris\n| image_size         = \n| background       = group_or_band\n| alias            = \n| origin           = [[Birmingham]], England, United Kingdom\n| genre            =  [[Electronic music]], [[Industrial music|industrial]], [[Dub music|dub]], [[Ambient music|dark ambient]], [[Experimental music|experimental]], [[industrial metal]] (early) \n| years_active     = 1991\u20132011\n| label            = [[Resist Records|Resist]]/[[OHM Resistance]], [[Vivo Records|Vivo]], [[Hymen Records|Hymen]], [[Ant-Zen]], [[Invisible Records|Invisible]], [[KK Records|KK]], [[Possible Records|Possible]], [[Earache Records|Earache]], [[Combat Recordings]]\n| associated_acts  = [[Napalm Death]]\n| current_members  = \n| past_members     = [[Mick Harris]]<br/>[[Nicholas Bullen]]<br/>[[Justin Broadrick]]<br/>[[James Plotkin]]\n}}\n'''Scorn''' was an English [[electronic music]] project. The group was formed in the early 1990s as a side project of former [[Napalm Death]] members [[Mick Harris]] and [[Nicholas Bullen|Nic Bullen]] (the latter as one of the founding members of the band in 1981). Bullen left the group in 1995 and the project continued on until the end of 2011 as an essentially solo project for Harris.\n\nSince their early years, Scorn is often associated with [[industrial music|industrial]] and experimental music, particularly with their early releases as a duo with much of their [[Earache Records]]-era output. Since the departure of Bullen, much of the output has been minimalist beats with an emphasis on very deep bass lines, often resembling [[Dub music|dub]] and [[trip-hop]] in structure. The departure from their early sound eventually led to Harris parting ways with Earache after the ''[[Logghi Barogghi]]'' release, both sides apparently having been unhappy with how the project was being handled."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"19508":{"pageid":19508,"ns":0,"title":"Murat Ses","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"[[File:Murat Ses, Florida (USA).png|thumb| Murat Ses at Dal\u00ed Museum St Petersburg - Florida (USA) 2012 by \u00d6pBe]]\n'''Murat Ses''' (''Ses means '''sound''' or '''voice''' in [[Turkish language|Turkish]]'') (born 1946, [[Bayrakli]], [[Izmir]], [[Turkey]]) is a [[Turkey|Turkish]] [[Keyboard instrument|keyboard]] player and [[composer]] with strong [[Eurasian Avars|Eurasian]] electronic elements. He is creator of the Anadolu Pop style, a synthesis of Anatolian Music and Western elements that has been influencing [[Turkish music]] scene for decades.\n\nHe worked with several bands: Meteorlar (Meteors) (1966-1967), [[Sil\u00fcetler]] (Silhouette) (1967), [[Mo\u011follar]] (Mongols) (1967-1972), [[Bar\u0131\u015f Man\u00e7o]] and Kurtalan Ekspres (Express) (1973-1974), [[Edip Akbayram]] and Dostlar (Friends) (1974) and [[Cem Karaca]] and Dervi\u015fan (Dervishes) (1975-1976). Also, he founded A\u011fr\u0131 Da\u011f\u0131 Efsanesi (Legend of [[Mount Ararat]]) band. This band was dissolved in 1976 and 3 45 rpms. He migrated to [[Austria]] in 1979.  \n\nHis [[album]] ''Danses et Rythmes de la Turquie d'hier \u00e0 aujourd'hui'' was awarded the [[Grand Prix du Disque]] by the [[Charles Cros Academie]] in [[Paris]], [[France]] with [[Mo\u011follar]]. The albums ''Automaton (Slave with Ewer Device)'', ''Binfen (feat.Tan)'' and ''Culduz'', all released in the 1990s, are parts of a [[trilogy]] with the concept: \"The Timeless and Boundaryless Context of Culture and Civilization\". Ses has had excellent press (US Keyboard, Audion, i/e, Expose ...) and airplay (Automaton\u00b2 was no.1 in Rhode Island, Binfen no.7 in Ohio). His main influences are [[Pink Floyd]], [[Traffic (band)|Traffic]], [[Jimmy Smith (musician)|Jimmy Smith]], Eastern Mediterranean music, [[Levant]]ine, and [[Central Asia]]n cultures and music. He is the most important Turkish artist still internationally active and shaping today's independent [[electronic music]] scene.\n\nHis earlier (late 60s early 70s) psychedelic-[[Anatolia]]n works with [[English language|English]] [[lyrics]] released under [[United States|US]], [[Netherlands|Dutch]], [[Germany|German]] and [[Canada|Canadian]] labels in the late 1990s through 2002. Murat's album with his \"San Francisco/Miami Impressions\" was recorded in [[Miami, Florida]] and was published in 2005 as Automaton\u00b2 (Automaton Squared) followed by \"Binfen 2005 Remix\", \"Electric Levantine\" (2006), \"Umami\" (2007), \"Beside the Sun\" (2010), \"Light Cone\" (2012) and \"Sundial\" (2013).  His newest release is \"Kiosk Torba\" (2014), his eleventh solo album in a row.\n\nIn the early 1990s Murat Ses developed a [[music genre|musical style]] he terms ''Electric Levantine''.  The main elements of the style are microtonal properties created on authentic [[Levant]]ine scales, electronically produced instrument timbres and Western music. It's an experimental form of ''Anadolu Pop''. His typical ''Electric Levantine'' sound can be heard on his album ''AUTOMATON (Slave with Ewer Device)'' and on the subsequent albums of his 90's trilogy.\n\nIn 2007 Advertising agency [[TBWA]] decided to use the early 70s Mo\u011follar song 'Garip \u00c7oban' (meaning Poor Shepherd in Turkish), composed by Murat Ses, in [[PlayStation 3]] campaigns commercial."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2716271":{"pageid":2716271,"ns":0,"title":"Shadowfax (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Shadowfax\n| image               = P16329FBAAR.jpg\n| image_size          = 200\n| caption             = Photo by Sam Emerson.\n| background          = group_or_band\n| alias               =\n| origin              = [[Chicago]], [[USA]]\n| genre               = [[Chamber jazz]]<br>[[New-age music|New-age]]<br>[[electronic music|Electronic]]<br>[[Blues]]\n| years_active        = 1972\u20131995\n| label               = [[ABC Records|Passport/ABC]]<br>[[Windham Hill]]<br>[[Capitol Records|Capitol]]<br>[[Private Music]]<br>[[Sonic Images]]\n| associated_acts     =\n| website             =\n| current_members     =\n| past_members        = [[#Members|See \"Members\"]]\n| notable_instruments = [[Lyricon]]\n}}\n\n'''Shadowfax''' was a [[new age]]/[[electronic music|electronic]] musical group formed in Chicago in the early 1970s and best known for their albums ''[[Shadowfax (album)|Shadowfax]]'' and ''[[Folksongs for a Nuclear Village]]''. In 1989 they won the Grammy for Best New Age Performance for ''Folksongs for a Nuclear Village''.<ref>Yurochko (1993) pp. 225-226</ref> In 1993, they were nominated for the Grammy for ''[[Esperanto (Shadowfax album)|Esperanto]]''.\n\nThe group formed in 1972<ref>Larkin (1995) p.3727</ref> and disbanded after 1995 when [[Lyricon]] player and leader [[Chuck Greenberg (musician)|Chuck Greenberg]] died of a heart attack. Having lost their signature sound, Shadowfax's members went on to other projects.\n\nThe group takes its name from [[Gandalf the Grey]]'s horse [[Shadowfax (Middle-earth)|Shadowfax]] in [[J. R. R. Tolkien]]'s ''[[The Lord of the Rings]]''."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"780623":{"pageid":780623,"ns":0,"title":"Jonah Sharp","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Redirect|Spacetime Continuum|the space-time continuum|Spacetime}}\n'''Jonah Sharp''' alias '''Spacetime Continuum''' is a producer, remixer, and DJ of [[electronic music]].<ref name=\"NYT\">{{Cite news |url=http://www.nytimes.com/1995/01/04/arts/critic-s-notebook-dance-music-for-the-immobile.html?pagewanted=1 |first=Neil |last=Strauss |date=4 January 1995 |title=Critic's Notebook: Dance music for the immobile |publisher=New York Times }}</ref>  After starting his musical career as a [[jazz]] drummer in [[London]], [[UK]], he moved to [[San Francisco]], [[USA]].<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.sfgate.com/cgi-bin/article.cgi?f=/c/a/2002/02/26/DD44035.DTL&type=printable |title=Club kids tell their stories at monthly Bored collective |first=Neva |last=Chonin |date=26 February 2002 |publisher=San Francisco Chronicle |accessdate=23 January 2010 }}</ref>  During the 1990s Sharp released a series of albums on the [[Astralwerks]] record label.  The first of these, entitled ''[[Alien Dreamtime]]'',<ref name=\"NYT\"/> featured a live recording of [[ethnobotany|ethnobotanist]], writer and [[Psychedelia|psychedelic]] [[researcher]] [[Terence McKenna]] delivering a series of lectures to the accompaniment of Spacetime Continuum music.<ref>{{Cite news |url=http://www.wired.com/beyond_the_beyond/2007/02/research_that_u/ |publisher=Wired |first=Bruce |last=Sterling |title=RE/SEARCH, that unique, time-honored service from San Francisco\u2019s Bohemia |accessdate=23 January 2010 |date=6 February 2007}}</ref>  Sharp's subsequent albums combined experimental electronic music with subtle jazz elements and elaborate [[rhythm]] structures.  His work has had a clear influence on contemporary [[psybient]] artists, such as [[Shpongle]] and others.\n\nJonah Sharp has also released collaborations with [[Tetsu Inoue]], [[Bill Laswell]], [[Mixmaster Morris]], [[Pete Namlook]], [[David Moufang]], and [[Plaid (band)|Plaid]].
