The group includes [[Simon Posford]] (aka [[Hallucinogen (musician)|Hallucinogen]]) and [[Raja Ram (musician)|Raja Ram]] (one third of [[The Infinity Project]]). The duo are considered to be one of the progenitors of the [[psybient]] genre - a genre combining [[world music]] with [[psychedelic trance]] and [[ambient music|ambient]]. Their musical style combines traditional music from all over the globe and vocals with contemporary western synthesizer-based psychedelic music. When asked to describe Shpongle's music, Posford has responded that it is \"like nothing you've ever heard before.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.myspace.com/therealshpongle |title=SHPONGLE &#124; Listen and Stream Free Music, Albums, New Releases, Photos, Videos |publisher=Myspace.com |date= |accessdate=2014-07-25}}</ref> Shpongle's first track, \"Vapour Rumours\", was released on [[TIP World|TIP Records']] ''Infinite Excursions'' compilation in 1996.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.discogs.com/release/48877 |title=Various - Infinite Excursions - Softer Psychedelic Sounds (CD) at Discogs |publisher=Discogs.com |date= |accessdate=2014-07-25}}</ref> Their debut album, ''[[Are You Shpongled?]]'', was released in 1998 on [[Twisted Records (UK)|Twisted Records]]. On September 9th, 2014, Simon Posford confirmed that work has begun on a sixth album.\n\nPosford is generally responsible for the synthesizers, studio work, and live instrumentation while Raja Ram contributes broad musical concepts and [[flute]] arrangements. Raja Ram stated in an interview that \"Shpongle\" is an umbrella term for feeling positive and euphoric emotions.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nme.com/artists/shpongle|title=Shpongle Biography|publisher=NME|accessdate=17 December 2009}} {{Dead link |date=April 2013}}</ref>  Shpongle's music is heavily influenced by [[psychedelic experience]]s and frequently makes use of sonic textures that approximate psychedelic states as well as vocal samples relating to consciousness expansion, hallucinations, and altered states of awareness. For example, the track, \"A New Way to Say 'Hooray,'\" contains a vocal sample of [[Terence McKenna]] describing the effects of [[Dimethyltryptamine|DMT]], and the most popular song from their first album, 'Divine Moments of Truth', alludes to the abbreviation DMT."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1370171":{"pageid":1370171,"ns":0,"title":"Yaniv Shulman","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#redirect [[Shulman (band)]]"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1307950":{"pageid":1307950,"ns":0,"title":"Michael Shrieve","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = Michael Shrieve\n| birth_date                = {{birth date and age|1949|07|06|df=yes}}\n|birth_place =[[San Francisco]], [[California]], [[United States]]\n| instrument          = Drums, percussion\n| origin              = [[San Francisco]], [[California]], [[United States]]\n| years_active        = 1965-present\n| associated_acts     = [[Santana (band)|Santana]]<br>[[Hagar Schon Aaronson Shrieve]]<br>[[Klaus Schulze]]<br>[[Go (band)|Go]]\n| background=non_vocal_instrumentalist\n}}\n\n'''Michael Shrieve''' (born July 6, 1949, in [[San Francisco]]) is an [[United States|American]] [[drummer]], [[percussionist]], and later, an [[electronic music]] composer. He is best known as the [[drummer]] in [[Santana (band)|Santana]], playing on their first eight albums from 1969 through 1974.<ref name=\"DrummerWorld\">{{cite web  | title = Michael Shrieve bio | publisher = Drummerworld.com | url = http://www.drummerworld.com/drummers/Michael_Shrieve.html | accessdate = 2010-04-06 }}</ref> His performance at the 1969 [[Woodstock festival]], when he was 20 years old, made him one of the youngest musicians to perform at the festival. Shrieve's [[drum solo]] during an extended version of \"[[Soul Sacrifice]]\" in the ''[[Woodstock (film)|Woodstock]]'' film has been described as \"electrifying\".<ref name=\"GreatRockDrummers\">{{cite book | last= Cianci |first = Bob| title = Great Rock Drummers of the Sixties | date=1 July 2006 |publisher= Hal Leonard |isbn=0-634-09925-6 |page=215}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"23961071":{"pageid":23961071,"ns":0,"title":"The Sight Below","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=August 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist  <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = The Sight Below\n| image                 = Tsbnode.jpg\n| caption            = The Sight Below performing a live audio/visual set at NODE Festival in [[Modena]], Italy June 6, 2009\n| image_size            = 210\n| landscape           = Yes\n| background          = group_or_band\n| alias               = \n| origin              = [[Seattle]], Washington, United States\n| instrument          = Guitar, laptop\n| genre               = [[Intelligent dance music|Ambient techno]], [[shoegazing]], [[electronic music|electronic]]\n| occupation          = Producer, composer, musician\n| years_active        = 2008&ndash;present\n| label               = [[Ghostly International]]\n| associated_acts     = [[Rafael Anton Irisarri]]<br>[[Simon Scott (drummer)|Simon Scott]]<br>[[Benoit Pioulard]]<br>[[Orcas_(duo)|ORCAS]]<br>[[Pantha Du Prince]]<br>[[TNAF]]<br>[[School of Seven Bells]]<br>[[Tiny Vipers]]<br>[[Biosphere (musician)|Biosphere]]\n| website                 = http://www.myspace.com/thesightbelow\n| notable_instruments = \n}}\n\n'''The Sight Below''' is an American [[Intelligent dance music|ambient techno]]/[[Shoegazing|shoegaze]] act from [[Seattle]], Washington. Its main member is the American [[Minimalist music|post-minimalist]] composer [[Rafael Anton Irisarri]]. \n\nSam Valenti IV signed The Sight Below to his [[Ghostly International]] imprint in 2008 after listening to a [[demo tape]]. A promotional EP ''[[No Place for Us]]'' was soon released by the label as a free MP3 download on August 26, 2008.<ref>[http://www.wired.com/listening_post/2008/09/mp3s-the-sight/] {{dead link|date=January 2015}}</ref> \n\nThe Sight Below debuted its live set at Seattle's [[KEXP]] radio station on September 20, 2008.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://kexp.org/live/liveperformance.aspx?rID=27971|title=KEXP 90.3 FM - Live performance by The Sight Below on 9/20/2008|publisher=Kexp.org|accessdate=January 17, 2015}}</ref> The in-studio session was recorded and is available on Ghostly's website as a [[podcast]] ([http://static.ghostly.com/media/mp3/podcast_player/podcastplayer.html GhostlyCast #18]).<ref>[http://static.ghostly.com/media/mp3/podcast_player/podcastplayer.html] {{dead link|date=January 2015}}</ref> A well-received performance followed at the Ghostly International showcase during [[Decibel Festival]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://lineout.thestranger.com/lineout/archives/2008/09/28/decibel-the-sight-below-audion-carl-craig/|title=Decibel: The Sight Below, Audion, Carl Craig|publisher=Lineout.thestranger.com|accessdate=January 17, 2015}}</ref>  These performances paved the way for an extensive European tour that saw the artist perform at 18 different cities in the continent, including [[Unsound festival]] in [[Krakow, Poland]], EME Festival in [[Lisbon, Portugal]], [[Soy Festival|S.O.Y. Festival]] in [[Nantes]], France and TimeZones Festival in [[Bari]], Italy.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.residentadvisor.net/news.aspx?id=9799|title=RA News: The Sight Below releases debut, tours|work=Resident Advisor|accessdate=January 17, 2015}}</ref>\n\nThe Sight Below's debut album ''[[Glider (The Sight Below album)|Glider]]'' was released in the United States on November 2008 and January 2009 worldwide. It is available as both a physical and digital release. The album was very well received by the press and music community, including praise from [[Radiohead]]'s [[Thom Yorke]], who charted \"At First Touch\" on his January 6, 2009 [http://www.radiohead.com/deadairspace/index.php?a=461 \"Office Chart\"] posting on the band's website [[Dead Air Space]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.radiohead.com/deadairspace/index.php?a=461|title=RADIOHEAD|work=RADIOHEAD.COM - DEAD AIR SPACE|accessdate=January 17, 2015}}</ref>\n\n''[[Murmur EP]]'' followed in 2009, including remixes by [[Biosphere (musician)|Biosphere]], [[Eluvium (musician)|Eluvium]] and [[Simon Scott (drummer)|Simon Scott]] (of [[Slowdive]]). \n\nThe Sight Below's second full-length, ''[[It All Falls Apart]],'' was released on April 6, 2010. It features music written with the aforementioned Simon Scott and a cover version of [[Joy Division]]'s \"[[New Dawn Fades]]\" (with guest vocals by [[Tiny Vipers]]). Described by [[All Music Guide]] as ''\"impeccably made ambient thump-and-drone\"'', [[Pitchfork Media]] called it ''\"A beautifully bleak cloud of sound\"'' while [[XLR8R]] magazine gave it a 9/10 ranking and praised it as ''\"an astounding range of visceral sonic possibilities\u2026a hurricane passing over an ocean, gathering heat and force while simultaneously cooling the waters below.\"''"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"148705":{"pageid":148705,"ns":0,"title":"Sigur R\u00f3s","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use dmy dates|date=February 2015}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name = Sigur R\u00f3s\n| image = Sigur Ros at Madison Square Garden.jpg\n| caption = Sigur R\u00f3s performing at [[Madison Square Garden]] in 2013.\n| background = group_or_band\n| origin = [[Reykjav\u00edk]], Iceland\n| genre = [[Post-rock]]\n| years_active = 1994\u2013present\n| label = [[Fat Cat Records|Fat Cat]], [[Geffen Records|Geffen]], [[EMI]], [[XL Recordings|XL]], [[Bad Taste (record label)|Smekkleysa]]\n| associated_acts = [[Amiina]], [[J\u00f3nsi & Alex]], [[J\u00f3nsi]], [[The Album Leaf]]\n| website = {{URL|sigur-ros.co.uk}}\n| current_members = [[J\u00f3nsi|J\u00f3n \u00de\u00f3r Birgisson]]{{br}}[[Georg H\u00f3lm]]{{br}}[[Orri P\u00e1ll D\u00fdrason]]\n| past_members = [[\u00c1g\u00fast \u00c6var Gunnarsson]]{{br}}[[Kjartan Sveinsson]]\n}}\n'''Sigur R\u00f3s''' ({{IPA-is|\u02c8s\u026a\u02d0\u0263\u028fr \u02c8ro\u02d0us|-|Sigur ros.ogg}} {{respell|SIG|\u0259r rohss}}<ref name=\"pronunciation\">{{cite web |url= http://www.sigur-ros.co.uk/band/pronunci.php| title=pronunciation |accessdate=2014-03-24 |publisher=sigur-ros.co.uk}}</ref>) is an [[Iceland]]ic [[post-rock]] band from [[Reykjav\u00edk]], which has been active since 1994. Montana Skies seemingly non-stop tour schedule has taken them all across the US as well as to Canada, Asia, and Russia; and their dedication to their musical vision has helped them build an enthusiastic grassroots fan base along the way. The duo formed in [[Austin, Texas]] in 1993 and they list among their influences [[Minimalist music|minimalist]] and [[Electronic art music|electronic composers]] such as [[Arvo P\u00e4rt]], [[Zbigniew Preisner]], [[Gavin Bryars]], and [[Henryk G\u00f3recki]], as well as [[Talk Talk]], [[post-rock]] artists [[Labradford]], and ambient innovator [[Brian Eno]]. Their compositions are largely beatless soundscapes, composed of droning, effects-treated guitars along with piano, strings, and horns; volume swells and feedback fill the gap of rhythmic instruments, providing dynamic movement. Their sound has been described as \"divine, classical drone without the tedious intrusion of drums or vocals.\"<ref>Southern Records. See page entitled 'Template:Infobox musical artist' for details.-->Thorsten Quaeschning<br>[[Hoshiko Yamane]]<br>[[Ulrich Schnauss]]{{cn|date=January 2015}}\n| past_members    = <!--DO NOT CHANGE ORDER OF MEMBERS! See page entitled 'Template:Infobox musical artist' for details.-->[[Edgar Froese]]<!--This section is for names only. Do not add 'deceased' here.--><br>Lanse Hapshash<br>Kurt Herkenberg<br>Volker Hombach<br>Charlie Prince<br>[[Steve Jolliffe]]<br>[[Klaus Schulze]]<br>[[Conrad Schnitzler]]<br>[[Christopher Franke]]<br>Steve Schroyder<br>[[Peter Baumann]]<br>[[Michael Hoenig]]<br>Klaus Kr\u00fcger<br>[[Johannes Schmoelling]]<br>[[Paul Haslinger]]<br>[[Ralf Wadephul]]<br>[[Jerome Froese]]<br>[[Linda Spa]]<br>Iris Camaa<br>[[Bernhard Beibl]]<!--Do not add touring musicians to this list. They were not official members of the band.-->\n}}\n'''Tangerine Dream''' was a German [[electronic music]] group founded in 1967 by [[Edgar Froese]]. The band underwent many personnel changes over the years, with Froese being the only continuous member. Drummer and composer [[Klaus Schulze]] was briefly a member of an early lineup, but the most stable version of the group, during their influential mid-1970s period, was as a trio with Froese, [[Christopher Franke]], and [[Peter Baumann]]. In the late 1970s, [[Johannes Schmoelling]] replaced Baumann, and this lineup, too, was stable and extremely productive.\n\nTangerine Dream released more than one hundred albums. Their early \"Pink Years\" albums had a pivotal role in the development of [[Krautrock]]. Their \"Virgin Years\" albums helped define what became known as the [[Berlin School of electronic music]]. These and later albums were influential in the development of [[electronic dance music]], and also the genre known as [[new-age music]], though the band themselves disliked the term. From the late 1990s into the 2000s, Tangerine Dream also explored some styles of [[electronica]].\n\nAlthough the group released numerous studio and live recordings, a substantial number of their fans were introduced to Tangerine Dream by their film soundtracks, which total over sixty and include ''[[Sorcerer (film)|Sorcerer]],'' ''[[Thief (film)|Thief]],'' ''[[The Keep (film)|The Keep]],'' ''[[Risky Business]],'' ''[[Firestarter (film)|Firestarter]],'' ''[[Legend (1985 film)|Legend]],'' ''[[Near Dark]],'' ''[[Shy People]]'', and ''[[Miracle Mile (film)|Miracle Mile]]''. They most recently composed the original score for the video game ''[[Grand Theft Auto V]]''."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"583950":{"pageid":583950,"ns":0,"title":"Team Sleep","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Refimprove|date=October 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name = Team Sleep\n| image = Chino Moreno live.jpg\n| caption = Vocalist Chino Moreno performing live\n| image_size = \n| background = group_or_band\n| origin = [[Sacramento, California]], United States\n| genre = \n| years_active = 2000\u2013present\n| label = [[Maverick Records]]\n| associated_acts = [[Deftones]], Tinfed, [[Hella (band)|Hella]],  [[Pinback]], [[Helium (band)|Helium]], [[Phallucy (Band)|Phallucy]], Decibel Devils, [[Mike Patton]], [[Smashing Pumpkins]], [[Goon Moon]], [[Crosses (band)]], [[Death Grips]]\n| current_members = [[Chino Moreno]]<br />Todd Wilkinson<br />DJ Crook<br />Rick Verret<br />Chuck Doom<br />[[Gil Sharone]]\n| past_members = [[Zach Hill]]\n}}\n\n'''Team Sleep''' is an American [[experimental rock|experimental]] [[alternative rock]]/[[post-rock]] group led by singer/guitarist [[Chino Moreno]]. Her work critically combines themes of [[identity politics]] - including [[gender]], [[human sexuality|sexuality]], [[Social class|class]], [[linguistics]], [[ethnicity]] and [[Race (classification of human beings)|race]] - with an ongoing critique of the socio-economics of commercial media production. The band, who are also well known in Europe, play [[improvisation]]al pieces of up to an hour in length that explore the development and demise of repeating musical figures. The band's 17th album ''Open'' was released in late 2013.<ref name=\"Dean\">{{cite news|title=Are The Necks the best band in the world?|url=http://theconversation.com/are-the-necks-the-best-band-in-the-world-21088?utm_medium=email&utm_campaign=Latest+from+The+Conversation+for+16+December+2013&utm_content=Latest+from+The+Conversation+for+16+December+2013+CID_dadc7299240c9f9e5e7e02f449023d0c&utm_source=campaign_monitor&utm_term=Are%20The%20Necks%20the%20best%20band%20in%20the%20world|accessdate=15 December 2013|newspaper=The Conversation Australia|date=13 December 2013|author=Dean Biron}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"19400235":{"pageid":19400235,"ns":0,"title":"Robert Scott Thompson","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{multiple issues|\n{{BLP sources|date=December 2009}}\n{{No footnotes|date=December 2009}}\n}}\n\n'''Robert Scott Thompson''' (born 1959, California) is a [[composer]] of [[Ambient music|ambient]], [[instrumental]] and [[electroacoustic music]].  He earned the [[Bachelor of music|B.Mus.]] degree from the [[University Of Oregon|University of Oregon]] and [[Master of Arts (postgraduate)|M.A.]] and [[Ph.D.]] degrees from the [[UCSD|University of California at San Diego]].  His primary teachers include [[Bernard Rands]], [[Roger Reynolds]], [[Joji Yuasa]] and F. Richard Moore.  He creates work in a wide variety of forms ranging from [[chamber music|chamber]] and [[orchestral music]] to works for the [[virtuoso]] [[solo (music)|soloist]], [[computer music]], and experimental [[video art]].\n\nHe is the recipient of many prizes and distinctions for his music including the First Prize in [http://www.musica.cz/musnova/MN03-FIN.htm Musica Nova] 2003 (Czech Republic), First Prize in the 2001 Pierre Schaeffer competition (Italy) and awards in the XVI Concorso Internazionale \u201cLuigi Russolo\u201d (Italy), [http://www.jml-irino.jp/IrinoPrize/IrinoPWinner1991_2000.html Irino Prize Foundation Competition 1995] for chamber Music (Japan), and [http://www.imeb.net/MFLi/index.php?option=com_content&task=view&id=909&Itemid=194 Concours International de Musique Electroacoustique de Bourges (France)], among others.  He was a Research Assistant of the [http://www.jstor.org/pss/3680355 Center for Music Experiment (CME)Computer Audio Research Lab (CARL)] throughout the 1980s, assisting significant composers in the realization of advanced computer music works.\n\nIn 1991, he was named a [[Fulbright Research Fellowship|Fulbright Research Scholar]] and was Composer in Residence at the [http://www.musik-kons.dk/english/diem/index.php Danish Institute of Electroacoustic Music (DIEM)] where he collaborated on fundamental research and composed the long-form computer music work \u2013 ''The Strong Eye''.  Over the past decade, he has become increasingly well known internationally for his instrumental and computer music works and also for his many recordings which have been broadcast worldwide.\n\nHis music is published on recordings by [http://www.emfmedia.org/ EMF-Media], [http://www.neumarecords.com/ Neuma], Drimala, [http://www.capstonerecords.org/ Capstone], [[Hypnos (record label)|Hypnos]], [http://www.oasisproductions.com/ Oasis/Mirage], Groove, [http://www.lensrecords.com/ Lens Records], [http://www.spaceformusic.com/ Space for Music], Zero Music and [http://www.aucourantrecords.com/ Aucourant] record labels, among others.\n\nWhile composing and recording takes up most of his creative time, he is also involved in various tangent activities.  He is active as a composer for films and often collaborates as an audio mastering engineer, creating master recordings for labels such as Funtone and [[Composers Recordings, Inc.|CRI (Composer's Recordings, Inc.)]].  On the technical side, he has collaborated with Micro Technology Unlimited, and assisted in the development of [http://www.mtu.com/basics/noiseremove.htm DNOISE] \u2013 a real-time digital audio noise reduction software application.\n\nHe is a contributing author for two books, ''Computer Music Techniques for the Electronic Musician'' and ''Software Synthesis, Sound Design and Programming'', both by Dr. Eduardo Reck Miranda and published by Focal Press in 1998 and 2002 respectively.  He is currently under contract for a book with [http://www.areditions.com/ A-R Editions, Inc.] on the subject of musical signal processing and sonic design using Csound 5.  He was named the Distinguished Honor\u2019s Professor of Georgia State University, College of Arts and Sciences in 1994 where he is Professor of Music Composition and Coordinator of Music Technology Studies in the School of Music."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"327220":{"pageid":327220,"ns":0,"title":"TimeShard","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{multiple issues|\n{{Refimprove|date=July 2010}}\n{{Notability|date=July 2010}}\n}}\n\n'''Time Shard''' were one of the innovators in underground [[United Kingdom|UK]] electronic [[dance music]] during the 'second summer of love' in 1989.  During their first five years Gobber, Psi and Angstrom became known as one of the UK's first live '[[acid house]]' acts,<ref>Bush, John [http://www.allmusic.com/artist/timeshard-p182876 \"became known as the area's first live acid-house band.\"], ''All Music Guide''</ref> during this time they developed a sound which (later) became known as [[Psychedelic trance]] although at the time they were often described as producing Ambient or Shamanic Trance music.\n\nTheir early music was a synthesis of [[Dub (music)|dub]] with the pulsating sounds of [[Kraftwerk]] and on slower pieces the influence of [[Brian Eno]] is in evidence. Their signature sound of analogue synthesizers, sequencers and drum machines overlaid with glissando guitars and an [[electric sitar]] player became popular as  music magazine publishers struggled to deal with the new rift between [[rock and roll]] and the burgeoning [[house music]] music.   Time Shard built a devoted following among the mixture of punks and Acid House followers which flocked to Britain's fields during this period.\n\nTheir initial successes were on the UK's free - festival circuit, which was in a period of transition and fusion as acid house fans found a place to dance (initially) without restriction, outside mainstream club culture, which had yet to develop the 'superclubs' such as [[Cream (nightclub)|Cream]].\n\nIn later years (1996- ) they fell victim to the UK's criminal justice bill which killed many venues, this, combined with the fragile financial health of their record company [[Planet Dog]] urged them to take to the web, where they became one of the first groups to attempt distribution of MP3 files, striking a deal with webmusic distribution pioneers e-music.\n\nIn recent years they have been quiet, but still maintain a web page at http://www.timeshard.com."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"89580":{"pageid":89580,"ns":0,"title":"Amon Tobin","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=December 2014}}\n{{good article}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n|name = Amon Tobin\n|image = Amon tobin luxemburg.jpg\n|caption = Tobin performing live in [[Luxembourg (city)|Luxembourg City]]\n|landscape = yes\n||background = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n|birth_name = Amon Adonai Santos de Ara\u00fajo Tobin\n|alias = Cujo\n|birth_date = {{birth date and age|1972|2|7}}\n|death_date = \n|origin = [[Rio de Janeiro]], Brazil\n|instrument = Synthesizers, keyboards, guitar, bass, drums, [http://www.amontobin.com/ amontobin.com]\n}}\n'''Amon Adonai Santos de Ara\u00fajo Tobin''' (born February 7, 1972), known as '''Amon Tobin''', is a [[Brazilian people|Brazilian]] musician, composer and producer of [[electronic music]].<ref name=allbrazint>{{cite web | url=http://www.allbrazilianmusic.com/en/Servicos/ParaImprimir.asp?Nu_Materia=2155 | title=Amon Tobin, Brazilian star in the electronica scene | accessdate=2008-09-27 | publisher=AllBrazillianMusic.com | date=April 26, 2001 | author=Vaz de Castro, Nana}}</ref> He is described as a virtuoso sound designer<ref name=ArticlesReviews>{{cite web|last=Dorston|first=A.S.Van|title=OFOW Article|url=http://www.fastnbulbous.com/amon_tobin_out.htm|work=Article|publisher=Fast n' Bulbus|accessdate=2005-05-20}}</ref> and is considered to be one of the most influential electronic music artists in the world.<ref name=CreatorsProject>{{cite web|last=Creators Project|first=The Creators Project|title=Amon Tobin Brazil|url=http://thecreatorsproject.com/creators/amon-tobin|work=Amon Tobin ISAM|publisher=Vice| accessdate=2011-09-11}}</ref> He is noted for his unusual methodology in sound design and music production. He has released seven major studio albums under the London-based [[Ninja Tune]] record label.\n\nIn 2007 he released ''[[Foley Room]]'', an album based entirely on the manipulation of field recordings. His latest album, 2011's ''[[ISAM (album)|ISAM]]'', included \"female\" vocals made from his own processed voice.<ref name=thequietus>{{cite web|last=John|first=Doran|title=Amon Tobin And Tessa Farmer: Control Over Nature|url=http://thequietus.com/articles/06256-amon-tobin-and-tessa-farmer-control-over-nature|work=ISAM|publisher=thequietus.com|accessdate=2011-05-16| archiveurl= http://web.archive.org/web/20110519094344/http://thequietus.com/articles/06256-amon-tobin-and-tessa-farmer-control-over-nature| archivedate= May 19, 2011 | deadurl= no}}</ref> His music has been used in numerous major motion pictures including ''[[The Italian Job (2003)|The Italian Job]]'' and ''[[21 (2008 film)|21]]''. Tobin has created songs for several independent films, including the 2006 [[Hungarian language|Hungarian]] film ''[[Taxidermia]]'', and had his music used in other independent films such as the 2002 ''[[Palme d'or|Cannes Palme d'Or]]'' nominated ''[[Divine Intervention (film)|Divine Intervention]]''. A selection of his tracks were featured in commercial [[Bumper (broadcasting)|bumps]] on [[Toonami]] and in the 2005 [[anime]] ''[[IGPX]]'', and he produced the musical scores to critically acclaimed video games ''[[Tom Clancy's Splinter Cell: Chaos Theory]]'' by [[Ubisoft]] in 2005, and [[Sucker Punch Productions|Sucker Punch]]'s ''[[Infamous (video game)|Infamous]]'' in 2009."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"426747":{"pageid":426747,"ns":0,"title":"Devin Townsend","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=December 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Devin Townsend\n| image               = DevinTownsend2012.jpg\n| alt                 = \n| caption             = Devin Townsend performing in July 2012\n| landscape           = yes\n| image_size          = 250\n| background          = solo_singer\n| birth_name          = Devin Garret Townsend<ref>''[[Infinity (Devin Townsend album)|Infinity]]'' booklet.</ref>\n| alias               =\n| birth_date          = {{birth date and age|1972|5|5}}\n| birth_place         = [[New Westminster]], British Columbia, Canada\n| death_date          = \n| death_place         = \n| origin              = \n| instrument          = Vocals, guitars, bass\n| genre               = [[Progressive metal]], [[progressive rock]], [[industrial metal]], [[extreme metal]], [[alternative metal]], [[punk rock]], [[Ambient music|ambient]], [[New-age music|new-age]], [[Electronic music|electronic]]\n| occupation          = Singer-songwriter, musician, producer\n| years_active        = 1993\u2013present\n| label               = HevyDevy, [[Century Media]], [[Inside Out Music]]\n| associated_acts     = The Devin Townsend Band, Devin Townsend Project, [[Strapping Young Lad]], [[Casualties of Cool]], [[Steve Vai]], [[Punky Br\u00fcster]], [[IR8]], [[Front Line Assembly]], Grey Skies, Caustic Thought, Noisescapes, [[Ayreon]], [[the Wildhearts]], [[Bent Sea]], [[ReVamp]], [[Removal (band)|removal]]\n| website             = {{URL|www.hevydevy.com}}\n}}\n'''Devin Garret Townsend''' (born May 5, 1972) is a Canadian musician, songwriter and record producer. He was the founder, songwriter, vocalist, and guitarist in [[extreme metal]] band [[Strapping Young Lad]] from 1994 to 2007 and has had an extensive career as a solo artist.\n\nAfter performing in a number of [[heavy metal music|metal]] bands in [[education in Canada|high school]], Townsend was discovered by a record label in 1993 and was asked to perform lead vocals on [[Steve Vai]]'s album ''[[Sex & Religion]]''. After recording and touring with Vai, Townsend was discouraged by what he found in the music industry, and vented his anger on the solo album ''[[Heavy as a Really Heavy Thing]]'' released under the pseudonym Strapping Young Lad. He soon assembled a band under the name, and released the critically acclaimed ''[[City (Strapping Young Lad album)|City]]'' in 1997. Since then, he has released three more studio albums with Strapping Young Lad, along with solo material released under his own independent record label, HevyDevy Records.\n\nTownsend's solo albums, a diverse mix of [[hard rock]], [[progressive metal]], [[ambient music|ambient]], and [[New-age music|new-age]], have featured a varying lineup of supporting musicians. In 2002 he formed '''the Devin Townsend Band''', a dedicated lineup which recorded and toured for two of his solo releases. In 2007, he disbanded both Strapping Young Lad and the Devin Townsend Band, taking a break from touring to spend more time with his family. After a two-year hiatus, he began recording again, and soon announced the formation of the '''Devin Townsend Project'''. The project began with a series of four albums, released from 2009 to 2011, each written in a different style, and Townsend continues to record and tour under the new moniker.\n\nAcross all his bands and projects, Townsend has released twenty studio albums and three live albums. Townsend's trademark production style, featuring a heavily multitracked [[wall of sound]], has been compared to the styles of [[Phil Spector]] and [[Frank Zappa]]. His versatile vocal delivery ranges from [[screaming (music)|screaming]] to an opera-esque [[clean vocals|singing]], and his songwriting is similarly diverse. Townsend's musical style is rooted in metal, and his albums are written to express different aspects of his personality."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"4685723":{"pageid":4685723,"ns":0,"title":"Troum","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{ref improve|date=March 2014}}\n[[File:Stefan Knappe 2.jpg|thumb|Stefan Knappe in 2014]]\n\n'''Troum''' is a [[Germany|German]] project of [[drone music]], [[ambient music]], [[noise music]], and [[experimental music]]. His music is a combination of downtempo vintage-style synthesizers and ambient melodies. The style of his music is very organic, typically incorporating clips of the human element into his songs (i.e. weather broadcasts, simple talking, or even breathing). His song, \"Dictaphone's Lament\", was used as the track on a music video entitled \"Live Life to the Fullest\", which was made by and featured on the action cartoon block [[Toonami]]. Their early works, such as ''[[Bergtatt \u2013 Et eeventyr i 5 capitler|Bergtatt]]'', were categorised as folklore-influenced [[black metal]] but have since evolved a fluid and increasingly eclectic musical style, blending genres such as [[Experimental rock|rock]], [[electronica]], [[symphonic music|symphonic]] and [[chamber music|chamber]] traditions, [[noise music|noise]] and [[experimental music]] into their oeuvre.<ref name=\"\"UlverBiographyAllMusic\">{{cite web|last=All Music|title=Ulver Biography|url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/ulver-mn0000179632/biography|accessdate=2014-05-10}}</ref> 1997 marked their international debut with the release of their third album ''[[Nattens madrigal]]'' through German label [[Century Media Records|Century Media]]. However, following discord with the label, [[Kristoffer Rygg]] formed his own imprint [[Jester Records]] in 1998.<ref name=\"Discogs\">{{cite web | url=http://www.discogs.com/label/12795-Jester-Records | title=Jester Records | publisher=Discogs | accessdate=May 27, 2014}}</ref>\n\nIn 1998, multi-instrumentalist Tore Ylwizaker joined the band marking a drastic change in direction for ''[[Themes from William Blake's The Marriage of Heaven and Hell]]'' - a [[double album]] incorporating elements from [[drum and bass]], [[progressive rock]], [[spoken word]], [[industrial music]], and [[black metal]], fused into a somewhat [[ambient music|ambient]] new style. Further exploring [[trip hop]], [[jazz]], [[ambient music]], [[spoken word]] and [[electronica]] on 2000\u2019s ''[[Perdition City]]'', before moving into a more [[Experimental music|experimental]], [[Minimal music|minimalist]], [[ambient music|ambient]] direction, and [[soundtrack]] work.\n\n2005 marked another change in the band\u2019s sound, returning to standard instrumentation, combined with orchestral instruments and arrangements. title = ULVER official site | date = 2009-11-26 | accessdate = 2009-11-26}}</ref> and the band performed some of their first live concerts in their 15-year lifespan, including the prestigious Norwegian National Opera.\n\nUlver have sold in excess of half a million records, have well over 11,000,000 plays on [[Last.fm]],<ref name=\"MythologyAgencyUlver\">{{cite web | url=http://www.mythology-live.com/artist/ulver/ | title=Mythology Agency - Ulver | publisher=Mythology Agency | date=December 7, 2005 | accessdate=May 28, 2014 | author=York, William}}</ref> been twice nominated for the Norwegian Grammy Awards, Spellemannsprisen, in different categories,<ref name=\"UlverBloodInsidePR\">{{cite web | url=http://www.jester-records.com/ulver/ulver_blood_inside_press_release.html | title=ULVER BLOOD INSIDE | publisher=Jester Records | date=June 2005 | accessdate=May 28, 2014}}</ref> won ''Album of the Year'' at the Oslo Awards for ''[[Shadows of the Sun]]'' in 2008,<ref name=\"Osloprisen 2007\">{{cite web |url=http://pstereo.net/2009/05/04/ulver/ |title=Ulver \u2013 Records]], [[Polydor]], [[Deutsche Grammophon]]\n}}\n'''Evangelos Odysseas Papathanassiou''' ({{lang-gr|\u0395\u03c5\u03ac\u03b3\u03b3\u03b5\u03bb\u03bf\u03c2 \u039f\u03b4\u03c5\u03c3\u03c3\u03ad\u03b1\u03c2 \u03a0\u03b1\u03c0\u03b1\u03b8\u03b1\u03bd\u03b1\u03c3\u03af\u03bf\u03c5}} {{IPA-el|ev\u02c8a\u0272\u025felos o\u00f0i\u02c8seas papa\u03b8ana\u02c8siu|}}; born 29 March 1943), professionally known as '''Vangelis''' ({{lang-gr|\u0392\u03b1\u03b3\u03b3\u03ad\u03bb\u03b7\u03c2}} {{IPA-el|va(\u0272)\u02c8gelis|}}; English pronunciation: {{IPAc-en|v|\u00e6|\u014b|\u02c8|\u0261|\u025b|l|\u0268|s}}<ref>''Vangelis'' is a Greek diminutive of Evangelos; he pronounces his own name as {{IPAc-en|v|\u00e6|\u014b|\u02c8|\u0261|\u025b|l|\u0268|s}} in English, but it is commonly heard as {{IPAc-en|v|\u00e6|n|\u02c8|d\u0292|\u025b|l|\u0268|s}}.</ref>), is a [[Greeks|Greek]] composer of [[electronic music|electronic]], [[Progressive rock|progressive]], [[Ambient music|ambient]], [[jazz]], [[pop rock]], and [[orchestral]] music. He is best known for his [[Academy Awards|Academy Award]]\u2013winning score for the film ''[[Chariots of Fire]]'', composing scores for the films ''[[Nankyoku Monogatari|Antarctica]]'', ''[[Blade Runner]]'', ''[[Missing (film)|Missing]]'', ''[[1492: Conquest of Paradise]]'', and ''[[Alexander (2004 film)|Alexander]]'', and the use of his music in the [[Public Broadcasting Service|PBS]] documentary ''[[Cosmos: A Personal Voyage]]'' by [[Carl Sagan]].\n\nVangelis began his professional musical career working with several popular bands of the 1960s such as The Forminx and [[Aphrodite's Child]], with the latter's album ''[[666 (Aphrodite's Child album)|666]]'' going on to be recognized as a [[psychedelic music|psychedelic]] classic.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.progreviews.com/reviews/display.php?rev=ac-666 |title= Prog Reviews review of 666 |accessdate=4 November 2008 |publisher=Ground & Sky |date=5 January 2008}}</ref> Throughout the 1970s, Vangelis composed [[music scores]] for several animal documentaries, including ''[[L'Apocalypse des animaux (album)|L'Apocalypse Des Animaux]]'', ''[[La F\u00eate sauvage]]'' and ''[[Op\u00e9ra sauvage]]''; the success of these scores brought him into the film scoring mainstream. In the early 1980s, Vangelis formed a musical partnership with [[Jon Anderson]], the lead singer of progressive rock band [[Yes (band)|Yes]], and the duo went on to release several albums together as ''[[Jon & Vangelis]]''.\n\nIn 1981, he composed the score for the Oscar-winning film ''[[Chariots of Fire]]'', for which he won an [[Academy Award for Best Original Music Score]]. [[Chariots of Fire (album)|The soundtrack's]] single, ''[[Chariots of Fire (instrumental)|Titles]]'', also reached the top of the American [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]] chart and was used as the background music at the [[London 2012 Olympics]] winners' medal presentation ceremonies.\n\nHaving had a career in music spanning over 50 years and having composed and performed more than 52 albums, Vangelis is one of the most important exponents of [[electronic music]].<ref name=\"Telegraph UK\">{{cite news |author=Peter Culshaw |title=My Greek odyssey with Alexander |publisher=The Telegraph |date=6 January 2005 |url=http://www.telegraph.co.uk/arts/main.jhtml?xml=/arts/2005/01/06/bmvang06.xml&page=1 |accessdate=12 October 2008 | location=London}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url={{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p112251|pure_url=yes}} |title= Vangelis Biography |author=Jason Ankeny |accessdate=6 November 2008 |publisher=All Music}}</ref><ref name=\"Tranglos\">[http://www.tranglos.com/marek/yes/tr_60.html Tranglos review] Retrieved 6 October 2008</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2868793":{"pageid":2868793,"ns":0,"title":"Velvet Cacoon","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{unreferenced|date=March 2011}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Velvet Cacoon\n| image                 =\n| caption            = \n| image_size            = \n| background          = group_or_band\n| alias               = \n| origin              = [[Portland, Oregon]], [[USA]]\n| genre               = [[Ambient black metal]], [[dark ambient]]\n| years_active        = 1996&ndash;2009\n| label               = [[Starlight Temple Society]] <small>(2009 &ndash; [Part 3&#93; : UNT Digital Library |publisher=Digital.library.unt.edu |year=1969 |work=[[Pop Chronicles]] |format=audio |accessdate=2011-04-14}}</ref>  Released in 1967, the song reached #1 on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]] in July of that year. Later in 1967, an instrumental version by jazz [[guitarist]] [[Wes Montgomery]] became his biggest Hot 100 hit when it peaked at #44.  \"Windy\" was The Association's second U.S. number-one, following \"[[Cherish (The Association song)|Cherish]]\" in 1966. ''Billboard'' ranked the record as the No. 4 song for 1967.<ref>[[Billboard Year-End Hot 100 singles of 1967]]</ref>\n\nAccording to rumor, the original lyrics by Ruthann Friedman were about a man and The Association changed them to be about a woman.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://ruthannfriedman.com/lyrics/ |title=Ruthann Friedman lyrics |publisher=Ruthannfriedman.com |date= |accessdate=2012-07-11}}</ref> \n<blockquote>\n\"There are many explanations of who Windy actually was in Ruthann's life. She would have you know, she being me, Ruthann Friedman, that none of them are true.  Windy was indeed a female and purely a fictitious character who popped into my head one fine day in 1967...\n</blockquote>\n<blockquote>\nDuring the recording session the Association members, sure that they were in the middle of recording a hit, called the song writer, me again, in to sing on the fade at the end.  I can be heard singing a blues harmony as the song fades out...\"\n</blockquote>\n\nSession musician [[Hal Blaine]] was brought in to play drums.<ref name=\"songfacts\">{{cite web\n  | url = Founded in 1967, the group mixes elements of [[jazz]], [[classical music]],  [[world music]], and the sounds of animals and nature. They are often classified as \"[[New-age music|new age]]\" or \"ecological jazz\", and their unique musical style is often called \u201cEarth Music\u201d. The group has had many lineup changes since it was founded. Long-standing members currently in the group include Paul Winter, cellist [[Eugene Friesen]], bassist [[Eliot Wadiopan]], jazz oboist [[Paul McCandless]], and percussionist and [[frame drum]] specialist [[Glen Velez]]. Past members who were part of the group for a considerable length of time include [[Paul Halley]], [[Susan Osborn (musician)|Susan Osborn]], [[Oscar Castro-Neves]], [[Russ Landau]], [[David Darling child,<ref name=\"VOAnews20030615\"/><ref name=\"HellenismYanniBio\"/> blending [[jazz]], [[classical]], [[soft rock]], and [[world music]]<ref name=\"ChicagoTrib19980215\"/> to create predominantly instrumental works.<ref name=\"AugustaChron20120522\"/> Although this genre of music was not well suited for commercial pop radio and music television,<ref name=\"Courant19920426\"/><ref name=\"LATimes20001024\"/> Yanni received international recognition by producing concerts at historic monuments and by producing videos that were broadcast on public television.<ref name=\"LATimes20001024\"/> His breakthrough concert, ''[[Yanni Live at the Acropolis]],'' yielded the second best-selling music video of all time.<ref name=\"MontrealGazette20120614\"/> Additional historic sites for Yanni's concerts have included India's [[Taj Mahal]], China's [[Forbidden City]], the United Arab Emirates' [[Burj Khalifa]],<ref name=\"emirates247-20110921\"/> Russia's [[Moscow Kremlin|Kremlin]],<ref name=\"Kremlin20111101\"/> Puerto Rico's [[Castillo San Felipe del Morro|El Morro castle]],<ref name=\"ElMorro\"/> Lebanon's ancient city of [[Byblos]],<ref name=OrientLeJour20130702/> Tunisia's Roman Theatre of [[Carthage]],<ref name=LeconomisteMaghrebin20140723/> and India's [[Laxmi Vilas Palace, Vadodara|Laxmi Vilas Palace]].<ref Dream (Yanni album)|Dare to Dream]]'' and ''[[In My Time]]'') received [[Grammy Award]] nominations.<ref name=\"VOAnews20120123\"/> Through late 2011, Yanni had performed live in concert before more than two million people in more than 20 countries around the world, and has accumulated more than 35 platinum and gold albums globally, with sales totaling over 20&nbsp;million copies.<ref name=\"TheNationThailand20111013\"/> A longtime fundraiser for public television,<ref name=\"CourierJournal20120426\"/><ref name=\"SavannahNow20120526\"/> Yanni's compositions have been used on commercial television programs, especially for sporting events.<ref name=\"VOAnews20120123\"/><ref name=\"LATimes19930613\"/><ref name=GolfDigest20140612/>  He has written film scores and the music for an award-winning [[British Airways face advertisement|British Airways television commercial]].<ref name=\"LATimes19930613\"/>\n\nYanni popularized the combination of electronic music synthesizers with a full scale symphony orchestra.<ref name=DNAindia20150122/> He has employed musicians of various nationalities and has incorporated a variety of exotic instruments<ref name=\"SavannahNow20120526\"/><ref name=\"ChanVillager20120428\"/> Yanni has been called a \"True Global Artist\"<ref name=DNAindia20150122/> and his music is said to reflect his \u201cone world, one (abbreviated as '''YMO''') is a Japanese [[electronic music]] band consisting of principal members [[Haruomi Hosono]] (bass, keyboards, vocals), [[Yukihiro Takahashi]] (drums, lead vocals) and [[Ryuichi Sakamoto]] (keyboards, vocals).<ref name=\"allmusic_ymo\">{{Allmusic|artist|p5886|Yellow Magic Orchestra|accessdate=June 3, 2009}}</ref> For their early studio albums and live performances, the band was often accompanied by [[Programming (music)|music programmer]] [[Hideki Matsutake]].<ref name=\"sound_147\"/>\n\nThey are often considered influential [[innovator]]s in the field of popular electronic music.<ref name=\"allmusic_ymo\"/><ref name=\"fidelity_1993\"/> They contributed to the development of [[synthpop]],<ref>Buckley, P. (2003), ''The Rough Guide to Rock'', Rough Guides, London (pp. 1200&ndash;1201).</ref> [[ambient house]],<ref name=\"allmusic_ymo\"/> [[electronica]],<ref name=\"guardian_ymo\"/> [[electro 2011}}</ref> [[techno]],<ref name=\"UGO\"/><ref name=\"bogdanov_1996\"/> and [[hip hop music]].<ref name=\"guardian_ymo\"/> More broadly, their influence is evident across various genres of [[popular The group members began their musical careers as studio engineers and in 1997 formed the group Zero 7. Left to right: Mark Warren, Ben Ponton\n  |image_size            = \n  |years_active      =  1980&ndash;present \n  |origin            = [[Newcastle upon Tyne]], [[UK]] \n  |genre       =  [[Dark ambient]], [[post-industrial music|post-industrial]], [[industrial music|industrial]], [[ambient music|ambient]]\n  |label      = [[Charrm]], [[Red Rhino Records]], [[Staalplaat]], [[DOVentertainment]], [[Soleilmoon]], [[Mute Records]]\n  |background = group_or_band \n  |website    =\n  |associated_acts    =  [[Reformed Faction]], [[Rapoon]], [[Dead Voices on Air]]\n  |current_members   = Ben Ponton <br/> Mark Warren\n  |past_members   = Andy Eardley <br/> Lisa Hale <br/> [[Mark Spybey]] <br/> Paolo Di Paolo <br/> Peter Jensen <br/> [[Robin Storey]] \n}}\n\n'''Zoviet France''' (also known as <small>''':$OVIET:FRANCE:'''</small>, '''Soviet France''', ''':Zoviet-France:''' and latterly usually written as ''':zoviet*france:''') is a music group from [[Newcastle upon Tyne]] in north east [[England]]. While often dissonant and made of industrial textures, their music also falls into the [[ambient music]] category. Formed in 1980, and remaining largely anonymous,<ref>Interview with [[Brent Bambury]], [[CBC Radio]], 2 May 1991</ref> the group has had a number of members; presently it consists of co-founder Ben Ponton and Mark Warren. Former members included Neil Ramshaw, Peter Jensen, [[Robin Storey]] (who now records as [[Rapoon]]), Lisa Hale, Paolo Di Paolo, [[Mark Spybey]] (who now records as [[Dead Voices on Air]]) and Andy Eardley. In 2005 Storey, Spybey and Eardley formed a new group, [[Reformed Faction]].\n\nThe packaging of their releases was often unconventional, involving materials such as [[Hessian (cloth)|hessian]], [[tar paper]] and [[aluminium foil]]."}]}}}}[]
